# The Lotus Sutra: A Translation from the Classical Chinese

**Translated from Kumārajīva's Chinese Edition (Taishō Shinshū Daizōkyō No. 262)**

---

## Imperial Preface to the Great Vehicle Lotus Sutra
### 御製大乘妙法蓮華經序

*Imperial Preface by the Yongle Emperor*
*(永樂十八年四月十七日 — April 17, 1420)*

---

In ancient times, the Tathāgata dwelt at Mount Gṛdhrakūṭa together with the great Arhats Ājñātakauṇḍinya, Mahākāśyapa, and countless other assembled beings, and there expounded the great vehicle true sutra called the *Sutra of Immeasurable Meanings*. At that time, heavenly jeweled flowers rained down in abundance, the light of wisdom manifested auspicious signs illuminating both the hidden and the manifest, the entire Buddha-world shook in six ways, and all beings human and celestial experienced what they had never before experienced. All rejoiced and praised this teaching, understanding that this sutra is the secret treasury of all the Buddhas and Tathāgatas—spiritually wondrous and beyond measure, vast and ineffable in name.

Therefore it draws forth those sunk in the stagnant depths, rescues those confused and lost in their true nature. Its merit extends far beyond any limit one could mark. Tracing the source, it arose in India and flowed eastward to China. From the Western Jin dynasty, the śramaṇa Dharmarakṣa first translated it under the title *The Lotus of the Correct Dharma*. Then the Kucha Tripiṭaka Master Kumārajīva of the Eastern Jin retranslated it under the title *The Lotus Flower of the Wonderful Dharma*. Coming to the Sui dynasty, the Indian śramaṇa Jñānagupta translated it also as *The Wonderful Dharma*. Although these three translations overlap in text and meaning, each presenting the teaching in its own way, it is the Tripiṭaka Master [Kumārajīva] alone who grasped its true meaning. However, as the ages have passed, errors have inevitably crept in, and without revision and correction, doubts have gradually multiplied. For this reason, I have specially undertaken careful collation and commanded that it be carved in woodblock to spread its transmission widely.

Alas! The Tathāgata, out of compassion for all sentient beings who have various natures, various desires, various actions, and various thoughts and discriminations—entangled through countless eons with no prospect of liberation—appeared in this world for this one great cause. He expounded the wondrous teaching and established supreme skillful means so that all might attain liberation and ascend to correct awakening. This is truly the ferry-bridge across the sea of suffering and the torch of wisdom illuminating the darkness. Virtuous men and women, all sentient beings, who can hold this sutra with utmost sincerity, recite it, wear it reverently, bow to it, and make offerings to it—they shall be freed from all afflictions, all karmic obstructions shall be removed, and all the bonds of birth and death shall be released.

It is as when the hungry receive food, the thirsty receive drink, the cold receive fire, the heated receive coolness, the poor receive treasure, the sick receive a physician, a child receives its mother, a traveler receives a boat. Such comfort and joy cannot be expressed in words.

Ah! The Way cannot be preserved except through scripture; the Dharma cannot be transmitted except through scripture. Through scripture one seeks the Dharma; through the Dharma one awakens to the Way. Only then does one recognize that the meaning of this sutra is pure, subtle, and supremely rare. Those who follow it shall attain bodily health and peace; all roots of virtue shall be perfectly complete, like a lotus rising from the water unstained by mud. Immediately the five aggregates become empty, the six sense-faculties are purified, and it is not difficult to swiftly ascend to the highest good and accomplish correct awakening.

But if one remains sunk in confusion, stubbornly attached, willingly falling and cutting off the roots of virtue, then one's body shall fall into the paths of suffering, cycling through the realm of birth and death—is there limit to such consequences? Nevertheless, the two paths of good and evil depend on what one pursues: doing good brings fortune; doing evil brings misfortune. The karmic retribution in the visible and invisible realms is exact to the smallest measure. Let those who contemplate this sutra take heed! Let them be diligent!

*The seventeenth day of the fourth month of the eighteenth year of the Yongle reign*

---

---

## Translator's Note on Editorial Conventions

This translation follows Kumārajīva's Chinese text as preserved in the Taishō Shinshū Daizōkyō (No. 262). The following conventions are observed:

1. **Sutra Title**: The full title 妙法蓮華經 is rendered "Sutra of the Lotus Flower of the Wonderful Dharma." The abbreviated form 法華經 is rendered "Lotus Sutra" or "Dharma-Blossom Sutra" interchangeably throughout.

2. **Chapter Titles vs. Interpretive Headers**: The original Chinese chapter titles (e.g., 序品第一, 方便品第二) are preserved. *[Interpretive sub-headers in italics with brackets]* are translator additions for reader navigation and do not appear in Kumārajīva's text.

3. **Dhāraṇī Romanization**: Chapter 26 mantras are romanized in Hanyu Pinyin from the Chinese transliterations, not reconstructed into Sanskrit. Phonetic performance notes from the Chinese critical apparatus (such as *fanqie* pronunciation guides) are included in footnotes.

4. **Critical Apparatus**: Significant variant readings from Song (宋), Yuan (元), Ming (明), and Palace (宮) editions are noted where they affect translation. Example: "Taishō reads X; Song/Yuan editions read Y."

5. **Bracketed Text**: Material in [brackets] indicates words added for grammatical clarity in English that have no direct correspondent in the Chinese source.

6. **Translator Attribution**: The Taishō edition attributes this translation to "Kumārajīva of Kucha" (龜茲國...鳩摩羅什). Variant editions write "Qiuci" (丘茲) for the kingdom name.

---


## Preface to the Transmission of the Lotus Sutra
### 妙法蓮華經弘傳序

*Composed by the Vinaya Master Daoxuan of Zhongnan Mountain during the Tang Dynasty*
*(唐終南山釋道宣述)*

---

The *Sutra of the Lotus Flower of the Wonderful Dharma* represents the fundamental purpose for which all the Buddhas have descended into the world to manifest their spiritual presence. This teaching was preserved in the great kingdoms of the West for over a thousand years before being transmitted eastward to China, where it has flourished for more than three hundred years.

During the Yongkang era (300-301 CE) of Emperor Hui of the Western Jin dynasty, the Bodhisattva Dharmarakṣa of Dunhuang, residing at the Qingmen Gate of Chang'an, first translated this sutra under the title *The Lotus of the Correct Dharma* (正法華).

During the Longan era (397-401 CE) of Emperor An of the Eastern Jin dynasty, and the Hongshi era (399-416 CE) of the Later Qin, the śramaṇa Kumārajīva of Kucha produced the second translation, titled *The Lotus Flower of the Wonderful Dharma* (妙法蓮華).

During the Renshou era (601-604 CE) of the Sui dynasty, at the Da Xingshan Temple, the śramaṇa Jñānagupta of North India produced the third translation, also entitled *The Wonderful Dharma*.

These three translations, though overlapping in content, each present the meaning in their own way. Yet it is the Qin [Kumārajīva] version that has been most honored and widely disseminated through the generations. Beyond these, there exist various individual chapters and separate verses that have circulated as well, as recorded in the historical catalogues, and need not be enumerated here.

Now, the descent of spiritual power from the sacred peaks cannot be accomplished except through the Great Sage. The reach of transformative teaching cannot guide the mind except through karmic connections from past lives. Thus it was that the teaching was first announced at the deer park, where distinctions were made between the capacities of lesser and greater vehicles. At the Golden River, when the Buddha gave his final instructions, distinctions were made between the half and the complete teachings.

Is it not the case that teaching adapts to the times? In evaluating these great assemblies, we cannot merely examine them superficially. Thus we understand: the five thousand who withdrew from their seats had done so to make way for those afflicted by arrogant conceit. The five hundred who received prophecies together honored the traces of the esoteric transformation. Thus the emission of light and the manifestation of auspicious signs opened the teaching-origin that proceeded from inquiry. The Buddha's emergence from meditation and proclamation of virtue expressed the vast significance of Buddha-wisdom.

The decayed mansion elucidated the principles of entering the great vehicle; the phantom city guided those of past karmic connections so they would not fall away. The pearl concealed in the garment made clear the constant presence of the principle of Buddha-nature; the well-digging revealed the many paths to awakening. The language and meaning remain vivid; the similes extend far indeed.

Were it not for the vast compassion of universal salvation, who could pull beings forth from the depths of stagnant drowning? Were it not for the singular unbounded sorrowful heart, who could rescue those lost in confusion from their loss of true nature?

From the Han dynasty to the Tang, throughout six hundred and more years, examining the totality of the texts—over four thousand scrolls—none has been so widely received and maintained as this sutra. Is this not because the teaching struck a resonance with the capacity of beings, following in the traces left by the wisdom of Jixuesheng Buddha? Those who heard it generated profound reverence, following in the remaining merit of King Weiyin.

Therefore, at the very beginning of this sutra, I compose this preface to synthesize its meaning—hoping that we may quickly purify the six sense faculties and ascend to the joyful gathering of the Compassionate Lord; that we may swiftly accomplish the four virtues and proceed toward the profound path of the Pure Land. May praise and dissemination never be exhausted, and may this be bequeathed everlastingly to all future generations.

---


## Chapter 1: Introduction

**Translation from the Classical Chinese Original**
Based on Kumarajiva's Translation
Scholarly English Translation with Philosophical and Scientific Apparatus

---

# Chapter 1: Introduction

## Opening: The Transmission of the Teaching

Thus have I heard.[^1] At one time, the Buddha was dwelling at Mount Gṛdhrakūṭa near the city of Rājagṛha,[^2] together with a great assembly of twelve thousand bhikṣus.[^3] All of these practitioners had attained the state of Arhat—having exhausted all outflows of mental affliction, having eliminated all defilements, having realized their own ultimate benefit, having severed all bonds of conditioned existence, and having attained complete mastery and freedom of mind.[^4]

Their names are recorded as follows: Ājñātakauṇḍinya, Mahākāśyapa, Uruvilvākāśyapa, Gayākāśyapa[^fn_gaya], Nadīkāśyapa, Śāriputra, Mahāmaudgalyāyana[^fn_maud], Mahākātyāyana, Aniruddha[^fn_aniruddha], Kapphiṇa, Gavāṃpati, Revata, Pilindavatsa, Bakkula, Mahākauṣṭhila, Nanda, Sundarananda, Pūrṇamaitrāyaṇīputra, Subhūti, Ānanda, and Rāhula—great Arhats of this caliber, well known throughout all communities of practitioners.[^5]

[^fn_gaya]: **Gayākāśyapa**: The text distinguishes this Kāśyapa brother using the phonetic 伽 (*qié*) for "Gayā," whereas the other two brothers (Uruvilvā and Nadī) use the standard 迦 (*jiā*). While the base Taishō text prints 迦 here as well, the critical apparatus emends this to 伽 to preserve the distinction found in the Sanskrit.

[^fn_maud]: **Mahāmaudgalyāyana**: The Taishō text utilizes the character 揵 (*qián*), written with the hand radical (手), as opposed to the character 犍 (*jiān*), written with the cow radical (牛), which appears in the Song, Yuan, and Ming editions. The reading Mahāmaudgalyāyana remains standard.

[^fn_aniruddha]: **Aniruddha**: The Taishō text uses the rare variant character 㝹 (*nóu*), as confirmed by critical notes, rather than the more common transliterations 那 (*nà*) or 耨 (*nòu*). This indicates a specific phonetic reconstruction intended by the translator distinct from other versions of the sutra.

---

## The Assembly: All Beings Present

Furthermore, there were also two thousand persons[^6] among both those still in training and those who had completed their training. The bhikṣuṇī Mahāprajāpatī was present together with her retinue of six thousand bhikṣuṇīs.[^7] Yaśodharā, the mother of Rāhula, was also present with her retinue.[^8]

Additionally, there were eighty thousand Bodhisattva-Mahāsattvas,[^9] all of whom had become irreversible in their aspiration toward the attainment of anuttara-samyak-saṃbodhi (supreme perfect enlightenment).[^10] All had attained the dharaṇī[^11]—the power to retain and preserve teaching—and possessed eloquence in joyful exposition. They had already turned the irreversible Dharma wheel,[^12] spreading teachings that cannot be reversed or overturned.

These Bodhisattvas had made offerings to innumerable hundreds of thousands of Buddhas, and in the presence of all these Buddhas they had planted deep roots of virtue. They were constantly praised by all Buddhas on account of their devotion and accomplishment. They cultivated themselves through the mind of compassion (maitrī and karuṇā), skillfully entered into Buddha-wisdom,[^13] thoroughly penetrated the great wisdom of ultimate reality,[^14] and thereby reached the farther shore—transcending the realm of conditioned existence.[^15]

Their fame was universally heard throughout immeasurable worlds, and they possessed the power to liberate innumerable hundreds of thousands of living beings. Their names are recorded as: the Bodhisattva Mañjuśrī (He of Transcendent Wisdom),[^16] the Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara (the One Who Observes the Sounds of the World),[^17] the Bodhisattva Mahāsthāmaprāpta, the Bodhisattva Nityodyukta (Ever-Exerting), the Bodhisattva Aniksiptadhura, the Bodhisattva Ratnapāṇi (He with the Jeweled Hand), the Bodhisattva Medicine King, the Bodhisattva Pradānaśūra (Courageous in Giving), the Bodhisattva Ratnacandra (Jeweled Moon), the Bodhisattva Candraprabha (Moonlight), the Bodhisattva Pūrṇacandra (Full Moon), the Bodhisattva Mahāvikramin (Great Strider), the Bodhisattva Anantavikramin (Boundless Strider), the Bodhisattva Trailokyavikrama (Strider Through the Three Realms), the Bodhisattva Bhadrapāla (Excellent Guardian), the Bodhisattva Maitreya (He of Loving-Kindness), the Bodhisattva Ratnākara (Ocean of Jewels), and the Guide Bodhisattva (導師菩薩)—eighty thousand Bodhisattva-Mahāsattvas of this caliber were all present in the assembly.[^18]

---

## The Celestial and Divine Attendants

Moreover, Śakra Devānām Indra (the Lord of the Thirty-Three Heavens) was present with his retinue of twenty thousand celestial sons.[^19] The celestial sons Candravimala (Moonlight), Manojñasvara, Ratnacchattra, and the Four Great Heavenly Kings were also present, together with their retinue of ten thousand celestial sons.[^20]

The celestial sovereigns Īśvara and Maheśvara were present with their retinue of thirty thousand celestial sons. The Brahmā Heavenly King—the lord of the Sahā world (our cosmic realm)—together with Śikhin Mahābrahman, Jyotiṣprabha Mahābrahman, and others, were present with their retinue of twelve thousand celestial sons.[^21]

There were eight Dragon Kings: the Dragon King Nanda, the Dragon King Upananda, the Dragon King Sāgara, the Dragon King Vāsukin, the Dragon King Takṣaka, the Dragon King Anavatapta, the Dragon King Manasvin, and the Dragon King Utpalaka—each accompanied by several hundreds of thousands of retinue members.[^22]

There were four Kiṃnara Kings: the Kiṃnara King Dharma, the Kiṃnara King Sudharma, the Kiṃnara King Mahādharma, and the Kiṃnara King Dharmadhara—each with several hundreds of thousands of attendants.

There were four Gandharva Kings: the Gandharva King Manojña, the Gandharva King Manojñasvara, the Gandharva King Madhura, and the Gandharva King Madhurasvara—each with several hundreds of thousands of retinue members.

There were four Asura Kings: the Asura King Balin, the Asura King Kharaskandha, the Asura King Vemacitra, and the Asura King Rāhu—each with several hundreds of thousands of attendants.

There were four Garuḍa Kings: the Garuḍa King Mahātejas (Great Radiance), the Garuḍa King Mahākāya (Great Form), the Garuḍa King Mahāpūrṇa (Great Fullness), and the Garuḍa King Manojña (Pleasing to Mind)—each with several hundreds of thousands of retinue members.

King Ajātaśatru, son of Vaidehī, was present with several hundreds of thousands of retinue members.[^23] All in the assembly bowed respectfully at the Buddha's feet and withdrew to sit respectfully to one side.[^24]

---

## The Buddha's Teaching and Cosmic Manifestation

At that time, the World-Honored One, surrounded by the fourfold assembly[^25] and having been honored with reverent offerings, praise, and adoration, expounded for the assembled Bodhisattvas a Mahāyāna sutra entitled the *Sutra of Immeasurable Meanings*—a teaching for Bodhisattvas, treasured and protected by the Buddhas.[^26]

Having concluded his exposition of this sutra, the Buddha sat in full lotus posture (padmāsana)[^27] and entered into the samādhi of the abode of immeasurable meanings[^28]—a meditative absorption in which his body and mind remained utterly still and unmoved, entering a state of unified, non-dualistic awareness.[^29]

Thereupon heavenly mandārava flowers, great mandārava flowers, mañjūṣaka flowers, and great mañjūṣaka flowers rained down abundantly from the heavens, scattering upon the Buddha and upon the great assembly.[^30] The entire Buddha-world quaked and trembled in six ways—a cosmic manifestation signifying the profound nature of the teaching being conveyed.[^31]

---

## The Universal Response

At that time, all the beings present in the assembly—bhikṣus, bhikṣuṇīs, upāsakas (male lay practitioners), upāsikās (female lay practitioners), devas (celestial beings), nāgas (serpent-beings), yakṣas (nature spirits), gandharvas (celestial musicians), asuras (anti-gods), garuḍas (divine eagles), kiṃnaras (celestial musicians), mahoragas (great serpents), humans, and non-human beings, together with the lesser kings and wheel-turning sage kings[^32]—the entire great assembly experienced phenomena they had never before experienced.

Filled with joy, they placed their palms together in salutation and gazed upon the Buddha with unified attention, their minds focused single-pointedly.[^33]

---

## The Buddha's Light and the Revelation of Other Worlds

At that time, the Buddha emitted a ray of light from the tuft of white hair between his eyebrows (the ūrṇā-keśa, an auspicious mark of Buddhahood).[^34] This light illuminated eighteen thousand worlds to the east, omitting none, extending downward to the Avīci hell[^35] and upward to the Akaniṣṭha Heaven (the highest heaven of the form realm).[^36]

Within this illumination, from the perspective of our world, the beings of the six paths of rebirth[^37] in all those lands were completely visible. The six destinies of sentient existence—beings born in hell, as hungry ghosts, as animals, as asuras, as humans, and as celestial beings—each in their respective realms, appeared as if in direct vision.

Moreover, the Buddhas presently dwelling in those eighteen thousand worlds to the east were seen, and the sutras and Dharma teachings that those Buddhas were expounding were heard as if directly transmitted. Also visible were the bhikṣus, bhikṣuṇīs, upāsakas, and upāsikās who had cultivated the path through meditation and ethical practice and had thereby attained the Way.[^38]

Furthermore, the Bodhisattva-Mahāsattvas were seen practicing the Bodhisattva path through various causes and conditions, through various frames of understanding and belief, and through various appearances and manifestations adapted to their respective capacities.[^39]

Also seen were Buddhas entering parinirvāṇa (final transcendence)—a sight indicating the impermanent and conditional nature of even the Buddha's manifest form in the world.[^40] Also seen, after those Buddhas' parinirvāṇa, were stūpas of the seven precious materials being erected and dedicated to preserve their sacred relics (śarīra).[^41]

---

## Maitreya's Inquiry

At that time, the Bodhisattva Maitreya[^42] had this thought: "Now the World-Honored One has manifested this extraordinary spiritual transformation and display of supernatural power. For what cause and condition has this auspicious sign appeared? The Buddha, the World-Honored One, has now entered into samādhi—this inconceivable manifestation of rare phenomena heretofore unprecedented. To whom should I pose my question? Who possesses the capacity to answer such a profound matter?"[^43]

Then he harbored this further thought: "This Mañjuśrī, the prince of the Dharma King, has previously drawn near and made offerings to immeasurable Buddhas of the past through countless eons. Surely he must have witnessed these rare signs before. I shall now inquire of him."[^44]

---

## The Assembly's Collective Doubt

At that time, the bhikṣus, bhikṣuṇīs, upāsakas, upāsikās, and all the devas, nāgas, and other spirits all harbored this thought: "This extraordinary Buddha-light and display of spiritual power—of whom should we now inquire? To whom shall we address our questions?"[^45]

---

## Maitreya Addresses Mañjuśrī

At that time, the Bodhisattva Maitreya, wishing to resolve his own doubt and observing the minds of the fourfold assembly—the bhikṣus, bhikṣuṇīs, upāsakas, upāsikās, and all the devas, nāgas, and spirits of the assembly—addressed Mañjuśrī directly, saying:

"For what cause and condition has this auspicious spiritual sign appeared? For what reason does the Buddha emit this great light, illuminating the eighteen thousand lands to the east, whereby all the magnificent adornments of those Buddha-lands are completely visible to us?"

---

## Maitreya's Verse Inquiry

Thereupon, the Bodhisattva Maitreya, wishing to restate this meaning in verse form, spoke the following inquiry:

*O Mañjuśrī!*  
*Why does the Guide,*  
*From the white hair between his brows,*  
*Universally illuminate with great light?*  

*Raining mandārava flowers,*  
*And mañjūṣaka flowers,*  
*While sandalwood-scented breezes*  
*Delight the hearts of all—*  

*By this cause and condition,*  
*The earth is perfectly adorned,*  
*And this world itself*  
*Quakes in six ways.*  

*At this time, the fourfold assembly*  
*All rejoice in unison,*  
*Their bodies and minds delighted,*  
*Experiencing what they have never experienced before.*  

*The light between the brows*  
*Illuminates the east—*  
*Eighteen thousand lands*  
*All become golden in hue.*  

*From Avīci hell*  
*Up to the Summit of Existence,*  
*In all those worlds,*  
*The beings of the six paths—*  

*Where birth and death lead,*  
*The karmic connections of good and evil,*  
*The beautiful and ugly results they receive—*  
*All these are seen here.*  

*Also visible are the Buddhas,*  
*Those sage lords and spiritual lions,*  
*Expounding sutras and teachings,*  
*Most subtle and supremely profound.*  

*Their voices pure and undefiled,*  
*Emitting gentle, compassionate tones,*  
*Teaching Bodhisattvas*  
*Numbering countless myriads—*  

*Brahman voices profound and wondrous,*  
*Causing people to delight in hearing.*  
*In each world,*  
*They expound the correct Dharma—*  

*Through various causes and conditions,*  
*With immeasurable parables and illustrations,*  
*Illuminating the Buddha-Dharma,*  
*Awakening living beings.*  

*If people encounter suffering,*  
*Weary of old age, sickness, and death,*  
*For them they expound nirvāṇa,*  
*The ending of all suffering's limits.*  

*If people possess merit,*  
*Having made offerings to Buddhas,*  
*And aspire to the supreme Dharma,*  
*For them they expound pratyekabuddhahood.*  

*If there are sons of Buddha*  
*Cultivating various practices*  
*And seeking supreme wisdom,*  
*For them they expound the pure bodhisattva path.*  

*O Mañjuśrī!*  
*Dwelling here,*  
*I see and hear such things,*  
*And thousands of billions more—*  

*So numerous that words cannot measure them,*  
*I shall now briefly speak.*  
*I see in those lands*  
*Bodhisattvas numerous as the sands of the Ganges,*  

---

## Mañjuśrī's Response: The Teaching of Skillful Means

Then the Bodhisattva Mañjuśrī addressed Maitreya and all the great Bodhisattvas and virtuous men assembled: "Based on what I understand and contemplate, the World-Honored One is about to expound the great Dharma. He will rain down the great Dharma rain, sound the great Dharma trumpet, and beat the great Dharma drum, in order to expound the great significance of the Dharma."[^46]

"O virtuous men, in ages past, spanning countless immeasurable eons prior to the present, there existed a Buddha named the Sun Moon Lamp Bright Tathāgata (Candrasūryapradīpa), one worthy of offerings, possessing perfect knowledge, perfect conduct, well-gone, knower of the world, supreme guide, trainer of men, teacher of gods and humans, the Buddha, the World-Honored One.[^47] He expounded the correct Dharma—a teaching that was good at the beginning, good in the middle, and good at the end, whose meaning was profound and far-reaching, whose language was skillfully composed, pure and simple without admixture, adorned with complete and perfect conduct befitting a Brahmin sage.[^48]

"To those seeking the status of Śrāvaka (disciple), he taught the Four Noble Truths,[^49] enabling them to transcend birth, old age, sickness, and death, and ultimately attaining the perfect peace of nirvāṇa.[^50] To those seeking the status of Pratyekabuddha (solitary awakener), he taught the Twelve Links of Dependent Origination.[^51] To the Bodhisattvas, he taught the Six Perfections (pāramitās),[^52] enabling them to attain anuttara-samyak-saṃbodhi and perfect enlightenment, becoming endowed with all-knowing wisdom."[^53]

"Now, in succession to this Buddha, there appeared another Buddha, also named the Sun Moon Lamp Bright Tathāgata. In fact, in this manner, there appeared a succession of twenty thousand Buddhas, all bearing the same name and title, all belonging to the same lineage. O Maitreya, you should know that the first Buddha and the last Buddha were all of the same name and title, called the Sun Moon Lamp Bright Tathāgata, and all possessed the ten epithets.[^54] The teachings they expounded were good at the beginning, good in the middle, and good at the end."[^55]

"The last of these Sun Moon Lamp Bright Buddhas, before he had renounced the household life and attained Buddhahood, had eight sons as a prince. Their names were: the Prince with Intention, the Prince of Good Intention, the Prince of Boundless Intention, the Prince of Jeweled Intention, the Prince of Increasing Intention, the Prince of Intention without Doubt, the Prince of Intention Directed Forward, and the Prince of Dharma Intention.[^56]

"These eight princes possessed great supernatural power and authority, each ruling over the Four Continents of the world. When these sons heard that their father had renounced the household life and attained anuttara-samyak-saṃbodhi, they all immediately abandoned their royal positions and also followed him in renouncing the world. They developed the great bodhisattva intention and continuously cultivated the Brahmin conduct of ethical purity, becoming Dharma teachers. All of them had already planted roots of virtue in the presence of thousands of millions of Buddhas."[^57]

---

## The Parable of Sun Moon Lamp Bright and the Prophecy

"At that time, the Sun Moon Lamp Bright Tathāgata expounded the Mahāyāna sutra called the *Sutra of Immeasurable Meanings*, a teaching for Bodhisattvas, treasured and protected by the Buddhas. After completing the exposition of this sutra, he sat in full lotus posture in the assembly and entered into the samādhi called the abode of immeasurable meanings, with his body and mind completely unmoving.

"Thereupon, heavenly mandārava flowers, great mandārava flowers, mañjūṣaka flowers, and great mañjūṣaka flowers rained down, falling upon the Buddha and the great assembly. The entire Buddha-world quaked and trembled in six ways. At that time, the assembly of bhikṣus, bhikṣuṇīs, upāsakas, upāsikās, devas, nāgas, yakṣas, gandharvas, asuras, garuḍas, kiṃnaras, mahoragas, humans and non-humans, as well as lesser kings and wheel-turning sage kings—all in the great assembly experienced what they had never experienced before. They rejoiced, placed their palms together in salutation, and gazed at the Buddha with unified, single-pointed attention.[^58]

"At that time, the Sun Moon Lamp Bright Tathāgata emitted a ray of light from the tuft of white hair between his eyebrows, illuminating eighteen thousand Buddha-worlds to the east, with nothing omitted, the light extending downward to the Avīci hell and upward to the Akaniṣṭha Heaven. Like you, the assembled Bodhisattvas in that time saw these very things being revealed.

"O Maitreya, you should know that in that assembly, there were two billion Bodhisattvas, all eager to hear the Dharma. These Bodhisattvas, having seen the light illuminating all the Buddha-lands, were astonished and wanted to know the cause and condition for this light.

"At that time, there was a Bodhisattva named Wonderful Light (Myoho) who had eight hundred disciples. The Sun Moon Lamp Bright Tathāgata, having risen from the samādhi, thereupon, because of the Bodhisattva Wonderful Light, expounded the Mahāyāna sutra called the *Sutra of the Wonderful Dharma Lotus Flower*, a teaching for Bodhisattvas, treasured and protected by the Buddhas. He taught this sutra for sixty small eons without rising from his seat.[^59]

"And the assembly listening to the Dharma also sat continuously in one place for sixty small eons without any movement of body or mind, listening to the Buddha's teaching. Yet to those who listened, it seemed only like a brief meal duration.[^60] In the assembly, there was not a single person whose body or mind gave rise to fatigue or weariness."[^61]

---

## The Prophecy and the Continuity of Teaching

"After the Sun Moon Lamp Bright Tathāgata had expounded this sutra for sixty small eons, he then announced to the assembly of Brahmā kings, Māra, śramaṇas, Brahmins, gods, humans, asuras, and all other beings: 'In this very night, the Tathāgata shall enter into parinirvāṇa (final transcendence).'

"At that time, there was a Bodhisattva named Treasure Store (Kosha), and the Sun Moon Lamp Bright Tathāgata immediately bestowed upon him a prophecy. He announced to all the bhikṣus: 'This Bodhisattva Treasure Store shall become a Buddha next, and his name shall be Pure Body Buddha (Vimalakaya Tathāgata), who shall be an Arhat, Perfectly Enlightened One, possessing perfect knowledge, perfect conduct, well-gone, knower of the world, supreme guide, trainer of men, teacher of gods and humans, the Buddha, the World-Honored One.'[^62]

"The Buddha then, that very night, entered into nirvāṇa. After the Buddha's passing, the Bodhisattva Wonderful Light held and preserved the *Sutra of the Wonderful Dharma Lotus Flower*, teaching it extensively for eighty small eons. The eight sons of that Sun Moon Lamp Bright Buddha all became the disciples of the Bodhisattva Wonderful Light. She taught them, causing them to become firmly established in anuttara-samyak-saṃbodhi.

"These eight princes, after having made offerings to innumerable billions of Buddhas, all attained Buddhahood. The last of them to become a Buddha was named the Buddha of Burning Lamps (Dipamkara).[^63]

"Among the eight hundred disciples of Bodhisattva Wonderful Light, there was one disciple whose name was Seeker of Fame (Yasha-kami). This disciple was always lazy and loved profit and gain. Although he read and recited many sutras, he did not understand their meaning, and forgot much of what he had learned. Therefore he was called Seeker of Fame.

"This person also, because of having planted many roots of virtue, was able to encounter innumerable billions of Buddhas, made offerings to them, showed them respect, and praised them with reverence.[^64]

"O Maitreya, know that the Bodhisattva Wonderful Light at that time was none other than myself. And the Bodhisattva Seeker of Fame was you. Now that you have witnessed this very same auspicious sign, it is just like before. Therefore I have contemplated that the World-Honored One is about to expound the Mahāyāna sutra called the *Sutra of the Wonderful Dharma Lotus Flower*, the teaching for Bodhisattvas, treasured and protected by the Buddhas."[^65]

---

## Mañjuśrī's Verse Recapitulation

Thereupon, the Bodhisattva Mañjuśrī, wishing to restate this meaning in verse, spoke:

*I recall in ages past,*  
*Through countless immeasurable eons,*  
*There was a Buddha of supreme honor among men,*  
*Named the Sun Moon Lamp Bright Tathāgata.*  

*The World-Honored One expounded the Dharma,*  
*Liberating countless billions of beings,*  
*Numberless billions of Bodhisattvas,*  
*Leading them into the wisdom of Buddha.*  

*Before that Buddha had renounced worldly life,*  
*Were born eight sons as princes,*  
*Seeing the great sage renounce the world,*  
*They too cultivated the conduct of pure Brahmin ascetics.*  

*The Buddha at that time expounded the great vehicle—*  
*A sutra named the Teaching of Immeasurable Meanings—*  
*He explained it extensively to the great assembly,*  
*Breaking it down with manifold distinctions.*  

*After the Buddha had finished explaining,*  
*He sat upon the seat of truth,*  
*Entering into the samādhi,*  
*Called the abode of immeasurable meanings.*  

*Heavenly mandārava flowers rained down,*  
*The heavenly drums sounded naturally and spontaneously,*  
*The devas and dragons, ghosts and spirits,*  
*All made offerings to the supreme person.*  

*All the Buddha-lands trembled and quaked.*  
*The Buddha emitted light between his brows,*  
*Revealing all rare and wondrous phenomena,*  
*This light illuminated to the east—*  

*Eighteen thousand Buddha-lands,*  
*All became brilliant gold in color,*  
*Revealing to all sentient beings,*  
*The places where birth and death occur.*  

*Some saw Buddha-lands adorned,*  
*With all kinds of precious treasures,*  
*Crystal, beryl in radiant color,*  
*Made brilliant by the Buddha's light.*  

*And the divine beings, humans,*  
*Dragons, spirits, night-wanderers,*  
*Gandharvas and celestial musicians,*  
*Each making offerings to their own Buddha.*  

*Again, the great Tathāgatas*  
*Naturally become enlightened upon the path,*  
*Their bodies like golden mountains,*  
*Incomparably dignified and wondrous,*  

*Like pure crystal within,*  
*With a true golden image manifested within.*  
*The World-Honored One among the great assembly,*  
*Expounds the profound dharma significance.*  

*In each Buddha-land,*  
*Innumerable hosts of voice-hearers gather,*  
*Because of the Buddha's light illumination,*  
*All these great assemblies are visible.*  

*Some see Bodhisattvas,*  
*In the mountains and forests,*  
*Diligently maintaining pure precepts,*  
*Protecting them like precious pearls.*  

*Others see Bodhisattvas,*  
*Cultivating giving, patience, and other virtues,*  
*Numbering like Ganges' sands,*  
*All revealed by the Buddha's light.*  

*Others see Bodhisattvas,*  
*Deeply absorbed in meditative states,*  
*Bodies and minds at rest and unmoving,*  
*Seeking the supreme path.*  

*Others see Bodhisattvas,*  
*Who understand the characteristics of phenomena,*  
*As having no duality,*  
*Like empty space.*  

*Within the four groups of disciples,*  
*Seeing the Sun Moon Lamp Bright Buddha,*  
*Displaying great supernatural powers,*  
*All hearts were filled with joy—*  

*Each asking another,*  
*What is the cause and reason for this?*  
*The being honored by heaven and earth,*  
*Has just risen from meditation,*  

*And praised the Bodhisattva Wonderful Light:*  
*"You are the eye of the world,*  
*In all things the object of refuge,*  
*Able to preserve the treasury of the Dharma,"*  

*As I expound the teachings,*  
*Only you can fully understand them.*  
*The World-Honored One having praised you,*  
*Made the Bodhisattva Wonderful Light rejoice.*  

*He then expounded the Lotus Sutra,*  
*Throughout sixty small eons without rising.*  
*All who heard the teachings,*  
*Were able to receive and maintain them.*  

*The Buddha spoke this Dharma,*  
*Bringing joy to the assembly,*  
*Then announced to all beings:*  
*"The true nature of phenomena,*  

*I have now expounded to you;*  
*I shall now enter parinirvāṇa in this night.*  
*You should exert yourselves diligently,*  
*Never indulging in negligence—*  

*For Buddhas are most difficult to encounter,*  
*Meeting one only through countless billions of eons."*  
*The Buddha's sons,*  
*Hearing of the Buddha's entry into parinirvāṇa,*  

*Each felt deep sorrow and distress—*  
*How quickly the sage will depart!*  
*The supreme dharma king,*  
*Comforted the vast assembly,*  

*Saying: "When I pass away,*  
*You should not despair or fear,*  
*This Bodhisattva Treasure Store*  
*Has realized the nature of emptiness—*  

*His mind has already penetrated it,*  
*Next he shall become a Buddha,*  
*Known as Pure Body Buddha,*  
*Who shall liberate countless beings."*  

*That Buddha passed away that night,*  
*Like fire extinguished when fuel is exhausted,*  
*His relics were distributed widely,*  
*And countless stūpas were erected.*  

*Bhikṣus and bhikṣuṇīs,*  
*Numbering like Ganges' sands,*  
*All redoubled their diligent practice,*  
*Seeking the supreme path.*  

*This Bodhisattva Wonderful Light,*  
*Preserved the treasury of the Buddha's Dharma,*  
*For eighty small eons,*  
*Widely expounding the Lotus Sutra.*  

*The eight royal sons,*  
*Guided and taught by Wonderful Light,*  
*Became firmly established in the path,*  
*Encountering countless Buddhas,*  

*Having made offerings to the Buddhas,*  
*And following the great path,*  
*They succeeded each other in becoming Buddhas,*  
*Each receiving prophecy in turn.*  

*The last supreme being among beings,*  
*Was named the Buddha of Burning Lamps,*  
*The guide and teacher of sages,*  
*Who liberated countless beings.*  

*That Bodhisattva Wonderful Light,*  
*Once had a disciple,*  
*Whose mind was constantly lazy,*  
*Attached to profit and fame,*  

*Seeking fame and profit without end,*  
*Often visiting noble families,*  
*Abandoning the study and recitation,*  
*Forgetting and failing to understand.*  

*For this reason he was called Seeker of Fame,*  
*Yet he cultivated many virtuous deeds,*  
*Encountered countless Buddhas,*  
*Making offerings with reverence and praise.*  

*In the future he shall become a Buddha,*  
*Named Maitreya Buddha,*  
*Liberating countless living beings,*  
*Without limit or measure.*  

*After that Buddha's parinirvāṇa,*  
*You who are lazy are that one—*  
*The Bodhisattva Wonderful Light of that age,*  
*Is now my own body.*  

*I saw the Burning Lamps Buddha,*  
*And how his original auspicious sign appeared—*  
*Because of this, I know today's Buddha,*  
*Desires to expound the Lotus Sutra.*  

*Now the signs are like before,*  
*These are the skillful means of all Buddhas—*  
*Now the Buddha emits light,*  
*To reveal the meaning of the ultimate nature of reality.*  

*All you people, know this:*  
*Place your palms together in reverence and wait,*  
*The Buddha shall rain down the dharma rain,*  
*Satisfying all who seek the path.*  

*All those who seek the three vehicles,*  
*If they harbor any doubt or hesitation,*  
*The Buddha shall dispel it completely,*  
*Leaving nothing remaining.*  

---

# Chapter 2: Skillful Means

## The Buddha's Opening Teaching on Buddha-Wisdom

At that time, the World-Honored One, having emerged from meditation with composed serenity, addressed Śāriputra:[^1]

"The wisdom of the Buddhas, the Tathāgatas, is infinitely profound and immeasurable. The gateway to this wisdom is difficult to comprehend and difficult to enter—beyond the capacity of all Śrāvakas (disciples) and Pratyekabuddhas (solitary awakeners) to understand. Why is this?

"The Buddhas have approached and made offerings to hundreds of thousands of billions of Tathāgatas beyond number. They have completely practiced the infinite dharmic pathways of all the Buddhas. With courageous diligence, their renown has spread universally. They have accomplished teachings utterly unprecedented and extraordinary.[^2]

"Their teachings, adapted to circumstances and conditions, are of meaning (arthas) most difficult to comprehend. Śāriputra, since my own attainment of Buddhahood, I have employed innumerable causes and conditions, boundless parables and illustrations, and infinite skillful means (upayā) to guide and transform all beings, enabling them to transcend all forms of attachment and clinging.[^3] Why is this?

"The Tathāgata has completely perfected the transcendent wisdom and vision of skillful means (upaya-jñāna-darsana). Śāriputra, the Tathāgata's wisdom and vision is boundless and vast, profound and far-reaching, infinite and unobstructed. His supernatural powers, fearlessness, meditative concentrations, liberations, and samadhis extend into the infinite and reach to the limit. The Tathāgata has accomplished teachings utterly unprecedented.

"Śāriputra, the Tathāgata is able to make distinctions among the various dharmas and to discourse skillfully upon them, employing words gentle and soft that bring joy to the hearts of all beings.[^4] Śāriputra, in essential summary, the Tathāgata has accomplished infinite, boundless, unprecedented teachings."[^5]

---

## The Buddha's Cessation: The Limits of Teaching

Then the Buddha said: "Cease, Śāriputra. There is no need to speak further. Why? The supremely rare and extraordinary teaching that the Buddha has accomplished—the dharma most difficult to understand—can only be fully penetrated and exhausted by the Buddha together with other Buddhas. I refer to the realm of reality in which:[^6]

"The various dharmas possess such-like characteristics, such-like natures, such-like bodies, such-like powers, such-like activities, such-like causes, such-like conditions, such-like effects, such-like retributions, and such-like their beginning and end, their ultimate equivalence."[^fn_ten_suchnesses]

[^fn_ten_suchnesses]: **The Ten Suchnesses (十如是):** This famous list of ten factors (*characteristics, nature, substance, power, activity, cause, condition, effect, retribution, and ultimate equality*) is unique to Kumārajīva's Chinese translation (*shí rúshì*) and does not appear in this form in the Sanskrit *Saddharmapuṇḍarīka* or other Chinese versions. It became the foundational scriptural basis for the Tiantai school's doctrine of "Three Thousand Realms in a Single Moment of Life" (*yinian sanqian*). Kumārajīva likely expanded the pithy Sanskrit "ye dharma hetu prabhava..." concept into this systematic list to clarify the mechanism of reality for Chinese readers.

---

## Verse Statement of Buddha-Wisdom's Transcendence

The World-Honored One, wishing to restate this meaning, then spoke in verse:

*The Lord of Sages cannot be measured—*  
*By all the devas and all people,*  
*All classes of sentient beings,*  
*None have the capacity to know the Buddha.*  

*The Buddha's power is without limitation,*  
*His fearlessness, his liberations, his concentrations,*  
*And all other Buddha-dharmas are,*  
*Beyond any capacity to measure.*  

*From countless numberless Buddhas,*  
*He has completely practiced all the paths,*  
*The profoundly subtle dharmas,*  
*Difficult to see and difficult to comprehend.*  

*Through immeasurable billions of eons,*  
*Having practiced all these pathways,*  
*Upon the seat of enlightenment,*  
*I have fully realized and perceived all this.*  

*Such great fruitions,*  
*With their diverse characteristics and meanings,*  
*Only I and the ten-direction Buddhas,*  
*Are able to know these things.*  

*This dharma cannot be demonstrated,*  
*Language and verbal expression exhaust themselves;*  
*All other classes of sentient beings,*  
*Have no capacity to comprehend it,*  

*Except for the Bodhisattva assembly,*  
*Whose faith-power is firmly established.*  
*The Buddha's disciples assembled here,*  
*Having made offerings to all the Buddhas,*  

*Who have exhausted all outflows,*  
*And dwell in this their final body,*  
*Such persons as these,*  
*Lack the capacity for this.*  

*Even if the entire world were filled,*  
*All like Śāriputra in wisdom,*  
*Collectively thinking and measuring,*  
*They could not fathom Buddha-wisdom.*  

*And should the entire ten directions,*  
*All be filled with Śāriputra-like beings,*  
*And all other disciples,*  
*Completely filling all the Buddha-lands,*  

*All collectively thinking and measuring,*  
*Still they could not know it.*  
*Pratyekabuddhas of keen intelligence,*  
*With the unconditioned final body,*  

*Completely filling all ten-direction worlds,*  
*Numbering like bamboo forests,*  
*All of these, in unified mind,*  
*Throughout billions of immeasurable eons,*  

*Desiring to contemplate Buddha-wisdom,*  
*Could not know even a fraction of it.*  
*Newly-aspiring Bodhisattvas,*  
*Having made offerings to countless Buddhas,*  

*Understanding various meanings,*  
*And able to discourse skillfully upon the dharma,*  
*As numerous as rice grains, hemp seeds, bamboo stalks, and reeds,*  
*Filling all the ten-direction Buddha-lands,*  

*All with transcendent wisdom,*  
*Throughout the Ganges' sand-number of eons,*  
*All together contemplating,*  
*Could not know Buddha-wisdom.*  

*The non-retrogressive Bodhisattvas,*  
*Numbering like Ganges' sands,*  
*All of one mind seeking to comprehend,*  
*Still could not know it.*  

*Again, I tell you, Śāriputra:*  
*The unconditioned, unthinkable,*  
*Profoundly subtle dharmas,*  
*I have now completely obtained.*  

*Only I am able to know their characteristics,*  
*And so too are the Buddhas of the ten directions.*  
*Śāriputra, you should know:*  
*The language of all Buddhas is without contradiction,*  

*Regarding the dharma spoken by the Buddha,*  
*You should generate great faith-power.*  
*The World-Honored One's dharma, after a long time,*  
*Will certainly speak the truth.*  

*Announcing to the assembly of Śrāvakas,*  
*And to those seeking the pratyekabuddha vehicle,*  
*I have enabled them to escape suffering's bonds,*  
*And to attain nirvāṇa.*  

*By the Buddha's skillful means-power,*  
*I have shown the three-vehicle teaching,*  
*And because sentient beings cling everywhere,*  
*I guide them to liberation.*  

---

## The Assembly's Confusion

At that time, there were in the great assembly twelve hundred Śrāvakas who had exhausted all outflows and were Arhats, including Ājñātakauṇḍinya and others, as well as those among the bhikṣus and bhikṣuṇīs, male and female lay disciples who had generated the aspiration toward Śrāvaka and Pratyekabuddha vehicles. All of them harbored this thought:

"Why does the World-Honored One so earnestly praise skillful means (upaya) and speak in this manner? He says that the dharma obtained by the Buddha is profoundly difficult to comprehend, that what he speaks is of meaning difficult to discern, that it exceeds the capacity of all Śrāvakas and Pratyekabuddhas to attain.

"The Buddha has spoken of one meaning of liberation,[^8] which we too have obtained, enabling us to reach nirvāṇa. Yet now we do not understand toward what end this teaching aims."[^9]

---

## Śāriputra's Inquiry

At that time, Śāriputra, recognizing the perplexity in the hearts of the fourfold assembly and being himself uncertain, addressed the Buddha:

"World-Honored One, for what cause and condition do you so earnestly praise the supreme skillful means of all the Buddhas—that dharma most profoundly subtle and difficult to comprehend? Since ancient times, I have never heard from the Buddha such teaching as this. Now the fourfold assembly harbors doubt about this matter. I beseech you, World-Honored One, to elucidate this matter! Why do you so earnestly praise the dharma so profoundly subtle and difficult to comprehend?"[^10]

---

## Śāriputra's Verse of Inquiry

Then Śāriputra, wishing to restate this meaning, spoke in verse:

*O Wisdom-Sun, Great Sage of Honor,*  
*Long have you refrained from speaking this dharma,*  
*You yourself have spoken of possessing such power, fearlessness, and concentrations,*  
*Meditations, liberations, and other inconceivable dharmas.*  

*The dharma obtained upon the seat of enlightenment,*  
*—no one has capacity to question about it.*  
*Your intention is difficult to measure,*  
*And there is none who can question you.*  

*Without being asked, you spontaneously speak,*  
*Praising the path you have traversed,*  
*Your wisdom is supremely subtle,*  
*The attainment of all the Buddhas.*  

*The unconditioned Arhats,*  
*And those seeking nirvāṇa,*  
*Now find themselves caught in a net of doubt—*  
*Why do you speak in this manner?*  

*Those seeking the pratyekabuddha vehicle,*  
*The bhikṣus and bhikṣuṇīs,*  
*All the devas, dragons, ghosts, and spirits,*  
*And the gandharvas and others,*  

*Gaze at each other with doubt in their hearts,*  
*Reverently looking to the Two-Footed Honored One,*  
*Asking: What is the meaning of this?*  
*I beseech the Buddha to explain.*  

*Regarding all the Śrāvaka assembly,*  
*The Buddha has said I am foremost.*  
*But I myself harbor doubt regarding wisdom—*  
*Is this the ultimate dharma, or is it the practiced path?*  

*Sons of the Buddha, joined hands reverently,*  
*Await in anticipation,*  
*Wishing to hear your subtle voice,*  
*At this time explaining what is truly so.*  

*The devas, dragons, and spiritual beings,*  
*Number like Ganges' sands,*  
*The Bodhisattvas seeking the Buddha,*  
*Are eighty thousand in great number.*  

*Moreover, all the billions of worlds,*  
*Including wheel-turning sage kings,*  
*With palms joined in reverent respect,*  
*Desire to hear the complete path.*  

---

## The Buddha's Hesitation and Reassurance

Then the Buddha said to Śāriputra: "Cease, cease! There is no need to speak further. If I were to explain this matter, the entire world of devas and humans would be astonished and filled with perplexity."[^11]

Śāriputra again respectfully addressed the Buddha: "World-Honored One, I beseech you to speak! I beseech you to speak! Why is this? This assembly includes immeasurable, hundreds of thousands of billions of asankhya sentient beings who have witnessed countless Buddhas before. Their faculties are keen and sharp, their wisdom is clear and lucid. These beings, having heard the dharma the Buddha speaks, will be able to generate respectful faith."[^12]

---

## Verse on the Assembly's Readiness

Then Śāriputra, wishing to restate this meaning, spoke in verse:

*O Dharma King without superior,*  
*I beseech you to speak without hesitation—*  
*This assembly contains immeasurable multitudes,*  
*Who are capable of generating respectful faith.*  

---

## The Buddha's Continued Reluctance

The Buddha again restrained Śāriputra, saying: "If I were to explain this matter, all the devas, humans, and asuras would be astonished. Moreover, monks seized by arrogant conceit will fall into a great abyss."[^13]

---

## The Buddha's Verse on the Difficulty of Teaching

Then the World-Honored One spoke in verse:

*Cease, cease—there is no need to speak.*  
*My dharma is wonderfully difficult to conceive,*  
*Those seized by arrogant conceit,*  
*Hearing it, will generate no respectful faith.*  

---

## Śāriputra's Final Entreaty

Then Śāriputra again respectfully addressed the Buddha: "World-Honored One, I beseech you to speak! I beseech you to speak! In this assembly, there are ones comparable to myself, numbering in the hundreds of thousands and billions across countless ages. Having long been transformed by the Buddha, such persons will certainly generate respectful faith and enjoy long safety and repose, receiving immeasurable benefit."[^14]

---

## Verse of Śāriputra's Final Request

Then Śāriputra, wishing to restate this meaning, spoke in verse:

*O Unsurpassed Two-Footed Honored One,*  
*I beseech you to teach the supreme dharma—*  
*I am the Buddha's eldest son,*  
*I alone receive your distinctions of teaching.*  

*This assembly contains immeasurable multitudes,*  
*Capable of generating faith in this dharma.*  
*The Buddha has, through countless ages,*  
*Taught and transformed beings such as these.*  

*All with unified, joined hands,*  
*Desire to hear the Buddha's words.*  
*We twelve hundred,*  
*Together with all who seek Buddhahood,*  

*On behalf of this assembly,*  
*I beseech you to make distinctions clear.*  
*These beings, hearing this dharma,*  
*Will generate great joy.*  

---

## The Buddha's Consent and the Departure of Doubters

Then the World-Honored One said to Śāriputra: "You have made your earnest request three times. How could I not speak? Now listen attentively and think carefully upon what I say. I shall make clear distinctions for you."[^15]

At the moment the Buddha spoke these words, there arose from their seats among the assembly five thousand bhikṣus, bhikṣuṇīs, male and female lay disciples, and they bowed to the Buddha and withdrew.[^16] Why was this?

"This group harbored deep karmic roots of transgression and, moreover, arrogant conceit. They presumed attainment without having truly attained, and presumed realization without having truly realized. Possessed of such failings, they did not remain. The World-Honored One, observing this, made no attempt to prevent them from departing."[^17]

---

## The Buddha's Affirmation of the Remaining Assembly

Then the Buddha said to Śāriputra: "Now my assembly here is entirely purified, without superfluous branches—consisting only of authentic fruit. Śāriputra, such proud and conceited persons departing is a good thing. Now listen well. I shall explain this to you. Śāriputra replied: 'Excellent, World-Honored One. I earnestly desire to hear.'"[^18]

---

## THE HEART OF THE TEACHING: THE ONE GREAT CAUSE

## The Rarity and Incomparability of the Buddha's Teaching

The Buddha then addressed Śāriputra:

"This Wonderful Dharma is something that all the Buddhas, the Tathāgatas, only rarely teach. It is comparable to the udumbara flower, which blooms but once in a very long age. Śāriputra, you and others should believe in the words of the Buddha, for the Buddha's speech is not false and cannot deceive.[^19]

"Śāriputra, the Buddhas teach the dharma adaptively (upaya) according to circumstances and conditions, and their meaning is difficult to comprehend. Why is this?

"I employ innumerable skillful means, various causes and conditions, parables and verbal expressions to expound upon the various dharmas. This dharma cannot be comprehended through thinking and discrimination—only the Buddhas are capable of knowing it.

"Why is this? All the Buddhas, the World-Honored Ones, appear in the world for one great cause alone. Śāriputra, what is meant by 'the Buddhas appear in the world for one great cause'?

"The Buddhas, the World-Honored Ones, appear in the world in order to open for sentient beings the perception of Buddha-wisdom (buddha-jñāna). They appear in order to show sentient beings the Buddha-perception. They appear in order to cause sentient beings to awaken to Buddha-perception. They appear in order to guide sentient beings into the path of Buddha-perception.[^20]

"Śāriputra, this is the one great cause for which the Buddhas appear in the world."[^21]

---

## The One Buddha Vehicle

"Śāriputra, the Buddhas teach and transform only Bodhisattvas. Whatever the Buddhas undertake to do is always for one purpose alone: to show sentient beings the Buddha-perception, to cause them to awaken to it.

"Śāriputra, because of the One Buddha Vehicle, the Tathāgata teaches the dharma to all sentient beings. There are no other vehicles—neither two nor three.[^22] Śāriputra, all the Buddhas of the ten directions teach the dharma in this very manner."[^23]

---

## Universal Attainment Through One Vehicle

"Śāriputra, the Buddhas of the past employed innumerable skillful means, various causes and conditions, parables and verbal expressions to expound upon the various dharmas. All these dharmas were for the One Buddha Vehicle alone. The sentient beings who heard the dharma from these Buddhas ultimately obtained the wisdom-knowing-all-aspects (sarvākārajñatā).[^24]

"Śāriputra, the Buddhas of the future shall appear in the world, and they too shall employ innumerable skillful means, various causes and conditions, parables and verbal expressions to expound upon the various dharmas. All these dharmas will be for the One Buddha Vehicle alone. The sentient beings who hear the dharma from these Buddhas shall ultimately obtain the wisdom-knowing-all-aspects.

"Śāriputra, in the present age, in the boundless, countless, billion-fold Buddha-lands of the ten directions, the World-Honored Ones who dwell there bring immeasurable benefit and peace to sentient beings. These Buddhas too employ innumerable skillful means, various causes and conditions, parables and verbal expressions to expound upon the various dharmas. All these dharmas are for the One Buddha Vehicle alone. The sentient beings who hear the dharma from these Buddhas shall ultimately obtain the wisdom-knowing-all-aspects.

"Śāriputra, these Buddhas teach and transform only Bodhisattvas, desiring to show sentient beings the Buddha-perception, desiring to cause sentient beings to awaken to the Buddha-perception, desiring to guide sentient beings into the path of Buddha-perception.

"Śāriputra, I too am now in precisely this manner. Knowing that sentient beings possess various desires, deeply attached according to their fundamental natures, I employ various causes and conditions, parables and verbal expressions, skillful means, to expound the dharma for them. Śāriputra, in all these ways, my purpose is to realize the One Buddha Vehicle and the wisdom-knowing-all-aspects."[^25]

---

## The Denial of the Three Vehicles in Absolute Reality

"Śāriputra, in the worlds of the ten directions, there do not even exist two vehicles, much less three. Śāriputra, the Buddhas appear in the world amid the five corruptions and turbidities[^26]—namely, the corruption of the age, the corruption of afflictions, the corruption of sentient beings, the corruption of views, and the corruption of lifespan.

"Thus, Śāriputra, when the age is corrupted and turbid, sentient beings are weighted with defilements, stingy and jealous, and have accumulated roots of unwholesomeness. Therefore, the Buddhas, by means of skillful means-power, within the One Buddha Vehicle, make distinctions and teach the three vehicles.[^27]

"Śāriputra, if my disciples, claiming to be Arhats or Pratyekabuddhas, do not hear about this matter—that the Tathāgata teaches and transforms only Bodhisattvas—then they are not disciples of the Buddha, not Arhats, and not Pratyekabuddhas."[^28]

---

## The False Claim of Arhatship

"Moreover, Śāriputra, those bhikṣus and bhikṣuṇīs who claim they have already attained the state of Arhat, that this is their final body, and that they have ultimately realized nirvāṇa, and therefore no longer aspire to realize anuttara-samyak-saṃbodhi—you should understand that such persons are seized by arrogant conceit.

"Why is this? If a bhikṣu truly attains Arhatship, if he does not believe in this dharma, such a situation is impossible.[^29] [Exception exists only] when the Buddha has entered parinirvāṇa and no Buddha is present in the world.

"Why is this? After the Buddha enters parinirvāṇa, if there are persons who receive, read, recite, and understand the meaning of sutras such as this, these persons are rare indeed. When they encounter another Buddha, regarding this dharma they will attain decisive understanding.

"Śāriputra, you and all others should generate one-pointed faith and understanding, and receive and uphold the Buddha's words. The Tathāgata and all other Buddhas do not speak falsity. There are no other vehicles—the Buddha Vehicle alone exists."[^30]

---

## Verse Recapitulation of the One Vehicle Teaching

Then the World-Honored One, wishing to restate this meaning, spoke in verse:

*Bhikṣus and bhikṣuṇīs,*  
*Those harboring arrogant conceit,*  
*Male lay practitioners of pride,*  
*Female lay practitioners of faithlessness,*  

*Such among these four groups,*  
*Numbering five thousand in total,*  
*Who do not perceive their own shortcomings,*  
*With respect to the precepts possessing flaws,*  

*Who protect and hide their defects—*  
*The small-minded have now departed,*  
*The chaff among the assembly,*  
*Gone due to the Buddha's majesty.*  

*Now this assembly contains no branches,*  
*Consisting entirely of authentic fruit.*  
*Śāriputra, listen carefully!*  
*The dharma the Buddhas obtain,*  

*Is through immeasurable skillful means-power,*  
*That they teach the various dharmas to sentient beings.*  
*The beings' hearts' intentions,*  
*The various paths they pursue,*  

*The differing desires and natures,*  
*And the wholesome and unwholesome deeds from the past—*  
*The Buddha, having completely understood all this,*  
*By means of causes, conditions, parables, and verbal expressions,*  

*And skillful means-power,*  
*Teaches all beings to their joy.*  
*Teaching sutras and poetic gathas,*  
*Stories and previous lives,*  

*And also on causes and conditions,*  
*Parables, verses, and analytic discourse—*  
*Those of dull faculties who delight in small dharmas,*  
*Clinging to birth and death,*  

*Among the countless Buddhas,*  
*Not practicing the profound subtle path,*  
*Troubled by all sufferings,*  
*For such beings I teach nirvāṇa.*  

*I create this skillful means,*  
*To enable them to enter Buddha-wisdom,*  
*Never before have I taught that you,*  
*Should attain the Buddha path.*  

*Why have I not taught this before?*  
*Because the time for speaking had not yet come.*  
*Now at last the time has arrived—*  
*I shall now decisively teach the great vehicle.*  

*These nine categories of teaching,*  
*I teach in accordance with sentient beings,*  
*Taking the great vehicle as the foundation,*  
*Therefore I teach this sutra.*  

*There are Buddha-children,*  
*Pure of heart and of pliable faculties,*  
*Who have before countless Buddhas,*  
*Practiced the profound subtle path.*  

*For all such Buddha-children,*  
*I teach this great-vehicle sutra.*  
*I prophesy to such beings,*  
*That in the future they shall become Buddhas,*  

*Because of deep mindfulness toward the Buddha,*  
*And constant cultivation of pure precepts.*  
*Upon hearing the Buddha's dharma,*  
*Great joy fills their entire bodies.*  

*The Buddha knows their minds and deeds,*  
*And therefore teaches them the great vehicle.*  
*Whether Śrāvakas or Bodhisattvas,*  
*Who hear the dharma I teach,*  

*Even to the extent of a single verse,*  
*All shall without doubt become Buddhas.*  
*In the Buddha-lands of the ten directions,*  
*There exists only the One Vehicle dharma—*  

*Neither two nor three.*  
*Except for the Buddhas' skillful means-teaching,*  
*Which merely uses provisional names,*  
*To guide sentient beings,*  

*Speaking of Buddha-wisdom.*  
*All the Buddhas who appear in the world,*  
*Accomplish this single real principle,*  
*While the other two are not true.*  

*They shall never employ the small vehicle,*  
*To liberate any sentient being at all.*  
*The Buddha dwells in the great vehicle,*  
*In accordance with the dharma obtained,*  

*Adorned with concentrated power and wisdom,*  
*With this they liberate sentient beings.*  
*Having themselves realized the supreme path,*  
*The impartial dharma of the great vehicle,*  

*If one were to use the small vehicle,*  
*Even to transform a single person,*  
*I would fall into stinginess and attachment—*  
*This is an impossible matter.*  

*If a person takes refuge in the Buddha,*  
*The Tathāgata does not deceive or betray,*  
*Nor harbors any stingy or jealous intent,*  
*But severs all evil dharmas.*  

*Therefore the Buddha, in the ten directions,*  
*Stands alone without fear.*  
*I adorn my body with the sublime marks,*  
*And my light illuminates the world.*  

*Honored by countless multitudes,*  
*To proclaim the seal of the real nature of reality.[^31]*  
*Śāriputra, you should know,*  
*I have established the original vow,*  

*Desiring that all beings,*  
*Would be equal with me.*  
*As I vowed in the past,*  
*Now this is fully accomplished—*  

*I teach all sentient beings,*  
*Causing them to enter the Buddha path.*  
*If I encounter any sentient being,*  
*I teach them all the Buddha path—*  

*Those without wisdom become confused,*  
*Bewildered and unable to receive the teaching.*  
*I know such sentient beings,*  
*Have never cultivated wholesome roots,*  

*Firmly attached to the five desires,*  
*Caused suffering by delusion and craving.*  
*Because of various desire-conditions,*  
*They fall and descend into the three evil paths,*  

*Circling through the six destinies,*  
*Completely experiencing all suffering and pain,*  
*Receiving tiny embryonic forms,*  
*Continually increasing through world after world.*  

*Those of slight virtue and meager good fortune,*  
*Pressed upon by all sufferings,*  
*Enter into forests of perverted views—*  
*Viewing existence and non-existence equally.*  

*Relying on such perverted views,*  
*Possessed of sixty-two such views,*  
*Deeply attached to false dharmas,*  
*Firmly grasping them as inseparable,*  

*With self-pride and exalted conceit,*  
*Scheming hearts and untruthful intentions,*  
*For billions of eons,*  
*They hear not the Buddha's name,*  

*Nor hear the correct dharma—*  
*Such beings are difficult to liberate.*  
*Therefore, Śāriputra,*  
*I create skillful means,*  

*Teaching all dharmas that exhaust suffering,*  
*Showing them nirvāṇa.*  
*Although I teach nirvāṇa,*  
*This is also not true extinction.*  

*For all dharmas have,*  
*From the beginning, the characteristic of quiescence.*  
*Buddha-children practicing the path,*  
*In the future will become Buddhas.*  

*I possess skillful means-power,*  
*Opening and revealing the three-vehicle dharmas.*  
*All the World-Honored Ones,*  
*All speak the one-vehicle path—*  

*In this assembly,*  
*All should cast off their doubts.*  
*The language of the Buddhas is without variance—*  
*Only One Vehicle without a second.*  

*In past countless eons,*  
*Countless, immeasurable Buddhas have passed away,*  
*A hundred thousand billion types,*  
*Beyond measure in number.*  

*All such World-Honored Ones,*  
*Through various causes, conditions, and parables,*  
*Immeasurable skillful means-power,*  
*Expounded the characteristics of various dharmas.*  

*All these World-Honored Ones,*  
*All taught the one-vehicle dharma,*  
*Transforming countless sentient beings,*  
*Causing them to enter the Buddha path.*  

*Again, all the great sage-rulers,*  
*Knowing all the world—*  
*Devas, humans, and all other living kinds,*  
*The deep desires of their hearts—*  

*By means of alternative skillful means,*  
*They further reveal the supreme reality.[^32]*  
*If there are sentient beings,*  
*Who encounter the Buddhas of the past,*  

*Or hearing the dharma of giving,*  
*Or maintaining precepts, practicing patience,*  
*Exerting effort, meditation, and wisdom—*  
*Cultivating all manner of virtue and good fortune—*  

*All such persons,*  
*Have already become Buddhas.*  
*After the Buddhas have passed away,*  
*If beings possess gentle, soft hearts,*  

*All such sentient beings,*  
*Have already become Buddhas.*  
*After the Buddhas have passed away,*  
*Those who make offerings to the relics,*  

*Erecting billions of kinds of stūpas,*  
*Of gold, silver, and crystal,*  
*Beryl and agate,*  
*Pearls and jewels—*  

*Brightly adorned with purity,*  
*Decorated and ornate with many stūpas,*  
*Or building stone temples,*  
*Sandalwood and aloe-wood,*  

*Timber and other materials,*  
*Brick, tile, clay and earth—*  
*Or in wastelands,*  
*Accumulating earth into Buddha shrines,*  

*Even children at play,*  
*Piling sand to make Buddha stūpas—*  
*All such persons as these,*  
*Have already become Buddhas.*  

*If a person, for the Buddha's sake,*  
*Establishes all manner of Buddha images,*  
*Carving and sculpting all kinds of forms—*  
*All have already become Buddhas.*  

*Made from the seven precious substances,*  
*Copper, stone, red and white bronze,*  
*White lead and tin,*  
*Wood and clay, etc.—*  

*Or with glue, lacquer, and cloth,*  
*All adorned as Buddha images—*  
*All such persons as these,*  
*Have already become Buddhas.*  

*Painted and rendered as Buddha images,*  
*Adorned with the hundred-fold blessings—*  
*Whether one creates or directs others to create—*  
*All have already become Buddhas.*  

*Even to the extent that children in play,*  
*With grass, wood, or a brush,*  
*Or with their fingernails or teeth,*  
*Paint Buddha images—*  

*All such persons as these,*  
*Gradually accumulate blessed merit,*  
*Complete the heart of great compassion,*  
*And have already become Buddhas.*  

*Transforming only Bodhisattvas,*  
*Liberating countless sentient beings.*  
*If a person, in stūpas or temples,*  
*With precious images and painted ones,*  

*Makes offerings with flowers, incense, banners, and canopies,*  
*With a heart of reverent respect.*  
*Or causes music to be made,*  
*Striking drums and blowing horns and conches,*  

*Flutes, lyres, and harps,*  
*Lutes and cymbals, and brass bells—*  
*All such marvelous sounds,*  
*Are employed in making offerings.*  

*Or with a joyful heart,*  
*One sings hymns praising the Buddha's virtue—*  
*To the extent of even one small utterance,*  
*All have already become Buddhas.*  

*If a person with distracted mind,*  
*Even offers a single flower,*  
*To a painted Buddha image,*  
*They shall gradually see countless Buddhas.*  

*Or if someone bows,*  
*Or merely joins their palms,*  
*Lifts a single hand,*  
*Or even slightly bows the head,*  

*In making offerings to an image—*  
*They shall gradually perceive countless Buddhas.*  
*And will themselves attain the supreme path,*  
*Widely liberating countless sentient beings,*  

*Entering the unconditioned parinirvāṇa,*  
*Like fire extinguished when fuel is exhausted.*  
*If a person with scattered mind,*  
*Enters into a stūpa or temple,*  

*And utters a single "Homage to the Buddha,"*  
*All have already become Buddhas.*  
*Regarding past Buddhas,*  
*Both in their living presence and after their passing,*  

*If any being hears this dharma,*  
*All have already become Buddhas.*  
*The future World-Honored Ones,*  
*Shall be boundless in number,*  

*All such Tathāgatas,*  
*Shall also teach the dharma through skillful means.*  
*All the Tathāgatas,*  
*Through immeasurable skillful means-power,*  

*Liberate all sentient beings,*  
*Causing them to enter the Buddha's unconditioned wisdom.*  
*If there is one who hears the dharma,*  
*There is none who shall not become a Buddha.*  

*All the Buddhas' original vows,*  
*Are that the path I have practiced,*  
*I universally desire all sentient beings,*  
*To attain this path equally.*  

*The future World-Honored Ones,*  
*Though teaching hundreds of billions,*  
*Of countless dharma-teachings,*  
*In reality constitute but one vehicle.*  

*All the Buddhas, the two-footed honored ones,*  
*Know that dharma is ever without nature,*  
*Buddha-seed arises from conditions—*  
*Therefore they teach the one vehicle.*[^33]  

---

## Conclusion: The Truth of the Teaching

"This dharma dwells in the dharmic position; the characteristics of the world ever remain constant. Upon the seat of enlightenment, having understood this, the guide teaches it through skillful means.[^34]

"The beings honored by heaven and people, the present Buddhas in the ten directions, numbering like Ganges' sands, appearing in the world in order to bring peace to sentient beings, all teach this same dharma.

"Understanding supreme quiescence through skillful means-power, although they show various paths, in reality this is the Buddha Vehicle. Understanding sentient beings' practices, the deep desires of their hearts, their past habits and karmic deeds, the desires and exertions of their faculties, dull and keen—through various causes, conditions, parables, and verbal expressions, they teach adaptively according to circumstances.

"I too am now in this manner, bringing peace to sentient beings through infinite dharma-teachings, revealing the Buddha path.

"I employ the power of wisdom to know sentient beings' natures and desires, teaching the dharmas through skillful means such that all attain joy.

"Śāriputra, with the Buddha-eye I observe the six-path sentient beings—poor, without virtue and good fortune, entering the dangerous path of birth and death, their suffering continuously unceasing, deeply attached to the five desires, like oxen attached to their own tails, blinded by greed and affection, unseeing.

"They do not seek the power of the great Mahāsattva Buddha, nor seek the dharma that cuts suffering; they deeply enter perverted views, and with suffering seek to transcend suffering.

"For the sake of such sentient beings, I generate the mind of great compassion.

"When I initially sat upon the seat of enlightenment, observing the trees and practicing circumambulation, within twenty-one days, I contemplated this matter: The wisdom I have obtained is subtle and supreme; sentient beings are dull-witted, bound by blindness and suffering—how can they be liberated?

"At that time, all the Brahmā kings, the devas of India, the Four Heavenly Kings, and the great Maheśvara devas, together with all celestial retinues numbering in the hundreds of thousands and millions, showed respect through palms joined in salutation, requesting me to turn the Dharma wheel.

"I then reflected within myself: If I merely praise the Buddha Vehicle, sentient beings submerged in suffering will be unable to generate faith in this dharma. If they reject the dharma due to faithlessness, they will fall into the three evil paths. It would be better for me not to teach the dharma and to quickly enter parinirvāṇa.[^35]

"Then I recalled the skillful means-power of the Buddhas of the past. Now, the path I have obtained should also employ teaching of the three vehicles.

"While contemplating this matter, all the Buddhas of the ten directions appeared to me and spoke with voices of Brahmā, comforting me: 'Well done, Śākyamuni, supreme guide! We have also obtained this dharma. In accordance with the conduct of all the Buddhas, we employ skillful means-power.

"'We too have all attained the supreme, most wonderful dharma. In order to teach all sentient beings, we make distinctions among the three vehicles. Although we teach the three vehicles, it is only to guide Bodhisattvas.

"'Those of limited wisdom delight in small dharmas and do not generate faith that they shall become Buddhas. This is why we employ skillful means, distinguishing the results.

"'Although we teach the three vehicles, in reality we guide all toward the Bodhisattva path.'

"Śāriputra, upon hearing the words of these Buddha-sages, and recalling their words, I rejoiced and called out, 'Homage to the Buddhas!' and contemplated this matter further.[^36]

"I realized that the appearance of Buddhas in the world is to teach Buddha-wisdom. And now is precisely the time to teach this dharma.[^37]

"Śāriputra, you should know: Those of dull faculties, those of limited wisdom, those seized by attachment and arrogant conceit, are unable to generate faith in this dharma.

"Now I am glad and without fear regarding all Bodhisattvas. I shall forthwith abandon skillful means and teach only the supreme path.

"The Bodhisattvas, having heard this dharma, will have their nets of doubt completely severed. The twelve hundred Arhats shall all become Buddhas.[^38]

"Just as all the Buddhas of the three times teach the dharma through such methods, I now likewise teach the undifferentiated dharma.

"The appearance of Buddhas in the world is extraordinarily rare, and the chance to encounter them is difficult; even if one encounters them, to hear this dharma is rare; and the capacity to listen to this dharma is rare indeed.

"It is comparable to the udumbara flower, which all love and esteem, which devas and humans regard as rare, appearing only at certain times.

"One who hears this dharma with joyful praise, even to the extent of uttering a single word, has already made offerings to all the Buddhas of the three times. Such a person is extremely rare, surpassing even the udumbara flower.

"You should harbor no doubt! I am the Dharma King of all dharmas,[^39] and I hereby universally announce to the great assembly: It is through the One Buddha Vehicle alone that I teach the Bodhisattvas. There are no voice-hearer disciples.

"You, Śāriputra, together with all voice-hearers and Bodhisattvas, should understand that this wonderful dharma is the secret treasury of all the Buddhas.[^40]

"Because the five corruptions exist in this evil world, sentient beings delight in and cling to various desires. Such beings will never seek the Buddha path. When those evil-natured humans of the future age hear the Buddha teaching the One Vehicle, confused and faithless, they will reject the dharma and fall into the evil paths.[^41]

"But for those possessing shame and purity, seeking the Buddha path, I shall extensively praise the One Vehicle path.

"Śāriputra, you should know: The dharma of all Buddhas is thus—through immeasurable skillful means, teaching dharmas according to circumstances. Those who have not studied and learned cannot fully comprehend this.[^42]

"Now that you have already understood the Buddhas' nature and the matter of teaching through skillful means, without any further doubts, your hearts generate great joy, and you shall surely become Buddhas."

*[End of Fascicle 1 (卷一)]*

---

# Chapter 3: Parables

## Śāriputra's Joy and Understanding

At that time, Śāriputra, overflowing with joy and delight, immediately rose from his seat, pressed his palms together in salutation, gazed upon the Buddha's face with reverent attention, and addressed the Buddha:

"Now, having heard this dharma-sound from the World-Honored One, my heart overflows with joy and I have experienced what has never been experienced before. Why is this?

"In ancient times, when I heard from the Buddha such a teaching as this, I saw that the various Bodhisattvas received prophecies of Buddhahood, yet I and my companions were not included in these events. I deeply sorrowed within myself, feeling that I had lost the infinite wisdom of the Tathāgata.[^1]

"World-Honored One, I have often dwelt alone in mountain forests and beneath trees, whether sitting or walking, constantly entertaining this thought: 'We have all entered into the dharma-nature equally—why then does the Tathāgata appear to guide us through the small vehicle?' This fault lies with us, not with the World-Honored One. Why is this?

"Had we expected the teaching of that which would enable us to achieve anuttara-samyak-saṃbodhi, we would surely have been liberated through the great vehicle.
