In all directions—south, west, north, the four intermediate directions, above and below—in every region touched by the radiance of this white-light beam from the Buddha's brow curl, the same cosmic vision appeared: infinite worlds, each containing innumerable Buddhas and Bodhisattvas, all teaching the Dharma together in perfect synchronization.[^13]

Then all the Buddhas in these ten directions, observing what had occurred, spoke to their assembled Bodhisattvas:

"Good children, we must now journey to the Śākyamuni Buddha's realm, the Sahā world, to do honor to both Śākyamuni Buddha and the stupa of Prabhūtaratna Buddha."[^14]

In that instant, the Sahā world transformed completely. It became luminous and pure, with crystal serving as its earth. Precious trees adorned its landscape. Golden ropes marked out the eight cardinal paths. All villages, towns, cities, settlements, oceans, rivers, and mountain ranges simply vanished from sight, made invisible. The entire realm was perfumed with precious incense, and mandāra flowers covered the ground completely. Precious nets wove themselves above the entire landscape. Precious bells hung suspended in the air. Only the assembly of those present at this teaching remained visible in this realm; all other celestial beings and humans were transferred to other worlds to make room for what was about to occur.[^15]

Then each Buddha from the ten directions, bringing with them a single great Bodhisattva as an attendant, journeyed toward the Sahā world. Each arrived at the foot of a precious tree. Each precious tree stood five hundred *yojanas* in height, with branches, leaves, flowers, and fruits arranged in perfect harmony. Beneath every precious tree was set a lion-throne, five *yojanas* in height, adorned with the finest precious substances.[^16] Upon these thrones, all the Buddhas arranged themselves in the meditation posture, legs crossed.

Continuing in this manner, the Buddhas spread throughout the entire three-thousand-fold thousand-fold world-system. Yet even as the Buddha-assembly covered this entire cosmic expanse, the division-bodies of Śākyamuni Buddha—those manifestations sent to one direction alone—had still not all arrived.[^17]

To provide space for all the remaining Buddhas to gather, Śākyamuni Buddha transformed eight additional cosmic regions beyond the eight primary directions. In each region, he created two hundred million times a billion *yojanas* of additional worlds, all made pure and radiant. He removed all hells, hungry ghosts, animals, and asuras from these worlds, and transferred the celestial beings and humans dwelling there to other realms to make space. These transformed worlds too had crystal as their foundation, precious trees for adornment, trees five hundred *yojanas* in height with perfectly arranged branches, leaves, flowers, and fruits. Beneath each tree stood a lion-throne five *yojanas* high, adorned with precious substances. These worlds had no oceans, rivers, or great mountains—the entire region became a single unified Buddha-realm of perfect clarity. The earth itself became pure and gleaming, with precious curtains draped above it. Precious bells hung suspended everywhere. Great precious incense filled the air, and celestial flowers covered the ground.[^18]

The Buddha prepared yet another eight regions beyond these for the remaining division-bodies to sit within. In each region, he transformed two hundred million times a billion *yojanas* of additional worlds, purifying them completely. He removed all suffering realms from them and transferred other beings to different worlds. All these worlds too became bases of crystal, adorned with precious trees, with perfect arrangements of branches, leaves, flowers, and fruits. Lion-thrones of five *yojanas* stood beneath each tree. No oceans, rivers, or mountains existed here. Each realm became a single, unified Buddha-realm. The earth was pure and gleaming, precious curtains hung everywhere, precious bells were suspended, great precious incense filled the space, and the flowers of the celestial realms covered the ground entirely.[^19]

Now in sequence, all the Buddha-bodies that Śākyamuni had manifested in the eastern direction—those dwelling in lands numbering beyond the mathematical limits of description—all came together to this gathering. In this manner, all the Buddhas from the ten directions progressively assembled. In each of the eight outer directions, four hundred million times a billion *yojanas* of Buddha-lands were completely filled with seated Buddhas. Each Buddha sat beneath a precious tree upon a lion-throne, and each sent an attendant to offer respects to Śākyamuni Buddha. These attendants carried precious flowers in both hands as they approached, speaking these words:

"Good child, go to Vulture Peak where Śākyamuni Buddha dwells. Convey greetings from our Buddha, saying: 'May the Buddha be well and free from afflictions. May all Bodhisattvas and disciples be at ease and at peace. Our Buddha sends you these flowers as an offering and expresses our wish to open the precious stupa together.'"[^20]

All the Buddhas in the ten directions sent their messengers in this manner.

When Śākyamuni Buddha beheld all his division-bodies assembled and at rest upon their lion-thrones, when he heard from all the Buddhas their agreement to open the precious stupa together, he rose from his seat and stood suspended in empty space. All the assembly of four kinds of beings rose up and joined their palms together, focusing their complete attention upon the Buddha.[^21]

At that moment, Śākyamuni Buddha extended his right hand and opened the seven-jeweled stupa. As the doors opened, a great sound echoed forth—like the turning of keys in locks, like the opening of great city gates. In that instant, the entire assembly could perceive Prabhūtaratna Buddha sitting in meditation posture upon a lion-throne inside the stupa. His body appeared completely whole and incorrupt, as if he were still in the depths of profound *samādhi*.[^22]

From within the stupa, Prabhūtaratna Buddha spoke these words: "Excellent, excellent, Śākyamuni Buddha! You have eloquently taught the Lotus Sutra. It was precisely to hear this Dharma that I made my original vow and came to this place."[^23]

When all the four kinds of beings witnessed this ancient Buddha—one who had passed into extinction countless eons ago—yet heard him speak in this very moment, they were filled with wonder beyond measure. Using precious celestial flowers gathered in heaps, they scattered countless offerings over both Prabhūtaratna Buddha and Śākyamuni Buddha.[^24]

Then Prabhūtaratna Buddha, still seated within the stupa, created space upon his own lion-throne and spoke to Śākyamuni: "Śākyamuni Buddha, please sit upon this seat beside me."[^25]

In that moment, Śākyamuni Buddha entered the stupa and sat upon the half-seat offered to him, placing himself in the meditation posture beside the ancient Buddha. Now the great assembly perceived that both Buddhas sat together in the seven-jeweled stupa upon the lion-throne, their bodies in perfect meditation.

Beholding this vision, each being in the assembly generated this thought: "The Buddha's seat is very high and far away. We wish that the World Honored One would use his supernatural power to allow us all to dwell together in empty space."[^26]

Immediately, through his supernatural powers, Śākyamuni Buddha lifted the entire great assembly upward, placing them all in the empty sky. Then, with a voice that resonated throughout all directions, the Buddha proclaimed to the four kinds of beings:

"Who will be able to extensively teach the supreme Lotus Sutra in this Sahā world?**Now is the time.** The Tathāgata will soon enter final *parinirvāṇa*. The Buddha wishes to entrust this supreme Lotus Sutra to someone for transmission. I seek those who will accept this sacred responsibility."[^27]

---
## At that time, the World Honored One, wishing to express this teaching again, spoke in verse:
The mighty saint, the World Honored One,
Though long ago he passed away—
His sacred form still dwells,
Within the tower, for Dharma's sake.

What living being would not strive,
To undertake the sacred work?
This Buddha's extinction occurred,
In eons countless as the sands.

Yet still he journeys everywhere,
To hear the teaching that is rare.[^28]
For such was his original vow:
When I have passed beyond this life,
Wherever the true Dharma lives,
I shall appear to hear it taught.

My transformation-bodies too,
Innumerable as sand-grains vast—
They come now seeking to hear the truth,
And to behold the Buddha gone.

Each one abandons precious lands,
Leaves disciples, heavenly hosts,
All who make offerings sacred—
To keep the Dharma ever true,
These Buddhas journey here to dwell.

That all these Buddhas find their seats,
Through supernatural power's grace,
Innumerable beings move,
So all worlds become supremely pure.

Each Buddha sits beneath a tree,
At the foundations luminous—
Like unto lotus flowers white,
Adorning a most perfect pond.

Beneath these trees of precious hue,
The lion-thrones of Buddhas wait—
The Buddhas sit in glory there,
Their forms adorned with radiant light.

As darkness flees before great fire,
So shines their presence through all worlds.
Their sacred fragrance fills the space,
All beings sense and know great joy,

Just as the wind that bends the branch
Of trees so tender, small, and weak.[^29]

By such compassionate device,
The Dharma will endure through time.
The Buddha tells the gathered throng:
When I have entered into rest,
Who shall protect, who shall proclaim,
Who will maintain this Dharma true?

Let all declare before me now,
Your sacred vow to uphold this law.[^30]

That ancient Buddha, Prabhūtaratna,
Though eons past his leaving went,
Still roars like lion for the Dharma—
Such is the power of the vow!

Both Prabhūtaratna and myself,
Along with all the Buddhas here—
Understand that what we seek,
Is who will uphold this sacred way.

All Bodhisattva children true,
Who shall protect this Dharma-realm?
Now make your vows, profound and great,
That this true teaching may endure.

All those who guard this sacred Dharma,
Make offerings to me and him,
For Prabhūtaratna's stupa dwells,
Forever journeying through ten worlds—

For this Dharma's sake, it travels,
To make vast offerings as well,
To all the Buddhas manifested,
Who adorn and glorify the worlds.

When this Dharma is proclaimed and taught,
You are perceiving both myself,
And Prabhūtaratna Buddha,
With all the manifested Buddhas.

All children virtuous and true,
Observe this carefully and well:
What we proclaim to you this day,
This is indeed the deepest truth.

What other teachers, other ways,
Are numberless as grains of sand—
Yet even were they taught to all,
This would not yet be reckoned hard.

If one could take Mount Sumeru,
The cosmic mountain at world's core,
And fling it far across the void,
To other Buddha-lands afar—
Even this would not be hard.

If one could use a single finger,
To move the mighty thousand-fold worlds,[^31]
To hurl them far to other regions,
Even this would not be hard.

If one could stand at the world's apex,
Where the highest gods reside,
And teach innumerable sutras,
Other teachings without bound—
Even this would not be hard.[^32]

But if, when I have passed away,
A being could proclaim this Dharma,
When hatred, hatred fills this age,**This indeed would be most hard.**[^33]

If one could grasp the empty air itself,
And walk upon it as a path,
Even this would not be hard.
But if, after my extinction comes,
A being writes this scripture down,
Or has another write for them—**This indeed would be most hard.**

If one could place the vast earth,
Upon the tip of one small nail,
Then carry it to the Brahma heavens,
Even this would not be hard.

But if, when I have passed from life,
A being reads this scripture,
For just a brief and fleeting moment,**This indeed would be most hard.**[^34]

If ages burned in cosmic fire,
And one could carry grass so dry,
And enter that great conflagration,
Carrying it all through without burning—
Even this would not be hard.

But if, when I have entered rest,
A being teaches this scripture,
For even one single person,**This indeed would be most hard.**

If one could teach and comprehend,
Eighty thousand dharma-treasures,
The twelve-fold divisions of all teachings,
Leading countless sentient beings,
Billions, trillions, sand-grain multitudes,
All to attain the state of *arhat*,
Granting each supernatural powers—
Even this would not be hard.

But if, when I have passed beyond,
A being holds this scripture fast,
Receives it and maintains its truth,**This indeed would be most hard.**[^35]

I have proclaimed the Dharma widely,
Throughout a thousand billion lands,
Since time without beginning,
I have taught the sacred Dharma,
Yet among all these teachings,
This scripture stands preeminent.

All those who have the power to hold it,
Hold the Buddha's very body.

Now all my virtuous children,
After my extinction has occurred,
Who shall receive this scripture,
Read and recite its sacred words?
Come now, speak your vows before me,
Your solemn promise in this place.

This Dharma is most hard to hold—
Should anyone keep it briefly,
This Buddha will rejoice,
All Buddhas will rejoice likewise.

Such is the being whom the Buddhas,
Will proclaim with heartfelt praise:
This is the courageous one,
This is the diligent practitioner,
This one keeps the precepts pure,
This one practices *dhūta* austerity—[^36]
Such a being shall swiftly gain,
The most supreme and highest way.

Those who can read and hold,
This scripture in time to come,
Are truly the children of Buddha,
Dwelling in the place of goodness.

When Buddhas pass away,
Those who understand their meaning,
These shall be the eyes,
Of all the heavenly and human worlds.

In this age of fear and darkness,
Those who teach this scripture,
For even a fleeting moment,
All the heavens and humans,
Should come and make offerings,
To such a rare and precious being.

---

# Chapter 12: Devadatta and the Nāga Princess

## THE REDEMPTION OF THE ANTAGONIST; THE INSTANTANEOUS ENLIGHTENMENT OF THE EXCLUDED
At that moment, the Buddha addressed all the Bodhisattvas and the four kinds of celestial and human beings:

"Throughout the incomprehensibly distant past—through countless eons—I have sought this Lotus Sutra without ever becoming weary. During many aeons, I lived as a universal monarch, who made a great vow to seek the supreme enlightenment without ever wavering in resolve. Desiring to completely fulfill the six transcendent perfections, I practiced generosity with the most open heart, never hoarding or grasping.[^1]

"I gave without measure: elephants and horses, the seven precious treasures, my kingdoms and cities, wives and sons, servants and attendants. I even offered my head, eyes, bone-marrow, brain, and flesh—my entire body was offered as the cost of obtaining this teaching. During those ages, human life-spans were immeasurable. For the sake of this Dharma, I abandoned my throne and transferred the kingdom to my son. I caused great drums to be struck and proclaimed throughout all directions: 'Who is there who can teach me the Great Vehicle? Whoever explains the supreme teaching to me, I shall serve as their slave and attendant throughout my entire life.'

"At that time, a sage-hermit came before me and said: 'I possess a Great Vehicle called the supreme Lotus Sutra. If you do not rebel against me, I shall unfold its teaching for you.'

"Hearing these words, my heart overflowed with delight and my whole being trembled with joy. I immediately followed that hermit-sage, providing for all his needs. I gathered fruits and drew water. I collected firewood and prepared food. Even more than this—I used my own body as a seat upon which he might rest. With neither weariness in body nor fatigue in mind, I served him continuously for one thousand years, attending diligently to his every need so that nothing was lacking.[^2]

"The monks and disciples must now hear what I will tell you: that hermit-sage of that ancient time—that one is now Devadatta.[^3]

"It is through Devadatta as a good friend that I have been able to perfect the six transcendent perfections, the four measureless states of mind, the thirty-two marks of a Buddha, and the eighty beautiful characteristics. It is through Devadatta that I have developed the ten powers, the four kinds of fearlessness, the four methods of gathering others to myself, the eighteen unique Buddha-qualities, and all supernatural powers and capacities. It is through Devadatta that I have achieved supreme, perfect enlightenment and am now able to teach sentient beings extensively. All of this—my complete enlightenment and universal teaching—arises from Devadatta serving as a good friend."[^4]

The Buddha then addressed the assembled four kinds of beings:

"**Devadatta, in the distant future after countless eons have passed, shall himself attain complete Buddhahood. He shall be called the Heaven-King Thus-Come-One, the Worthy One, the Perfectly Awakened One, possessed of wisdom and conduct, the Well-Gone One, the Understander of the World, the Unsurpassed One, the Controller of Beings, the Teacher of Gods and Humans, the Buddha, the World-Honored One.**

"His world-realm shall be called the Heavenly Way. At that time, the Heaven-King Buddha shall dwell in the world for twenty intermediate aeons. He shall teach the supreme Dharma extensively to all sentient beings. Through his teaching, countless beings equal to the sands of the Ganges shall attain the state of arhat, the highest fruit of the listener's path. Immeasurable beings shall awaken to the understanding of solitary enlightenment. And countless beings—equal in number to the sands of the Ganges—shall develop the aspiration for supreme enlightenment, shall attain the non-regressing patience, and shall become irreversibly established on the path to Buddhahood.[^5]

"**After the Heaven-King Buddha's final extinction, the true teaching shall endure in the world for twenty intermediate aeons. His entire body, in the form of relics, shall be enshrined in a great seven-jeweled stupa measuring sixty *yojanas* in height and forty *yojanas* in length and breadth.**

"All the celestial and human beings of that world shall pay reverence to this stupa with every kind of offering: flowers both fresh and fragrant, powdered incenses, aromatic oils, clothing, precious ornaments, banners, parasols, musical performances, and songs of praise. Through their worship and offerings to this seven-jeweled stupa, countless beings shall attain the state of arhat. Immeasurable beings shall realize the understanding of solitary enlightenment. And beyond measure, beings shall develop the aspiration for supreme enlightenment, attaining the non-regressing patience and becoming irreversibly established."[^6]

"In worlds yet to come, should any virtuous men or women hear this Devadatta chapter of the supreme Lotus Sutra, developing completely pure faith and reverence without doubt or suspicion, such beings shall not fall into the hells, shall not be reborn as hungry ghosts, shall not be born as animals. Rather, they shall be reborn in the presence of all the Buddhas in the ten directions. Wherever they are reborn, they shall constantly hear this supreme Dharma. If they are born among humans or celestial beings, they shall experience the most sublime and exquisite joys. If they are reborn in a Buddha's presence, they shall spontaneously manifest within a lotus flower, already in bloom.[^7]

---
## THE EMERGENCE OF MAÑJUŚRĪ: GATEWAY TO THE NĀGA PRINCESS
At that moment, from the lower realms below the assembly, the Buddha called Prabhūtaratna—who had been dwelling in the lower reaches of this world-system—sent forth one of his Bodhisattva attendants, named Wisdom-Accumulation, bearing a message. This Bodhisattva approached Prabhūtaratna and spoke:

"We should return to our original home realm."[^8]

But Śākyamuni Buddha addressed Wisdom-Accumulation, saying:

"Good child, wait a moment. There is here a Bodhisattva named Mañjuśrī, the Dharma-Prince. You should meet with him and engage in dialogue about the supreme Dharma. After this discussion, you may return to your home."[^9]

At that very moment, Mañjuśrī, the Bodhisattva of supreme wisdom, appeared, seated upon a thousand-petaled lotus flower as large as a great cart-wheel. Accompanying him were other Bodhisattvas, likewise seated upon precious lotus-thrones. From the depths of the vast ocean—from the palace of Sāgara, the Dragon-King—they spontaneously surged upward, remaining suspended in the empty air. They ascended toward Vulture Peak, where they descended from their lotus-thrones. Upon arriving at the Buddha's presence, all bowed with their heads to the ground, paying homage to the feet of both World-Honored Ones. Their acts of respect completed, they approached Wisdom-Accumulation and engaged in friendly discourse, then seated themselves to the side.

Wisdom-Accumulation then questioned Mañjuśrī:

"When you went to the Dragon-King's palace, how many living beings did you cause to awaken to enlightenment? Tell me the number."[^10]

Mañjuśrī replied:

"The number is immeasurable and incalculable. It exceeds what words can express and surpasses what the mind can comprehend. Wait but a moment, and you shall witness this directly yourself."[^11]

Before Mañjuśrī had even finished speaking, an immeasurable multitude of Bodhisattvas, seated upon precious lotus-thrones, surged forth from the ocean, ascending to Vulture Peak where they remained suspended in the empty sky. All of these Bodhisattvas were beings whom Mañjuśrī had caused to transform and awaken. They possessed the complete range of Bodhisattva practices. They all engaged together in discourse concerning the six transcendent perfections.[^12]

Among them were beings who had previously been listeners to the teaching—who had practiced as *śrāvakas* (those who hear the Buddha's voice). In the empty sky, they demonstrated the path of the listener. Yet now all of them are practicing the Great Vehicle understanding of emptiness. Mañjuśrī turned to Wisdom-Accumulation and proclaimed:

"This is how the awakening occurs within the ocean's depths. The work of transformation and liberation unfolds in this manner."[^13]

Wisdom-Accumulation, witnessing this extraordinary scene, expressed his admiration in verse, singing the praises of Mañjuśrī's accomplishments:

"O Mañjuśrī, possessing great wisdom, virtue, and courage!
You have awakened to enlightenment immeasurable multitudes.
We see here all these great assemblies,
And I myself have witnessed this transformation.

You illuminate the meaning of how things truly are,
You reveal and proclaim the One Buddha Vehicle,
You guide all sentient beings widely,
Leading them speedily toward supreme enlightenment."[^14]

Mañjuśrī then addressed Wisdom-Accumulation:

"In the ocean's depths, I have been continuously proclaiming this supreme Lotus Sutra. That is all I have done."[^15]

Wisdom-Accumulation then posed another question to Mañjuśrī:

"This teaching is profoundly subtle and wondrous—it is the treasure among all the sutras, a rarity in all the worlds. Tell me: are there any sentient beings who, through diligent practice and cultivation of this supreme Dharma, might swiftly attain Buddhahood?"[^16]

Mañjuśrī replied:

"There is indeed. There is the daughter of the Dragon-King Sāgara. She is only eight years old. Her wisdom is keen and her capacity to understand profound. She possesses complete knowledge of the past actions and present conditions of all sentient beings. She has attained the *dhāraṇī*—the capacity to hold all the profound secret teachings that all Buddhas have explained. She is able to retain all these teachings completely. She has entered deeply into *samādhi*—the meditative absorption of perfect clarity. She has penetrated understanding of all dharmas. In a single moment—in less time than it takes a thought to arise—she developed the aspiration for supreme enlightenment. She has attained the non-regressing patience, is irreversibly established, and possesses eloquence without obstruction. She contemplates all living beings with compassion, as a mother regards her beloved child. Her virtues are complete and perfect.[^17]

"When she speaks, her words manifest as both subtle and profound, both spacious and great. She overflows with compassion and forbearance, with gentleness and grace. She is capable of attaining enlightenment."[^18]

---
## THE CHALLENGE: ŚĀRIPUTRA'S DOUBT
Wisdom-Accumulation then expressed his hesitation:

"I have observed Śākyamuni Buddha—how for immeasurable eons he has engaged in difficult and painful practice, accumulating merit and virtue without interruption, seeking the path to enlightenment without ever ceasing. I have witnessed how, throughout the three-thousand-fold thousand-fold world-system, there is not a single place, not even the size of a mustard seed, where this Bodhisattva has not sacrificed body and life for the sake of sentient beings.**Only after such inconceivable accumulation of virtue over countless ages did he finally attain supreme, perfect enlightenment.**

"I find it difficult to believe that this young girl, within a brief moment, could suddenly achieve Buddhahood."[^19]

At that moment, before Wisdom-Accumulation had even finished speaking, the Dragon-King's daughter suddenly appeared before the assembly. She bowed with her head touching the feet of the Buddhas, then stood to the side. With great joy in her heart, she proclaimed her understanding in verse:

"I have deeply penetrated the nature of all offenses and all virtue.
I have illuminated with my light all ten directions.
My dharma-body is subtle and perfectly pure.
I possess the thirty-two marks of beauty,
Adorned with the eighty excellent characteristics.
All celestial and human beings bow before me.
All dragons and protective deities show me respect.
All classes of sentient beings venerate and honor me.
I have heard that Buddhahood is attained
Only through the Buddha's own realization.**I shall unfold the Great Vehicle teaching,
And liberate all suffering sentient beings.**"[^20]

At that very moment, the great elder Śāriputra—one of the Buddha's principal disciples—challenged the young princess:

"You say that you will swiftly attain the state of unsurpassed enlightenment, but this is difficult to believe. Why is this so? The female form is defiled and impure. It is not a proper vessel for dharma. How could you possibly attain supreme enlightenment?

"The Buddha's path is distant and difficult, requiring passage through immeasurable ages of arduous practice and virtue-accumulation before perfecting all transcendent perfections. Only then does one achieve Buddhahood.[^21]

"Moreover, the female body is subject to five great obstacles. First, a woman cannot become the ruler of Brahmā heaven. Second, she cannot become Śakra, king of the gods. Third, she cannot become a Māra-king. Fourth, she cannot become a wheel-turning monarch. And fifth, she cannot become a Buddha.[^22]

"**How could a female body swiftly achieve Buddhahood?**"[^23]

---
## THE INSTANTANEOUS DEMONSTRATION: ENLIGHTENMENT WITHOUT DELAY
The Dragon-King's daughter then possessed herself of a single precious jewel. This jewel had a value equal to the entire three-thousand-fold thousand-fold world-system.[^24] She presented this jewel as an offering to the Buddha. The Buddha immediately accepted it.[^25]

The Dragon-King's daughter then turned to Wisdom-Accumulation and Śāriputra and spoke these words:

"I have made an offering of this precious jewel to the World-Honored One, and the Buddha has accepted it. Tell me: did this occur quickly?"

"Yes," they answered, "it was accomplished with extraordinary speed."

The princess replied:

"By means of your supernatural vision, observe my attainment of Buddhahood. I shall accomplish it with even greater speed than this!"[^26]

In that very moment, before the entire assembly gathered there, the Dragon-King's daughter suddenly transformed. Her female form changed into the form of a male, possessing the complete practice of a Bodhisattva. In that instant, she journeyed toward the southern direction, toward the realm called Spotless Purity. There she seated herself upon a precious lotus-throne and achieved the state of supreme, perfect enlightenment—*anuttara-samyak-sambodhi*.[^27]

She then manifested the thirty-two marks of a Buddha and the eighty beautiful characteristics. She revealed her transformed dharma-body to all sentient beings in the ten directions, teaching the supreme Dharma universally to all beings in her assembly.[^28]

At that very moment, in the Sahā world, all the Bodhisattvas, listeners to the Buddha's voice, the eight classes of protective beings, humans, and non-humans—all perceived from a distance how the Dragon-King's daughter had attained Buddhahood and how she was teaching the Dharma universally for the benefit of all beings in her assembly. Their hearts filled with great joy, all turned their attention toward her and bowed in reverence from a great distance.[^29]

Immeasurable numbers of sentient beings heard the teaching and achieved perfect understanding. They attained the non-regressing patience, irreversibly established on the path to Buddhahood. Countless beings received a prophecy that they would attain supreme enlightenment. In the Spotless Pure realm, the earth itself shook and trembled six times with tremendous force.[^30]

In the Sahā world, three thousand living beings were established in the non-regressing stage. Three thousand sentient beings awakened the aspiration for supreme enlightenment and received the prophecy of future Buddhahood.[^31]

Wisdom-Accumulation the Bodhisattva, Śāriputra, and all the assembled multitude—all remained silent, completely accepting this demonstration.[^32]

---

**At that time, the World Honored One, wishing to express this meaning again, spoke in verse:

**DEVADATTA AND THE PATH OF ANTAGONISM****

I recall an ancient age,
A time before time began,
When seeking the Dharma true and great,
I made a solemn vow.

I was a monarch of the world,
Yet held no love for pleasures five.
I caused drums to sound forth,
Proclaiming to all directions:

"What king among the sages
Possesses the supreme Great Vehicle?
If one would teach to me
This most profound teaching,

Forever shall I bow to him,
Serving as his humble slave."
And there appeared a hermit-sage,
A mystic of great power.

"I possess," he spoke, "a Dharma
Called the Lotus Sutra wondrous-supreme.
Should you not rebel against my word,
I shall its teachings unfold."

The king, on hearing thus,
Felt overflowing joy arise.
At once he followed that hermit-sage,
Attending all his needs.

He gathered fruits and drew the water,
Collected firewood, prepared the meals.
He rendered his own body
To serve the sage as seat and rest.

Neither his body grew weary,
Nor weariness touched his mind.
For one thousand years thus serving,
He tended the sage with constant care,

All that he offered was lack—
Each need was fully met.
This he did for all beings,
Seeking the supreme and highest Dharma.

Not for his own body's sake,
Nor for the pleasures of the world,
Did this great king thus labor—
But to attain the Dharma supreme.

Through such seeking, he attained,
And in the end, the Buddha became.**Today, for your sake, I speak these teachings.**[^33]

The Buddha declared to the monks:

"The king in that age of old,
That was none other than myself.
The hermit-sage who taught him,
Is Devadatta in your time.

Because Devadatta served
As a good friend and guide to me,
I perfected the transcendent perfections six,
And every quality of Buddha-nature.

The four immeasurable states of mind,
The thirty-two marks so beautiful,
The eighty excellent characteristics,
All marks of Buddha-excellence.

The ten great powers I attained,
The four kinds of fearlessness supreme,
All methods by which I gather beings,
The eighteen qualities unique to Buddha.

All supernatural powers came to be,
And all the Buddha's transformative capacities—
All these I gained through serving
Devadatta as my teacher true.

Because this one served as guide,
I reached enlightenment complete.
The teaching spreads, all beings are uplifted,
Through Devadatta's role as good friend."[^34]**DEVADATTA'S PROPHECY**

In countless eons yet to come,
When ages unnumbered shall have passed,
Devadatta too shall attain
To perfect Buddhahood supreme.

The Buddha-name he shall receive,
Called Heaven-King Thus-Come-One,
Worthy of all offerings pure,
Perfectly awakened, complete in truth.

Possessed of wisdom, conduct perfect,
Well-gone and understander of all worlds,
Unsurpassed, the charioteer of beings,
Teacher of gods and human kinds.

In that Buddha's world-realm,
Named the Heavenly Way it shall be,
Devadatta the Buddha shall dwell,
For twenty intermediate ages.

He shall teach the Dharma supreme,
In breadth and depth complete,
And countless beings equal
To the sands of Ganges' river,

Shall attain the highest fruit,
The stage where no more learning waits.
Immeasurable beings shall awaken,
To the solitary, silent enlightenment.

And beings countless as sand-grains,
The Ganges' waters cannot number,
Shall develop the aspiration
For the supreme and highest way.

They shall attain the patience
That never turns away, never retreats.**For Devadatta, wrongdoer transformed,
Shall become a Buddha in his turn.**[^35]**THE NĀGA PRINCESS: IMPOSSIBLE ENLIGHTENMENT ACHIEVED**

There is, within the ocean's realm,
A dragon-king of mighty power.
His daughter, only eight years old,
Possesses wisdom keen and deep.

She understands the inclinations,
The past deeds of all beings living.
She has attained the *dhāraṇī*,
That comprehends what Buddhas teach.

She entered *samādhi* profound,
And penetrated all dharmas true.
In just the moment of a thought,
She raised the aspiration for enlightenment.

She never turns away from truth,
She possesses eloquence complete.
Her compassion flows for all beings,
Like a mother for her child.

The virtues of this dragon-girl,
Are perfected utterly complete.**Yet is she but eight years old,
And yet she shall become a Buddha.**[^36]**THE CHALLENGE AND THE PROOF**

The great one, Śāriputra wise,
Posed forth this challenge then:
"The Buddha, through countless eons,
Engaged in painful discipline.

He practiced what is truly hard,
Accumulated merit without end.
In all the great world-system vast,
Upon each smallest point of space,

He offered up his form and life,
For all the sentient beings' sake.
Through such incomparable effort,
Only then attained he Buddhahood.

How can this young girl, in a moment,
Achieve enlightenment supreme?
This is most difficult to believe,
Too sudden to accept as true."[^37]

But then the dragon-princess spoke,
And offered up a precious jewel.
The Buddha took it from her hands—
This treasure worth entire worlds.

"When I presented this gem,
How swift was its acceptance here?"
The elders answered: "Swift indeed,
Most swift and instantaneous."

The princess then replied to them:
"Watch now with supernatural sight,
And see me reach enlightenment,
With speed exceeding even this!

See me abandon female form,
See male Bodhisattva arise,
Watch as I travel to the south,
To realms of utmost purity.

There shall I sit on lotus throne,
And attain enlightenment complete,
With Buddha-marks and excellences,
Teaching all the Dharma pure."[^38]

All the assembly gathered there,
Perceived this demonstration strange and wondrous:
The princess became a Bodhisattva,
In that very moment transformed.

She journeyed to the southern lands,
To the realm of Spotless Pure,
And there before all beings living,
In all the ten directions wide,

She sat upon the lotus throne,
And achieved the Buddhahood supreme.
The thirty-two marks displayed,
The eighty excellent characteristics.

All beings in ten directions,
Perceived her Buddhahood manifest.
They heard her teaching spread,
The Dharma flowing without limit.

Each being felt great joy arise,
And bowed to her from distant lands.
Countless beings heard the truth,
And understanding came to be.

Many reached the non-regressing state,
The point where turning back is not.
Many received the prophecy,
Of Buddha-attainment yet to come.

The realm where she had taken seat,
The earth itself shook six times through.
And in the Sahā world of ours,
Three thousand sentient beings here,

Attained the non-regressing stage,
No longer subject unto turning-back.
And three thousand beings more,
Awakened the enlightenment-aspiration,

And all received the prophecy,
Of Buddhahood in times to come.**Thus does the Lotus Sutra prove,
That any being—none excepted—

Can reach the Buddha's state supreme,
Through the teaching of this way.**[^39]

---

# Chapter 13: Exhortation to Uphold

## THE BODHISATTVAS' VOWS: ACCEPTING THE TRANSMISSION
At that moment, the Bodhisattva Mahāsattva named Medicinal-King—a Great Being of extraordinary compassion—and the Bodhisattva Mahāsattva named Great-Joy-in-Speaking—possessing the voice of great proclamation—together with twenty thousand Bodhisattvas and their retinues, all stood before the Buddha and spoke this pledge:

"World Honored One, we implore you: do not concern yourself with anxiety or doubt. After your extinction, when you have entered into final *parinirvāṇa*, we shall uphold, read, recite, and explain this supreme Dharma-teaching. We shall preserve it, we shall practice it, we shall make offerings to it.

"In the future ages, in the times that are to come, sentient beings in the worlds that follow your passing will have become fewer in wholesome roots and deeper in unwholesome tendencies. Pride and conceit will multiply. They will cling to profit and honor, hungry for recognition and worship. They will increase in destructive, unhealthy dispositions, and they will drift far from liberation and awakening.

"**Though these beings are difficult to teach and transform, we shall arise with great patient endurance. We shall read this Dharma, we shall recite it, we shall explain it and teach it. We shall write it down and preserve it in written form. We shall make every kind of offering to it. We shall not spare our bodies and lives in this sacred work.**"[^1]

At that very moment, five hundred arhats who had received the prophecy of future Buddhahood stood before the Buddha and proclaimed:

"World Honored One, after your extinction, we also vow freely and openly that we shall travel to different lands and teach this supreme Dharma extensively throughout many realms."[^2]

Then eight thousand men and women practitioners—both monks and lay followers who had received the prophecy of Buddhahood—rose from their seats, bowed with hands joined in reverence before the Buddha, and made this vow:

"World Honored One, we too vow freely to teach this supreme Dharma in lands different from our own, spreading it extensively through many realms. Why do we make this pledge? It is because in this Sahā world-realm, the beings are of base character, prone to corruption and destructive conduct. They are filled with prideful arrogance and conceit. Their wholesome roots are shallow and sparse. They are filled with anger, hatred, and filthy, twisted thoughts. Their minds are not straightforward and authentic in seeking the truth.[^3]

"For this reason, we shall undertake the burden of spreading this teaching throughout the worlds to come."[^4]

---
## THE BUDDHA'S AUNT AND THE WOMEN DISCIPLES
At that time, the Buddha's aunt, the Bhikṣuṇī Mahāprajāpatī—the great grandmother-mother of all Buddhist nuns—along with six thousand nuns, both learners and established adepts, rose from their seats. In perfect unison, they joined their hands in deep reverence, their eyes fixed constantly upon the Buddha's face without ever turning away. At that moment, the World Honored One turned his attention to the nun Gautamī and spoke:

"Why do you gaze upon me with such an expression of concern? Is your heart troubled, wondering perhaps whether I have not proclaimed your name among those receiving the prophecy of Buddhahood?"[^5]

The Buddha then addressed the assembled nuns:

"Gautamī, I have already proclaimed universally that all sentient beings endowed with Buddha-nature shall receive the prophecy of Buddhahood. When you now seek to know what future awaits you, you shall learn this: In the worlds yet to come, in ages beyond counting,**you shall become a Great Teacher of the Dharma before six hundred and eighty billion Buddhas.** Along with your six thousand nun-disciples, all of you together shall serve as Great Teachers of the Dharma.

"By gradually accumulating the Bodhisattva path in this manner, you shall perfect all qualities and become yourself a Buddha. Your Buddha-name shall be**'She Who Brings Joy to All Living Beings Thus-Come-One'**—the Worthy One, the Perfectly Awakened One, possessed of wisdom and conduct, the Well-Gone One, the Understander of the World, the Unsurpassed One, the Controller of Beings, the Teacher of Gods and Humans, the Buddha, the World-Honored One.

"Gautamī, these six thousand nuns together with you shall all progressively receive the prophecy of Buddhahood, achieving supreme enlightenment."[^6]

At that moment, the Bhikṣuṇī Rāhula's mother, the woman named Yaśodharā, had a troubling thought. She reflected: "Among all these prophecies and declarations of future Buddhahood, how is it that the World Honored One has not proclaimed my name?"[^7]

The Buddha then addressed Yaśodharā directly:

"In the worlds yet to come, in ages beyond all count, you shall cultivate the Bodhisattva path before countless Buddhas—before hundreds, thousands, millions, and billions of them. You shall become a Great Teacher of the Dharma, gradually perfecting the complete Bodhisattva way. In a good and wholesome world-realm, you shall attain Buddhahood yourself. Your Buddha-name shall be**'Possessing a Hundred Thousand Ten-Million Radiant Marks Thus-Come-One'**—the Worthy One, the Perfectly Awakened One, possessed of wisdom and conduct, the Well-Gone One, the Understander of the World, the Unsurpassed One, the Controller of Beings, the Teacher of Gods and Humans, the Buddha, the World-Honored One. The lifespan of that Buddha shall extend through numberless immeasurable eons."[^8]

At that time, both Bhikṣuṇī Mahāprajāpatī and the woman Yaśodharā—together with all their disciples—experienced great joy. They had encountered what they had never encountered before. Immediately, they expressed their happiness in verse, proclaiming before the Buddha:

"World Honored One, our Guide and Teacher,
You who bring peace and security to gods and humans,
We have heard the declaration of our future Buddhahood,
And our hearts are now complete and fully satisfied.

The names we shall bear in ages yet to come—
We shall become Buddhas, and at that time,
All the highest heavens and the human realms shall hear our teaching.
We shall protect and nurture all who come to us with trust."[^9]

After the nuns spoke these verses, they addressed the Buddha:

"World Honored One, we too are able to teach and proclaim this supreme Dharma extensively in other lands and in worlds yet to come."[^10]

---
## THE BODHISATTVAS' GREAT VOWS
At that moment, the World Honored One gazed out at eighty million billions of countless Bodhisattva Mahāsattvas. These Bodhisattvas were all of them Avaivartikas—those who have attained the irreversible stage, those who turn the wheel of irreversible dharma, those who have obtained all the *dhāraṇī*s, the capacities to remember and manifest all teachings without obstruction.[^11]

These Bodhisattvas rose from their seats and approached the Buddha. With a single unified intention, they joined their palms together in reverence. In their minds, they generated this thought:**"If the World Honored One commands us to uphold and teach this supreme Dharma, we shall follow the Buddha's instruction, spreading this teaching far and wide throughout all the realms."**

Yet another thought arose within them:**"But the Buddha now stands in silence, offering no explicit command. What then is his intention? How shall we respond?"**[^12]

At that moment, these Bodhisattvas, respecting the Buddha's will and wishing to fulfill their own original vows, stood before the Buddha and roared forth their lion-vow. With a great roar of determination, they proclaimed their pledge:

"World Honored One, we do not require your command. After your extinction, we shall journey throughout the ten directions, moving back and forth in all worlds. We shall enable sentient beings to write down this supreme Dharma, to receive it, to read it, to recite it, to understand its meanings, and to practice it according to the teachings. They shall abide in right understanding and mindfulness—and all of this shall be accomplished through the power and grace of the Buddha.

"We humbly beseech the World Honored One: watch over us from other worlds, protecting us from afar through your supernatural vision and wisdom-power."[^13]

At that very moment, all the Bodhisattvas together proclaimed their determination in verse:

"Do not harbor concern or anxiety,
After the Buddha's passage into *parinirvāṇa*,
In this dark and dangerous age to come,
We shall teach this Dharma widely.

There will be those of no wisdom,
Who hurl angry words of curse and blame,
And those who come with violent weapons,
Against whom we shall exercise patience.

In the evil times ahead, there will be monks,
Possessed of twisted, perverted minds,
Who say they have attained what they have not,
Whose hearts are swollen with arrogant pride.

Or some who retreat into hermitages,
Wearing patched and ragged robes,
Who claim to practice the true path,
Looking down upon those dwelling in the world.

Driven by love of profit and gain,
They teach the Dharma to those of worldly power,
And are revered by the world like *arhats* of six powers,
Yet they harbor evil intentions.

They constantly contemplate worldly affairs,
These so-called forest dwellers of hollow name,
And they take delight in revealing our faults,
Speaking thus of us before the multitudes:

'These monks practice for profit and gain!
Their teachings are not from the Buddha,
They have invented this Sutra themselves,
To mislead and deceive the world!

They seek fame and reputation thereby,
These monks of twisted intentions.'
Making such accusations against us,
They separate themselves from the assembly.

In this evil age ahead, such are the accusations.
Yet we shall endure all such hostility,
For we deeply respect the Buddha's will,
And shall withstand whatever hardships come.

We shall wear the armor of patient endurance,
And bear witness to this Dharma,
Through all the suffering and danger,
Across this difficult and defiled age.

We do not love our bodies or our lives,
But treasure infinitely the supreme path.
In the ages yet to come, we shall
Guard what the Buddha has entrusted to us.

We are the messengers of the World Honored One,
Working in the midst of multitudes without fear.
We shall teach the Dharma with skillful means,
And pray that the Buddha find peace and rest.

Before the World Honored One,
Before all Buddhas coming from ten directions,
We make this solemn vow here,
For the Buddha's own understanding alone.

All the Bodhisattvas throughout the cosmos,
Know the sincerity of our hearts today.
We shall protect what the Buddha has entrusted—
The Buddha himself already understands our minds."[^14]

*[End of Fascicle 5 (卷五)]*

---

# Chapter 14: The Bodhisattva's Peaceful Ways of Practice

## THE FOUR CONDITIONS FOR SAFE DHARMA-TEACHING
At that time, Mañjuśrī, the Bodhisattva of supreme wisdom and the Dharma-Prince, addressed the Buddha:

"World Honored One, these Bodhisattvas are indeed most extraordinary, rarely encountered. They possess great respect for the Buddha and profound commitment. They generate great vows for the future. In those evil ages to come, they wish to teach and proclaim this supreme Lotus Sutra.

"World Honored One, how shall these Bodhisattva Mahāsattvas, in those evil ages yet to come, be enabled to teach this supreme Sutra? How shall they do so with confidence and without timidity?"[^1]

The Buddha replied to Mañjuśrī:

"If any Bodhisattva Mahāsattva desires to teach this supreme Lotus Sutra in the evil ages yet to come, they must dwell firmly established in four essential practices. What are these four?**First: Establishing oneself in the Bodhisattva's dwelling-place and associations.**

Mañjuśrī, if a Bodhisattva Mahāsattva wishes to teach this supreme Sutra in the evil ages, they must establish themselves upon the ground of patience, becoming gentle, yielding, and harmonious. Their heart shall not be suddenly startled or disturbed by difficulties. Moreover, regarding all teachings, they shall not practice attachment or discrimination. Rather, they shall perceive all dharmas as they truly are—not inverted, not unstable, not regressing, not transforming—remaining like empty space, possessing nothing whatsoever.[^2]

"Mañjuśrī, what is meant by 'the Bodhisattva's association' or proper companions? It means the Bodhisattva shall not associate closely with kings, princes, ministers, or officials. They shall not keep company with those who practice false teachings, heretics, or various ascetics. They shall not spend time with those who create worldly compositions glorifying other texts. They shall not befriend those who practice destructive amusements or wrestling matches and various entertainments.[^3]

"Furthermore, they shall not associate with those of base caste—hunters, butchers, those engaged in harmful livelihoods—nor shall they maintain close relationships with such people. If any such people come to them, they shall teach the Dharma without expectation of gain.

"They shall not associate with monks or nuns who seek the listener's path, nor with lay practitioners. They shall not dwell together in the same place, nor speak together often. If any such people come to them, they shall teach the Dharma as circumstances require, without seeking anything in return.[^4]

"Mañjuśrī, regarding women: the Bodhisattva shall not look upon women's bodies as objects of desire when teaching them the Dharma. They shall not delight in viewing women's forms. When entering a household, the Bodhisattva shall not speak with young girls, unmarried women, or widows. They shall not become intimate with the five kinds of gender-ambiguous persons. They shall not enter another's household alone. If there is some pressing reason to enter a house alone, the Bodhisattva shall focus the mind entirely upon the Buddha.[^5]

"When teaching the Dharma to women, the Bodhisattva shall not display their teeth in smiling, shall not expose their chest or inner garments. Even for the sake of the Dharma, they shall not become intimate with women—how much less so for other matters. The Bodhisattva shall not delight in keeping young disciples, novice monks, or children as attendants, nor shall they wish to study together with fellow disciples under the same master.

"The Bodhisattva shall constantly delight in sitting in meditation, remaining in quiet, secluded places, gathering and controlling their mind. Mañjuśrī, these practices constitute what is called the Bodhisattva's associations.[^6]**Second: The Bodhisattva's intellectual and spiritual cultivation.**

"Moreover, Mañjuśrī, the Bodhisattva Mahāsattva should observe all dharmas as empty. They should perceive their true nature—not inverted, not moving, not regressing, not transforming—as entirely resembling empty space, possessing no nature whatsoever.

"All verbal and conceptual elaborations shall cease. They shall not be born, shall not emerge, shall not arise. They shall possess no name, no characteristic. In truth, they possess nothing whatsoever. They are immeasurable, boundless, without obstacle or impediment. They exist only through causes and conditions; they arise from inverted thinking; therefore, they are taught.[^7]

"The Bodhisattva shall always delight in observing dharmas in this manner—this is called the Bodhisattva Mahāsattva's second form of dwelling, the second place of proper association.**Third: The peaceful way of proclaiming the Dharma.**

"Mañjuśrī, after my extinction, in the final age of the Dharma, those who wish to teach this supreme Sutra must practice the peaceful way of expression. When speaking or reading the Sutra, they shall not delight in discussing others' faults or the Sutra's faults. They shall not look down upon other dharma-teachers with contempt. They shall not speak of others' strengths and weaknesses, their merits and defects.[^8]

"Regarding listeners of the Buddha's voice: they shall not speak their names when discussing their faults. They shall not speak their names when praising their virtues. Neither shall they harbor resentment or hostility toward any being. Because they have cultivated this peaceful mind, all those who listen to them shall not oppose their intention.[^9]

"When some listener poses a difficult question, the Bodhisattva shall not answer with the listener's limited understanding. Rather, they shall answer only through the perspective of the Great Vehicle, enabling all listeners to awaken the aspiration for supreme enlightenment and eventually attain all-knowing wisdom.[^10]

"The Bodhisattva shall not be lazy or slack. They shall not harbor worries or disturbances. They shall teach the Dharma with a compassionate heart. Day and night, they shall constantly proclaim the supreme teaching of the Buddha. Through various causes and conditions, through numberless parables and illustrations, they shall illuminate the teachings so that all sentient beings rejoice.[^11]

"The Bodhisattva's garments, bedding, food, and medicines—regarding all these material supports, they shall harbor no hope of gain. They shall focus only upon the intention to teach the Dharma. They shall desire to attain the Buddha-way and to enable all sentient beings to accomplish the same. This is called the supreme and peaceful offering.[^12]

"In the Buddha's final age, when any monk or nun is able to proclaim this supreme Lotus Sutra—if their heart is free from jealousy, hatred, resentment, and all mental obstacles, free from worry and sorrow, free from being cursed or condemned, and free from the threat of violence or weapons—such a person shall dwell in the peaceful way as I have described.[^13]

"By cultivating such peaceful practice, the teacher shall encounter no one who creates disturbances. They shall find good fellow-practitioners with whom to study this Sutra together. They shall obtain a great assembly who come to listen. Those who listen shall be able to retain the teaching, able to recite it, able to explain it, able to proclaim it, able to write it down. If they cause others to write it, they shall respect and honor the written text, shall praise and glorify it.**Fourth: The cultivation of compassion and proper regard.**

"Furthermore, Mañjuśrī, the Bodhisattva Mahāsattva in the Buddha's final age, when the Dharma is about to perish, whoever preserves this Lotus Sutra shall generate great compassion toward all sentient beings, whether lay or ordained. They shall generate great compassion toward those who are not Bodhisattvas. They should reflect thus: 'This is what such beings lack. The Tathāgata has taught the teachings through skillful methods adapted to conditions, yet these beings do not hear, do not understand, do not awaken, and do not seek to understand this Sutra. Their loss is great.[^14]

"'Although these beings have not questioned the teachings, have not sought faith, have not sought understanding, when I attain supreme enlightenment, I shall, through supernatural power and wisdom-power, draw all such beings and enable them to dwell in this Dharma.'

"Mañjuśrī, the Bodhisattva Mahāsattva should generate this kind of compassionate reflection toward all sentient beings. The Bodhisattva should regard all Buddhas with the attitude of a most devoted child toward a father. The Bodhisattva should regard all Bodhisattvas with the attitude of a most devoted student toward a great teacher. The Bodhisattva should regard all sentient beings with universal equanimous compassion.[^15]

"When maintaining and reading this Sutra, they shall practice the way of peaceful, pleasurable proclamation. What does this mean? It means: cultivating a quality of gentleness in one's manner. Preparing a pure place for teaching. Providing a cushioned seat. Bathing the body and dressing in clean clothes. When any listener comes—whether monks, nuns, male lay practitioners, female lay practitioners, kings, princes, citizens, or brahmins—the Bodhisattva shall teach with subtle profundity and a gentle expression.[^16]

"If a listener poses a difficult question, the Bodhisattva shall respond according to the meaning, employing causes and conditions, parables and illustrations, in detailed explanation, enabling all who listen to awaken the aspiration for enlightenment and gradually enter the Buddha-way. This person's virtue and merit, across countless eons, cannot be fully calculated or described.[^17]

"In the Buddha's final age, if a monk or nun is capable of proclaiming this supreme Lotus Sutra—if their mind is free of jealousy, hatred, and all obstacles, if they are without worry or sorrow, if they endure mockery and rejection, maintaining patience—such a person has already established themselves in the peaceful way as I have described. Such a being's merit and virtue, throughout countless and immeasurable eons, cannot be exhausted through enumeration or comparison.[^18]

"It is as when a king of great power, desiring to subdue all other kingdoms, gathers all his generals and troops, and when he perceives among the warriors some of great courage and strength who have achieved significant victories, he becomes filled with great delight. To these victorious ones, he grants whatever they desire: lands, cities, villages, or precious garments, jewels, gold, silver, coral, pearls, precious stones, and all kinds of treasures. Yet there is one thing: the luminous pearl worn in the crown upon the king's head—this single pearl he has never given to anyone.[^19]

"Why is this? Because the king alone possesses this one pearl. There is no second pearl like it. If he were to give it to his soldiers and attendants, all his queens and concubines would be astonished and disturbed.

"The Tathāgata is exactly like this. The Tathāgata, through meditation-power and wisdom-power, has obtained the dharma-realm and rules over the three worlds, conquering all māras and demons. The Tathāgata's worthy disciples and noble saints have battled against the five-aggregates-demon, the defilements-demon, and the death-demon, achieving great victories and destroying the three poisons, escaping the three worlds, breaking the nets of māra.[^20]

"The Tathāgata, seeing such victorious warriors, becomes greatly delighted. The Tathāgata, among the multitude of listeners, teaches various dharmas, grants them meditation-attainment, liberation, and the supernatural powers of the undefiled path. The Tathāgata grants them the meditation-palaces and the cities of *parinirvāṇa*, speaking to them of the attainment of extinction, causing all to rejoice.

"Yet the Tathāgata does not teach this Lotus Sutra. Why not?**This Lotus Sutra is the highest among all teachings that the Tathāgata has proclaimed throughout the three times—past, present, and future.**[^21]

"The Sutra possesses the capacity to bring all sentient beings to the state of all-knowing wisdom. The realm where the Sutra is taught is one of many enemies and difficulty—a world where beings harbor great suspicion and distrust. Yet now, the Tathāgata, beholding the great deeds of these Bodhisattva-warriors who have vowed to uphold and teach this Sutra in such hostile times, becomes greatly delighted.

"This supreme Lotus Sutra—which can enable sentient beings to attain all-knowing wisdom, which all the Buddhas throughout the three times have proclaimed—is now given to these Bodhisattvas. It is like the king who finally grants the crown jewel to those who have achieved supreme victory.[^22]

"Therefore, Mañjuśrī, those Bodhisattvas who uphold this Sutra are the Tathāgata's most precious treasure. Know them to be the Buddha's children. Know them to be the most honored among all beings.

"How much more so: those Bodhisattvas who can read, recite, remember, understand, teach, and proclaim this Sutra—such beings, enduring abuse and rejection, maintaining patient forbearance—such beings are establishing themselves in the peaceful way of practice as I have described."[^23]

---

**At that time, the World Honored One, wishing to elaborate further upon this teaching, spoke in verse:

**THE FOUR PEACEFUL PRACTICES****

If one desires to teach this supreme Dharma,
In the evil age yet to come,
One must dwell with no fearful heart,
And wish to proclaim this teaching.

To enter the Bodhisattva's dwelling place
And proper associations pure,
One must always remain in patience,
Gentle, harmonious, without sudden disturbance.

# Chapter 15: The Emergence of Bodhisattvas from the Earth

## THE COSMIC DISCLOSURE: INFINITE DISCIPLES APPEAR
At that moment, the Bodhisattva Mahāsattvas from countless worlds beyond—more numerous than the sands of eight Ganges Rivers—rose from their seats. With joined palms in reverence, they addressed the Buddha:

"World Honored One, if you would grant us permission, after your extinction we shall remain in this Sahā world-realm. We shall diligently apply ourselves with great care and effort. We shall uphold, read, recite, write, and make offerings to this supreme Sutra. We shall proclaim it extensively throughout this realm."[^1]

At that moment, the World Honored One addressed all the assembled Bodhisattva Mahāsattvas:

"Stop, good children. There is no need for you to protect and preserve this teaching. Why is this so?**In my Sahā world-realm, there are already six hundred thousand Ganges' worth of Bodhisattva Mahāsattvas.** Each of these Bodhisattvas possesses six hundred thousand Ganges' worth of attendants and retinues.[^2]

"All of these beings shall be able, after my extinction, to protect, read, recite, and extensively teach this supreme Sutra."[^3]

---
## THE EARTH RESPONDS: THE COSMIC ASSEMBLY EMERGES
At the moment the Buddha spoke these words,**the entire three-thousand-fold thousand-fold world-system trembled and split open.** From within the fissures, there emerged without number countless millions upon millions of Bodhisattva Mahāsattvas—**an utterly immeasurable multitude, all rising forth simultaneously from beneath this very Sahā world-realm.**

All of these Bodhisattvas manifested bodies of golden radiance. Each possessed the thirty-two marks of a Buddha. Each was surrounded by measureless light. They had been dwelling in the empty space beneath this Sahā world-realm, and from their dwelling-places they rose upward.[^4]

These Bodhisattvas, hearing the voice of Śākyamuni Buddha speaking from above, emerged from below. Each of these Bodhisattvas served as a leader and guide directing multitudes. Each brought with them six hundred thousand Ganges' worth of attendants. And yet even those bringing "only" five hundred thousand Ganges of retinues, or four hundred thousand, three hundred thousand, two hundred thousand, or one hundred thousand Ganges' worth—those bringing fifty thousand, ten thousand, one thousand, one hundred, fifty, thirty, twenty, ten, five, four, three, two, or even just a single disciple—and those coming entirely alone, who delighted in solitary practice—**all such beings without number, beyond the power of calculation to encompass, came forth.[^5]

These Bodhisattvas, having emerged from the earth, proceeded to the empty space where the seven-jeweled stupa containing Prabhūtaratna Buddha and Śākyamuni Buddha sat suspended. Upon arriving, they bowed with their heads to the ground before both World-Honored Ones. They also made reverent obeisance to all the Buddhas seated beneath the precious trees upon their lion-thrones in all eight directions. Three times they circumambulated these Buddhas, with joined palms in reverent respect.

They praised the Buddhas using all manner of Bodhisattva-glorification, expressing their profound reverence. Then they stood to one side, their hearts delighting in gazing upon the two World-Honored Ones.**These Bodhisattvas Mahāsattvas, from the moment they emerged, praised the Buddha using all manner of Bodhisattva-glorification. This continued for fifty minor eons. During this entire time, Śākyamuni Buddha sat in silence, and all the assembled four kinds of beings also remained in silence for fifty minor eons.** Yet through the Buddha's supernatural power, all the great assembly perceived the passage of time as only half a day. The four kinds of beings, through the Buddha's supernatural power, perceived these Bodhisattvas filling without limit hundreds of thousands of millions of worlds throughout the three-thousand-fold thousand-fold world-system, suspended in the empty space.[^6]

---
## THE FOUR LEADER BODHISATTVAS: INQUIRY AND RECOGNITION
Among this Bodhisattva multitude, there were four foremost guide-leaders:

**Anantaviśiṣṭa** (Boundless Superior Conduct / *Wubian xing* )

**Sthiraviśiṣṭa** (Stable Conduct / *Anliixing* )[^8]

These four Bodhisattvas were the most foremost leaders and guides within the assembled multitude. Standing before the great assembly, they joined their palms together and gazed upon Śākyamuni Buddha, respectfully inquiring:

"World Honored One, are you in health and ease? Do you experience few ailments and minor troubles? Are the sentient beings whom you have undertaken to teach receptive to instruction? Do our efforts to teach bring you no weariness or fatigue?"[^9]

At that moment, the four great Bodhisattvas expressed their inquiry in verse:

"The World Honored One abides in peace and ease,
Experiencing few ailments and minor troubles.
The sentient beings whom you teach find transformation easy,
And your sacred effort brings no weariness or exhaustion to you."[^10]

---
## THE BUDDHA'S REVELATION: THE ANCIENT DISCIPLES
At that moment, Śākyamuni Buddha addressed the assembled Bodhisattva multitude:

"**Yes, precisely so. Yes, precisely so, good children. The Tathāgata is at ease, with few ailments and minor troubles. All sentient beings are easy to transform and teach, and there is no weariness in my work.**

"Why is this so?**It is because all these sentient beings, throughout innumerable eons, have constantly received my teaching.** They have also shown respect and reverence to the Buddhas of past ages, and they have planted countless good roots. These sentient beings, upon seeing my form and hearing the teachings I proclaim, immediately receive them with faith and enter into the wisdom of the Tathāgata.[^11]

"Except for those who previously studied and practiced the limited teachings of the small vehicle—**even these beings I now enable to hear this supreme Sutra and to enter into the Buddha-wisdom.**"[^12]

At that moment, all the great Bodhisattvas expressed their gratitude in verse:

"Excellent, excellent, great mighty World Honored One!
The sentient beings are easy to transform and teach.
They can question the Buddha regarding the deepest wisdom,
And having heard, they trust and practice accordingly.
We rejoice in all of this."[^13]

At that time, Śākyamuni Buddha praised the foremost Bodhisattvas:

"Excellent, excellent, good children. You are all capable of generating hearts of rejoicing regarding the Tathāgata's teaching."[^14]

---
## THE ASSEMBLY'S PERPLEXITY: WHERE DID THESE COME FROM?
At that moment, the Bodhisattva Maitreya and eight thousand Ganges' worth of Bodhisattva-multitudes all generated the same profound thought in their minds:

"We have never seen, never heard, during all the time we have traveled throughout worlds and realms, of such a vast assembly of great Bodhisattva Mahāsattvas emerging from the earth, standing before the World Honored One with joined palms, making offerings and respectful inquiry."[^15]

At that time, the Bodhisattva Mahāsattva Maitreya, understanding the thoughts that all eight thousand Ganges' worth of Bodhisattvas were contemplating, and wishing to resolve his own doubt, joined his palms together before the Buddha. Using verse, he questioned:

"Innumerable hundreds of thousands of millions,
Vast assembly of these great Bodhisattvas—
Beings we have never seen before in any age,
We pray, O One with Two Feet Most Honored, that you explain:

From where have these beings come?
Through what causes and conditions did they gather?
Their bodies possess immense majesty,
Their supernatural powers are inconceivable,
Their aspirations are firmly established,
Possessed of great patience and forbearance,
Pleasing to perceive by all sentient beings—
Tell us from where they originally came.

Each of these Bodhisattvas
Brings countless retinue-companions,
Numbers immeasurable as the Ganges' sands,
Some bringing six hundred thousand Ganges-multitudes.

Some great Bodhisattvas bring five hundred thousand,
Four hundred thousand, three hundred thousand, two hundred thousand,
One hundred thousand, ten thousand, one thousand,
One hundred, fifty, ten—

Even down to those bringing a single disciple,
And those who come alone, delighting in solitude—
Such numbers if one were to attempt to count,
Using even the measure of a Ganges-measuring rod,
Through immeasurable eons of counting,
Could never be exhausted or determined.

These Bodhisattvas of great spiritual power,
With intense vigor and concentrated aspiration—
Whose teaching have they received?
Who has educated and established them?
Whose Dharma have they accepted?
Whose Buddhist path do they cultivate?

These great Bodhisattvas,
With supernatural powers and wisdom inconceivable—
The four directions of the earth have opened,
And all have emerged forth from within.

World Honored One, in all the time I have journeyed,
I have never witnessed such an occurrence.
We pray that you reveal their origin,
And tell us the names of the lands they come from.

I have always traveled through many realms,
Yet I have never encountered this assembly.
Among all these Bodhisattvas here present,
There is not a single one I recognize.

They emerge suddenly from the earth—
We pray that you explain the cause and reason.
This great assembly gathered here
Is immeasurable, numbering hundreds and thousands of millions.

All these Bodhisattva-beings wish to know
The beginning and end of their story, their causes and conditions.
O World Honored One of immeasurable virtue,
We pray that you resolve this doubt for us all."[^16]

---
## THE BUDDHA'S IMPLICIT ANSWER: "These are my disciples whom I have taught"
At that moment, all the division-bodies of Śākyamuni Buddha—all those who sat beneath the precious trees on lion-thrones in the eight cardinal directions throughout countless Buddha-lands—heard the Buddha's voice declaring how this vast multitude had emerged.[^17]

The attendants of each of these Buddhas perceived this immense assembly of Bodhisattvas filling the three-thousand-fold thousand-fold world-system, emerging from the earth and suspending themselves in the empty space. The attendants of each Buddha asked their respective Buddha-lord:

"World Honored One, from where have come all these immeasurable, incalculable multitudes of great Bodhisattvas?"[^18]

At that moment, each Buddha instructed their attendants:

"Good children, wait but a moment. There is a great Bodhisattva Mahāsattva named Maitreya, who has received a prophecy from Śākyamuni Buddha that he shall become a Buddha in the next age. He has already posed this very question to the Buddha. The Buddha shall now answer it, and you shall hear the response through his words."[^19]

---
## THE BUDDHA ADDRESSES MAITREYA: REVEALING THE DISCIPLES
At that moment, Śākyamuni Buddha addressed Maitreya Bodhisattva, saying:

"Excellent, excellent, Ajita (O Maitreya)! You have posed to the Buddha a matter of great significance. All of you gathered here should now unite in a single-pointed mind. Put on the armor of diligent effort. Establish a firm and unshakable resolve.[^20]

"**The Tathāgata now wishes to reveal and proclaim the wisdom of all Buddhas, the absolute freedom and supernatural powers of all Buddhas, the lion's roar-power of all Buddhas, and the fierce and mighty dignity of all Buddhas.**"[^21]

At that moment, the World Honored One, wishing to elaborate further upon this teaching, spoke in verse:

"Gather all your strength and concentrate your minds,
I wish to tell you something of ultimate significance.
Do not allow any doubt or regret to arise—
The Buddha's wisdom is beyond all conceptualization.

You should manifest the power of faith,
Dwell in patience and the wholesome state.
What you have never heard before,
You shall now hear completely.

I now reassure and encourage you:
Do not harbor doubt or fear.
The Buddha speaks only what is true,
And Buddha-wisdom is immeasurable.

The supreme Dharma that was attained
Is most subtle and beyond discrimination.
This is what I shall now teach—
Listen together with undivided attention."[^22]

At the moment the Buddha completed this verse, he addressed Maitreya Bodhisattva, saying:

"I now proclaim to all of you here, O Ajita (Maitreya).**These great Bodhisattva Mahāsattvas—immeasurable, incalculable, inconceivable multitudes whom you have never previously seen—these are all Bodhisattvas whom I have educated and transformed, to whom I have taught the Dharma after I attained supreme, perfect enlightenment in this Sahā world-realm.**

"I have guided and trained their minds, causing them to generate the determination to pursue the path to enlightenment.**All these Bodhisattvas dwell beneath the surface of this Sahā world-realm, in the empty space within the earth itself.** They thoroughly master the meaning of all sutras, they contemplate and discriminate the teachings, and they maintain correct mindfulness.[^23]

"O Ajita, these good children do not delight in dwelling in crowds, they do not enjoy engaging in excessive speaking. They constantly delight in quiet, solitary places, they apply themselves with vigorous diligence, and they never pause in their endeavor. They do not rely upon or dwell attached to heavenly beings or humans. They constantly delight in profound wisdom, which encounters no obstacles. They also constantly delight in the teachings of all Buddhas, they apply themselves with undivided focus, and they seek the supreme, unsurpassed wisdom."[^24]

At that moment, Śākyamuni Buddha, wishing to express this teaching in verse form, spoke:

"O Ajita, understand this clearly:
These are the great Bodhisattvas
Who have cultivated Buddha-wisdom
Throughout innumerable eons.

All of them are those whom I have transformed,
To whom I have taught the aspiration for supreme enlightenment.
These are my children,
Dwelling and relying upon this world.

They constantly engage in ascetic practice,
Delighting in quiet, solitary places,
Abandoning the tumultuous crowds,
Not desiring to speak excessively.

Like students of my Dharma-teaching,
These children practice and study my path,
Day and night maintaining vigorous effort,
Seeking the path to supreme enlightenment.

In the empty space beneath the Sahā world,
They dwell and remain established,
Their resolve firm and their determination unshakable,
Ever diligently seeking wisdom.

Teaching the Dharma with infinite subtlety,
Their hearts harboring no fear.

At Gayā's holy site,
Beneath the Bodhi tree,
I attained the most perfect enlightenment,
And turned the wheel of supreme Dharma.

It was then that I taught them,
Inspiring them to generate the determination for enlightenment.
Now all of them dwell in the stage of non-regression,
And they shall all attain Buddhahood.

I now speak what is true:
You should all have faith and believe.
I have cultivated and taught these beings
For very long ages indeed."[^25]

---

# Chapter 16: The Tathāgata's Eternal Lifespan

## THE TRIPLE REQUEST: PREPARING FOR REVELATION
At that moment, the Buddha addressed all the Bodhisattvas and the entire great assembly:

"Good children, you must now have complete faith in the Tathāgata's truthful words."

A second time, he addressed the great assembly:

"Good children, you must now have complete faith in the Tathāgata's truthful words."

A third time, he addressed the great assembly:

"Good children, you must now have complete faith in the Tathāgata's truthful words."[^1]

At that moment, the assembled Bodhisattva multitudes, with Maitreya at the fore, joined their palms before the Buddha and spoke:

"World Honored One, we only pray that you will teach us. We shall place complete faith in the Buddha's words."

They made this request once. Again they spoke:

"World Honored One, we only pray that you will teach us. We shall place complete faith in the Buddha's words."[^2]

---
## THE REVELATION: THE BUDDHA'S INCONCEIVABLE LIFESPAN
At that moment, the World Honored One, knowing that the Bodhisattvas had made three requests without ceasing, addressed them, saying:

"Listen carefully to what I shall now reveal to you:**the Tathāgata's secret and supernatural power.** All the beings in the worlds—celestial and human, as well as asuras—believe and imagine that the present Śākyamuni Buddha left the Śākya palace, departed from the Śākya clan, traveled not far from the city of Gayā, sat upon the enlightenment seat, and there attained supreme, perfect enlightenment.[^3]

"**But hear this truth, good children: I have in reality been a Buddha for an immeasurable, incalculable number of eons—far beyond what could be expressed as hundred, thousand, ten-thousand, million, billion *asamkhyeya* eons of time.**[^4]

---
## THE MATHEMATICAL PARABLE: WORLDS AS DUST PARTICLES
"Let me give you an illustration, good children. Suppose there existed five hundred thousand million billion *asamkhyeya* three-thousand-fold thousand-fold world-systems. Further suppose someone were to grind all these worlds into fine dust-particles. And suppose this person were to journey eastward, dropping one particle of dust as they passed through five hundred thousand million billion *asamkhyeya* worlds, continuing eastward until they had exhausted all the dust.

"What do you think, good children? Would it be possible to calculate, to measure, to determine the number of all these worlds?"[^5]

Maitreya Bodhisattva and all the assembled Bodhisattvas spoke to the Buddha in unison:

"World Honored One, these worlds are immeasurable, incalculable, limitless. They exceed what can be computed through numbers, exceed what the mind can grasp. Even the śrāvakas and pratyekabuddhas, employing undefiled wisdom, cannot fathom the boundaries of these worlds. We Bodhisattvas, dwelling in the stage of non-regression, are likewise unable to comprehend the limit of such worlds. O World Honored One, all these worlds are innumerable and boundless."[^6]

At that moment, the Buddha told the assembled Bodhisattvas:

"Good children, now I shall make clear to you:

**Among all those worlds—whether those where dust has settled and those where it has not—if all these were converted into dust-particles, and one particle represented one eon, then the number of eons since I attained Buddhahood would exceed this calculation by hundreds of thousands of millions of billions of *asamkhyeya* eons.** [^7]
