Possess inexhaustible eloquence
Regarding all dharma-meanings, terminology, and linguistic expressions,
Like wind moving through space with no obstruction.

After the Tathāgata's passing,
Know the sutra's meaning well,
Understand its causes and sequences,
And explain it according to the dharma.

Like the sun and moon illuminating
All darkness and obscurity,
Such a person walks through the world
Bringing light to all beings' darkness,

Teaching infinite bodhisattvas,
Establishing them in the one path (the Lotus teaching).

Therefore, those possessing wisdom,
Hearing of these merits,
After the Buddha's passing,
Should receive and maintain this sutra[^10].

Regarding the Buddha's path,
Without doubt or hesitation,
This person shall truly attain it[^11].

## Philosophical Implications

Chapter 21 functions as a cosmic exclamation point, a demonstration that validates everything taught in the preceding chapters. The supernatural display—the extended tongue reaching Brahma realms, the light-rays illuminating all directions, the earth's six-fold trembling, the voice proclaiming across cosmos—are not mere theatrical effects. They constitute a metaphysical claim: that the dharma of the Lotus Sutra is verified by the entire Buddha-universe.

The extended tongue reaching the Brahma realms possesses profound symbolic significance. In Buddhist cosmology, the Brahma realms represent the highest reaches of conditional existence. The tongue—the organ of speech—extended to this limit suggests that dharma-transmission reaches the extremity of what can be expressed. Moreover, in Buddhist physiology, the tongue symbolizes the power of communication. A tongue extended to the heavens suggests that the sutra's words possess cosmic-spanning power.

The simultaneous display by Buddhas in all ten directions creates a mandala of verification. The historical Buddha Śākyamuni does not stand alone; he is surrounded and supported by all Buddhas across all space. Each Buddha from every direction performs the identical supernatural display, creating a unified, cosmic dharma-transmission. No Buddha differs from any other; all teach the identical sutra. This suggests that the Lotus Sutra represents not a particular teacher's innovation but the universal dharma of all Buddhas.

The six-fold earth trembling—trembling, quaking, roaring, cracking, heaving, and surging—represents a complete cosmic response to the dharma's revelation. Earth is not passive matter but a responsive being. The dharma's truth manifests physically, affecting the fundamental structure of reality. These tremors can be understood as the universe's acknowledgment of dharma-truth.

Most significantly, the chapter establishes that dharma-transmission is not limited to living Buddha-presence. The historical Buddha will pass away into final nirvāṇa. Yet the sutra itself becomes a continuing manifestation of Buddha-presence. Any location where the sutra is received and maintained—whether monastery or forest or lay residence—becomes a bodhi-seat, a place of enlightenment-attainment. This radical principle means that the Buddha's teaching function continues eternally through the sutra-text itself.

The instruction to erect stupas wherever the sutra is maintained reflects this principle at the architectural level. The stupa traditionally houses relics of the Buddha. But here, the text itself is declared to be Buddha-equivalent. The place where the sutra dwells becomes sacred space requiring stupa-honors. This suggests a sophisticated understanding that dharma is not merely abstract truth but concrete presence.

The cloud-like accumulation of offerings rising toward the heavens symbolizes the circulation of merit. The sutra's teaching generates merit that rises to support all the Buddhas; simultaneously, the Buddhas' blessings descend to support dharma-transmission. There is a continuous exchange between the Buddha-realm and the human realm, mediated by the sutra-text.

The declaration "the ten directions become unified and unobstructed, appearing as a single Buddha-realm" represents perhaps the sutra's most radical vision. Normally, the ten directions are separated by immeasurable distances; each Buddha-realm is isolated. Yet through the dharma-transmission of the Lotus Sutra, all realms merge into a single unified field. The boundaries separating Buddha-realms dissolve. This suggests that the sutra accomplishes not merely salvation of individual beings but the fundamental unification of all Buddha-realms, creating a cosmic sangha-body.

# Chapter 22: Entrustment

## The Final Assignment of Dharma-Continuity
At that time, Śākyamuni Buddha rose from his dharma-seat, revealed great supernatural powers, and with his right hand touched the heads of innumerable bodhisattvas, speaking these words: "Through countless, incalculable eons, I have cultivated and perfected the supreme dharma of unsurpassed, perfect enlightenment. Now I entrust this dharma to all of you. You should all unite in mind and widely proclaim this dharma, causing it to increase and flourish[^1]."

Thus did the Buddha touch the heads of the bodhisattva assembly three times, each time declaring: "Through countless, incalculable eons, I have cultivated and perfected the supreme dharma of unsurpassed, perfect enlightenment. Now I entrust this dharma to all of you. You should receive and maintain it, widely proclaim it in all realms, allowing all beings to hear it completely. Why? Because I possess great compassion, complete absence of stinginess or miserliness, and no fear whatsoever. I am able to bestow upon all sentient beings the Buddha's wisdom, the Tathāgata's wisdom, and the spontaneously arising wisdom[^2]. All the Tathāgatas are great benefactors to all sentient beings. You too should follow the example of the Tathāgata, abandoning all stinginess. In the future age, when virtuous men and women who possess faith in the Tathāgata's wisdom approach you, you should widely expound this Lotus Sutra to them so that they may hear it fully. For what reason? In order that they might attain Buddha-wisdom[^3].

"Should any sentient beings not believe, not receive, and not maintain this sutra, then you should guide them through the remaining profound dharmas taught by the Tathāgata, demonstrating benefits to them through skillful teachings, giving joy and delight so that they gradually attain the bodhisattva path. All of you should thereby repay the graciousness of all the Tathāgatas[^4]."

At that moment, hearing the Buddha's instructions, all the bodhisattva assembly experienced profound joy that pervaded their entire being. Even greater reverence and respect arose within them. Bowing low with bent bodies, lowering their heads, and bringing their palms together, they collectively declared: "Just as the World-Honored One has instructed, we shall certainly fulfill this teaching completely. Please have no concern or anxiety, World-Honored One. We shall certainly receive and maintain, read and recite, widely proclaim, and explain this dharma in all lands, enabling all beings to hear it. We shall widely teach it, fulfilling the World-Honored One's instructions[^5]."

The bodhisattva assembly made this declaration three times: "Just as the World-Honored One has instructed, we shall certainly fulfill this teaching completely. Please have no concern, World-Honored One. We shall certainly comply with the World-Honored One's instructions, receiving, maintaining, reading, and reciting this dharma in all lands."

At that moment, Śākyamuni Buddha caused all the emanation-Buddhas from the ten directions—Buddhas seated beneath precious trees throughout the universe—to return to their respective lands. The Buddha then declared: "Each of you Buddhas should rest content. The multi-jeweled stupa of the eternally present Buddha (Prabhūtaratna), may it return to its original condition." Hearing this instruction, all these things occurred as the Buddha proclaimed[^6].

At that time, Prabhūtaratna Buddha, together with Śākyamuni Buddha and all the emanation-Buddhas, the boundless company of bodhisattvas numbering like dust-particles, the leaders of the bodhisattva assembly (the Viśiṣṭa group), the śrāvaka assemblies of the four categories (monks, nuns, laymen, laywomen), and all beings throughout the world—gods, humans, asuras, and all—heard the Buddha's proclamation and all experienced great delight. Bowing respectfully with their heads to the Buddha's feet, they accepted his instruction as an eternal law[^7].
## The Eternal Transmission
*At that time, the Tathāgata wished to restate this meaning through verse:*

All the Buddhas, saviors of the world,
Dwelling in great supernatural power,
For the sake of the bodhisattva path,
Now entrust this dharma to you all.

My Buddha-dharma, accumulated across eons,
Through the cultivation of difficult practices,
Now I place within your hands—
Guard it and cause it to flourish[^8].

In all future worlds,
You should widely proclaim this teaching,
Never allowing it to be exhausted or lost,
So all beings may hear of it[^9].

Buddhas throughout the ten directions,
Both those present now and those of past and future,
Have all proclaimed through the gateway of skillful means,
But this sutra is supreme among all dharmas[^10].

Whoever receives and maintains this sutra,
Receives and maintains all the buddhas' dharmas;
Whoever reads and recites this sutra,
Reads and recites all the dharma spoken by all buddhas[^11].

Therefore practice with single-minded devotion,
Treat the sutra as the Buddha himself,
Just as you honor me with supreme respect,
So too honor this sutra without distinction.

In all places where this sutra dwells,
Whether in monasteries or in forests,
In gardens beneath trees or in dwellings,
Or in lecture-halls or any building—
In all such places should stupas be erected,
And all should make reverent offerings,
Gathering in masses like clouds,
Honoring this place as the Buddha's sacred site.

The Buddha, having attained enlightenment here,
Turns the dharma-wheel here,
Enters final nirvāṇa here—
All the Buddha-functions occur where the dharma dwells[^12].

After I enter the final extinction,
You should spread this sutra,
Causing all the world-systems
To hear of its teachings.

By this, you shall all repay
The kindness of the Tathāgata,
And quickly attain
Perfect enlightenment[^13].

## Philosophical Implications

Chapter 22 completes the Lotus Sutra's structure with an act of formal transmission. The Buddha, about to enter final nirvāṇa, entrusts the sutra-dharma to the assembled bodhisattvas and beings. This creates a legal and spiritual bond: the assembly vows to continue transmission; the Buddha authorizes this continuation.

The threefold touching of the bodhisattvas' heads carries profound significance. This is a gesture of blessing and authorization, appearing in multiple Buddhist contexts. More specifically, it echoes the Buddha's original awakening at the bodhi-tree, where he touched the earth to witness his enlightenment. Here, the Buddha touches the bodhisattvas' heads to witness and authorize their dharma-transmission capacity.

The language of the assignment itself deserves careful attention. The Buddha does not give merely a teaching or instruction but assigns "the dharma of unsurpassed, perfect enlightenment" itself. This is not a verbal transfer but a trans-temporal event. The Buddha places within the bodhisattvas' "hands" (metaphorically) the actual enlightenment-dharma that took him countless eons to perfect. This suggests a radical Buddhist principle: that enlightenment is not a personal achievement but a cosmic dharma that passes from Buddha to bodhisattva to future-Buddha across eons.

The emphasis on "refusing none and fearing none" deserves attention. The Buddha declares that he possesses "complete absence of stinginess" and "no fear whatsoever." In Buddhism, stinginess (mātcharya) is listed as a fundamental obstacle to generosity and enlightenment. The Buddha's complete absence of stinginess means unlimited generosity—specifically, the unreserved gift of enlightenment-dharma to all beings. His fearlessness means that this gift is offered regardless of whether beings believe or reject it.

The principle that Buddhas possess three wisdoms—the Buddha's wisdom, the Tathāgata's wisdom, and spontaneously-arising wisdom—represents a sophisticated Buddhist epistemology. The first wisdom involves knowing all dharmas; the second involves knowing all beings' capacities and inclinations; the third involves spontaneous, effortless knowing that requires no deliberation. The bodhisattvas are authorized to transmit these wisdoms.

The provision for those who "do not believe, do not receive, do not maintain" the sutra deserves careful attention. The Buddha does not declare such beings forever lost. Rather, he instructs the bodhisattvas to guide them through "remaining profound dharmas" and "skillful teachings" appropriate to their capacity. This reflects the principle of upaya (skillful means): dharma-teachers adjust their teaching to each being's capacity, recognizing that the Lotus Sutra represents one of infinite dharma-gates through which all beings eventually approach enlightenment.

The response of the assembly—their declaration made three times—mirrors the Buddha's threefold transmission. This creates a symmetrical structure: the Buddha speaks three times assigning the dharma; the assembly responds three times vowing to maintain it. This parallelism suggests perfect understanding and alignment.

The geographical distribution of the emanation-Buddhas returning to their respective lands symbolizes that dharma-transmission is not spatially limited. Buddhas in all directions return to their realms, yet remain connected through the unified dharma-transmission of the Lotus Sutra. Distance becomes irrelevant; through the sutra, all Buddha-realms maintain continuous connection.

The reincorporation of Prabhūtaratna Buddha's stupa—returning to its "original condition"—suggests that the stupa's manifestation served a specific function (verifying the sutra through its presence) that is now completed. The stupa dematerializes or returns to its eternal form, suggesting that temporal manifestations serve temporary purposes while eternal dharma persists.

The final declaration that all beings—"gods, humans, asuras, and all"—accept the instruction "as an eternal law" is crucial. The transmission is not merely to bodhisattvas or humans but to all categories of beings. Moreover, they accept it "as eternal law," suggesting that dharma-transmission acquires cosmic legal status. It becomes not merely spiritual practice but ontological necessity, woven into the structure of existence itself.

# Chapter 23: The Medicine King Bodhisattva's Original Practice

## The Bodhisattva's Extreme Offering
At that time, Śākyamuni Buddha addressed the Bodhisattva Prabhūtaratna: "Inquire of me regarding the Medicine King Bodhisattva's original practice. How did this bodhisattva cultivate? What dharma does he teach? Pray tell us the history of this one we honor[^1]."

Buddha replied: "In ages past, beyond measurement in incalculable eons, there existed a Buddha named Sun-Moon-Pure-Bright-Virtue—the Tathāgata, the Arhat, the Perfectly Awakened One, the One Perfectly Accomplished in Knowledge and Conduct, the Sugata, the Knower of the World, the Unsurpassable Guide, the Tamer of the Untamed, the Teacher of Gods and Humans, the Buddha, the World-Honored One. He possessed eighty billion great bodhisattvas and an assembly of seventy-two trillion enlightened śrāvakas. That Buddha's lifespan spanned four million billion nayuta eons. The true dharma remained in that realm for a period measured in years equal to the dust-particles of a continent. The semblance dharma likewise persisted through such measure.

"In that realm, there existed a bodhisattva named All-Beings-Are-Delighted-by-the-Sight—a bodhisattva who had long cultivated the roots of virtue, offered reverence to innumerable Buddhas, and perfected profound wisdom. This bodhisattva had achieved numerous samādhis: the samādhi of displaying all forms, the samādhi of dharma-blossoming, the samādhi of pure virtue, the samādhi of celestial play, and countless others[^2].

"At that time, the Buddha Sun-Moon-Pure-Bright-Virtue taught the Dharma-Blossom Sutra to all sentient beings. All-Beings-Are-Delighted-by-the-Sight heard this teaching and, wishing to demonstrate his understanding, entered the samādhi of displaying all forms. From within this samādhi, he caused himself to manifest in an ocean of amrita (divine nectar) within the void itself. Having perceived one hundred thousand kinds of precious flowers blooming in that ocean, he declared: 'The dharma I now perceive through the Dharma-Blossom Sutra is so profound! I vow to honor the Buddha and this supreme teaching through ultimate offering.'

"Having made this vow, the bodhisattva collected all the flowers from the ocean of amrita and, gathering them together, presented them to Buddha Sun-Moon-Pure-Bright-Virtue. The vast assembly received this offering and rejoiced greatly[^3].

"Afterward, the bodhisattva reflected: 'Though I have offered precious flowers, my heart is not yet satisfied. I now vow to offer my very body as a gift of honor to this Supreme Dharma Sutra.'

"The bodhisattva then gathered together all the celestial bodhisattvas, śrāvakas, and beings of the heavens, and spoke: 'All sentient beings, now listen! I vow to make an offering of my own body to the Buddha Sun-Moon-Pure-Bright-Virtue and to the Dharma-Blossom Sutra!' Having spoken, the bodhisattva began an extreme practice. He ingested all manner of fragrant waters and precious oils—sandalwood, aloeswood, and other aromatics—for one thousand two hundred years. His body became saturated with these precious substances. Then, wrapping himself in silk and jeweled vestments, and anointing himself with expensive oils, the bodhisattva used supernatural power to ignite his own body as an eternal offering.

"His burning body radiated light across eighty billion nayuta realms. All the Buddhas in these realms perceived this offering and spoke these words simultaneously: 'Excellent! Excellent! This virtuous man has accomplished the supreme offering! To offer flowers, fragrances, garlands, or even entire kingdoms and beloved family members to the Buddha cannot equal this supreme gift of one's own body! This is the supreme offering among all offerings, the most exalted offering among all offerings, given in honor of the dharma and Buddha-realization. O virtuous man, through this supreme sacrifice of your body, you have completed the bodhisattva path!'

"After the bodhisattva's body burned for one thousand two hundred years and was finally consumed, he was reborn in that same Buddha-realm in the royal family. His consciousness re-emerged in his mother's womb. At that moment, the bodhisattva addressed his father in verse:

*'Great King, hear now my words—*
*I have wandered in that place,*
*And suddenly obtained the samādhi*
*That manifests all forms.*
*I have cultivated the supreme offering,*
*And I have burned my body,*
*For I seek the incomparable wisdom,*
*The wisdom of the perfectly enlightened Buddha.'*

"Having spoken this verse, the bodhisattva said to his father: 'The Buddha Sun-Moon-Pure-Bright-Virtue remains present in that realm. I previously made offering to him and heard the Dharma-Blossom Sutra containing eight hundred trillion billion verses. Great King, I now vow to return to that Buddha's presence to honor him again.' With these words, the bodhisattva levitated into the void, ascending seven palm-trees' height, and approached the Buddha's presence where he again paid reverence and made offerings[^4].

"When this All-Beings-Are-Delighted-by-the-Sight Bodhisattva completed his remaining lifespan, he encountered two billion Buddhas, all called the Sun Moon Pure Bright Virtue Buddhas—Buddhas whose radiance illuminated all worlds—and in each Buddha's teaching he received, maintained, recited, and widely proclaimed the Dharma-Blossom Sutra. Because he taught this dharma to the four categories of disciples, his vision continuously clarified and he continued the practice of bodily offering.

"Subsequently, he encountered another two billion Buddhas, all called the Cloud Sovereign Lamp King Buddhas, and similarly received their teaching of the Dharma-Blossom Sutra. Through his continued proclamation, he further perfected the vision-clarity.

"Having encountered countless billions of Buddhas, received the Dharma-Blossom Sutra from all, and proclaimed it widely to the four categories of disciples, his complete enlightenment-wisdom was perfected. He thus attained supreme, perfect enlightenment.

"Prabhūtaratna, do you comprehend the meaning of my account? This All-Beings-Are-Delighted-by-the-Sight Bodhisattva—he is none other than the Medicine King Bodhisattva who sits here before us! Such are the bodhisattva's past accomplishments. This Medicine King has offered his own body to countless billions of Buddhas, sacrificing his form as supreme homage to the dharma. This bodhisattva has completed practice across countless eons. These accomplishments are immeasurable[^5].

"Should a virtuous man or woman aspire to perfect enlightenment and yet offer only a single finger or a single toe in homage to the Buddha-stupa—such an offering exceeds all offerings of kingdoms, wives, children, and entire world-systems! Furthermore, if a virtuous person fills the entire three-thousand-great-thousand-world-system with the seven jewels and offers them to Buddhas, bodhisattvas, solitary-buddhas, and arhats—such an offering pales before the merit of simply receiving and maintaining even a single four-line verse of this Dharma-Blossom Sutra!"

> **Note**: The Kumārajīva translation (T0262) does not contain verses for Chapter 23. Verses found in some other translations and the Sanskrit version are omitted here to maintain fidelity to the Taishō text.

## Philosophical Implications

Chapter 23 presents enlightenment-practice through its most extreme form: bodily self-immolation as dharma-offering. This raises profound questions about the nature of sacrifice, suffering, and the transformation of physical body into sacred presence.

The bodhisattva's practice unfolds in carefully structured stages. First comes the perception through samādhi (samadhi of displaying all forms). Second comes the flower-offering, which is subsequently recognized as insufficient. Third comes the ultimate sacrifice: the burning of one's own body sustained through aromatic-saturation for centuries.

The comparative logic is essential: even the most elaborate material offerings—kingdoms, treasures, family members—cannot equal the supreme offering of bodily self-immolation. This suggests a metaphysical claim that the body is ultimately the most valuable asset a being possesses. To surrender it is to surrender one's fundamental claim to existence.

Yet paradoxically, the chapter does not treat this sacrifice as termination but as transformation. The body burns for twelve hundred years yet consciousness is not destroyed. The bodhisattva is reborn immediately in that same realm, now embodied as a prince. What burns is not consciousness but form. The text presents this paradox without resolving it: the body can be simultaneously consumed and retained, destroyed and renewed.

The multiplication of Buddha-encounters is significant. This bodhisattva does not encounter one Buddha and achieve enlightenment. Rather, the pattern repeats across billions of Buddha-epochs. Each encounter involves the same practice: receiving the dharma-blossom sutra, proclaiming it, maintaining it. There is no final arrival, no termination of practice. Enlightenment emerges not from a single achievement but from eternal recurrence of the same fundamental practice.

The naming of this bodhisattva is itself instructive. "All-Beings-Are-Delighted-by-the-Sight" later becomes "Medicine King." The transformation from a name emphasizing visible form to one emphasizing healing suggests a spiritual development. The bodhisattva begins focused on perceptual transformation (all beings seeing) and ends focused on healing transformation (medicine-application).

The chapter also articulates a sophisticated economics of merit. Material offering, no matter how elaborate, produces merit limited by scarcity and finiteness. A person can give treasures and kingdoms because they are finite. But self-offering is infinite: the body's burning does not deplete the dharma; rather, each moment of burning constitutes a new offering. Time itself becomes the measure of gift-magnitude.

# Chapter 24: The Wonderful-Sound Bodhisattva

## The Interdimensional Visitor
At that time, Śākyamuni Buddha emitted the light-marks of universal brilliance from between his eyebrows, illuminating to the east one hundred eight hundred million nayuta realms. Beyond that number of worlds, there existed a realm named Pure-Light-Adorned. In that realm dwelt a Buddha named Pure Flower Constellation King Wisdom-Tathāgata, the Arhat, the Perfectly Awakened One, the One Perfectly Accomplished in Knowledge and Conduct, the Sugata, the Knower of the World, the Unsurpassable Guide, the Tamer of the Untamed, the Teacher of Gods and Humans, the Buddha, the World-Honored One. He was surrounded and honored by innumerable and incalculable assemblies of great bodhisattvas as he expounded the dharma[^1].

At that time, the light from the Buddha's eyebrow-mark illuminated the Pure-Light-Adorned realm, causing that Buddha and his assembly to perceive Śākyamuni Buddha's dharma-transmission. Within that realm dwelt a bodhisattva named Wonderful-Sound, one who had long cultivated roots of virtue, paid reverence to countless billions of Buddhas, and achieved profound wisdom. This bodhisattva had perfected eighteen kinds of dharma-gates (meditative absorptions and capacities), including the Marvelous-Banner Samādhi, the Dharma-Blossom Samādhi, the Pure-Virtue Samādhi, the Celestial-Play Samādhi, the Boundless Samādhi, the Wisdom-Seal Samādhi, the Gate of Understanding-All-Beings'-Language, the Samādhi of Gathering All Merits, the Pure Samādhi, the Divine-Play-Through-Powers Samādhi, the Wisdom-Torch Samādhi, the Sovereign-Adornment Samādhi, the Pure-Illumination Samādhi, the Treasury-of-Purity Samādhi, the Unshared Samādhi, the Solar-Revolution Samādhi, and countless billions of other dharma-gates[^2].

When the Buddha's light illuminated this bodhisattva's body, Wonderful-Sound immediately addressed his Buddha, Pure Flower Constellation King Wisdom: "World-Honored One, I perceive that the light from Śākyamuni Buddha's form reaches here. I wish to journey to the Sahā world-realm, to pay reverence to, to draw near to, to offer worship to Śākyamuni Buddha, and to see Mañjuśrī the Dharma-Prince and other bodhisattvas, including Medicine King and Courageous-Giver. I also wish to hear the Dharma-Blossom Sutra[^3]."

His Buddha, Pure Flower Constellation King Wisdom, replied: "My child, do not regard the Sahā realm with disdain or contempt. Why? Because the Sahā world is rocky and uneven, filled with dirt and soil. The body of Śākyamuni Buddha is diminutive, and the bodhisattvas too are small in stature. Yet your body measures forty-two thousand yojanas, while my body measures six hundred eighty thousand yojanas. Your form is supremely beautiful, adorned with hundreds of thousands of blessings and resplendent light, incomparably magnificent. When you travel there, do not regard that realm or its Buddha and bodhisattvas with contempt[^4]."

Wonderful-Sound replied to his Buddha: "World-Honored One, my journey to the Sahā world is entirely the power of the Tathāgata. It is the Tathāgata's miraculous display, the Tathāgata's virtue and wisdom adorning all things[^5]."

Having said this, Wonderful-Sound Bodhisattva did not rise from his seat, his body remained unmoved, yet through the power of samādhi, he manifested in the Sahā realm at Vulture Peak Mountain. Before the Buddha's dharma-seat, he created eighty-four thousand jeweled lotus flowers: their stems were made of refined gold, their leaves of white silver, their pistils of vajra-stone, their calyxes of precious carnelian-ruby stone[^6].

At that time, Mañjuśrī the Dharma-Prince, observing these lotus flowers, addressed the Buddha: "World-Honored One, what is the cause and significance of this miraculous manifestation? What auspicious sign do these countless thousands of lotus flowers, with stems of refined gold, leaves of silver, pistils of vajra, and calyxes of precious stones, portend[^7]?"

Śākyamuni Buddha replied to Mañjuśrī: "The Great Bodhisattva Wonderful-Sound desires to come from the Pure-Light realm, together with eighty-four thousand bodhisattvas, to visit this Sahā world-realm, to pay reverence, to draw near, to offer worship to me, and to hear the Dharma-Blossom Sutra[^8]."

Mañjuśrī asked: "World-Honored One, what virtuous roots has this bodhisattva cultivated? What dharma has this bodhisattva practiced? What samādhi does this bodhisattva dwell in? I wish to understand the name of this samādhi, that we too might cultivate and practice it. If one cultivates this samādhi, one may behold this bodhisattva's magnificent form, the marks of his bearing and deportment. I pray that the World-Honored One will display his miraculous power so that this bodhisattva comes, and allow us all to perceive him[^9]."

The Buddha told Mañjuśrī: "The eternally-present Buddha Prabhūtaratna shall display his form and reveal this bodhisattva's appearance[^10]."

At that moment, Prabhūtaratna Buddha addressed Wonderful-Sound from the jeweled stupa: "Come, virtuous man. The Dharma-Prince Mañjuśrī wishes to perceive your form[^8]."

Then Wonderful-Sound Bodhisattva disappeared from the Pure-Light realm and, together with eighty-four thousand bodhisattvas, journeyed to the Sahā world. Wherever they passed, the six kinds of earth-trembling occurred, and the sky rained precious lotus flowers. Celestial music played spontaneously without being played. The Great Bodhisattva's eyes resembled vast blue lotus flowers. His face was exceedingly beautiful and dignified, surpassing the magnificence created by the merger of a hundred thousand billion moons. His body shone with the radiance of refined gold, adorned with hundreds of thousands of merits and virtues. His magnificence blazed with resplendent light; his marks and signs were all complete, as if embodying the steadfast nature of the mighty Nārāyaṇa[^11].

He ascended the jeweled platform, rose seven palm-trees high in the void, and approached Vulture Peak Mountain together with his bodhisattva-assembly. Upon arrival, he descended from the jeweled platform and, holding an ornament of pearls worth hundreds of thousands, approached Śākyamuni Buddha, bowed with his head to the Buddha's feet, and presented the ornament, speaking:

"World-Honored One, the Buddha Pure Flower Constellation King Wisdom sends his regards. He inquires: Does the World-Honored One experience few ailments, few sufferings, and does he dwell in ease? Do the four elements remain in harmony? Is the world bearable? Are the people easy to teach? Do they experience little greed, anger, delusion, jealousy, and stinginess? Do they show respect to parents, honor monks, avoid perverse views and unwholesome thoughts, and guard their five senses well? Are the people able to overcome demonic armies? Has the eternally-present Buddha Prabhūtaratna, who entered final extinction ages ago, come to listen to the dharma? And how is the eternally-present Buddha—is he peaceful, few-suffering, and able to remain permanently? World-Honored One, I wish to behold the eternally-present Buddha. Please reveal him so that I may see[^12]."

Śākyamuni Buddha said to Prabhūtaratna: "This Great Bodhisattva Wonderful-Sound wishes to meet you."

Prabhūtaratna replied to Wonderful-Sound: "Excellent, excellent, virtuous man! You have come to this realm to honor Śākyamuni Buddha, to hear the Dharma-Blossom Sutra, and to see Mañjuśrī and others. You have accomplished this well[^13]."

At that time, the Bodhisattva Dharma-Virtue asked the Buddha: "World-Honored One, what virtuous roots has this Wonderful-Sound Bodhisattva cultivated? What dharmas does he practice to possess such miraculous power?"

The Buddha replied to Dharma-Virtue: "In ages past, there was a Buddha named Cloud-Thunder-Sound-Sovereign—the Tathāgata, the Arhat, the Perfectly Awakened One. In the dharma of that Buddha, Wonderful-Sound Bodhisattva cultivated celestial music as offering for twelve thousand years, presenting to that Buddha one hundred thousand varieties of musical instruments. Additionally, he offered eighty-four thousand seven-jeweled bowls. Through this karma, he was born in the Pure-Light-Adorned realm and acquired this miraculous power[^14].

"Dharma-Virtue, do you now see Wonderful-Sound Bodhisattva sitting here before you? Though his body appears to dwell in this place, he simultaneously manifests in countless forms throughout the ten directions, teaching the Dharma-Blossom Sutra to all sentient beings. Sometimes he appears as a Brahma-king, sometimes as Śakra, sometimes as a self-mastering deity, sometimes as a great self-mastering deity, sometimes as a celestial general, sometimes as King Vaiśravaṇa, sometimes as a Cakravartin-king, sometimes as a smaller king, sometimes as a clan-leader, sometimes as a householder, sometimes as an official, sometimes as a Brahmin, sometimes as a monk or nun, sometimes as a male or female lay follower, sometimes as a wife of a householder or official, sometimes as a Brahmin woman, sometimes as a boy or girl, or even as a divine dragon, nāga, yakṣa, gandharva, asura, garuda, kinnara, mahoraga, human or non-human being. He manifests in these forms to teach the dharma. And he saves even those in the hell-realms, hungry ghost realms, animal realms, and the difficult-to-escape realms. He even appears in royal palaces as a female form to teach the dharma[^15]."

The Buddha continued: "Dharma-Virtue, Wonderful-Sound Bodhisattva performs such miraculous transformations and through wisdom illuminates the Sahā world, enabling all sentient beings to understand according to their capacities. Likewise, in the ten-directional worlds numbering like the sands of the Ganges River, he manifests in similar ways. Depending on whom he encounters: if a being requires the form of a śrāvaka to be taught, he manifests that form; if a solitary-buddha, he manifests that form; if a bodhisattva, he manifests that form; if a Buddha, he manifests the Buddha-form; if a being requires extinction to reach liberation, he demonstrates that extinction[^16]."

Dharma-Virtue Bodhisattva asked: "World-Honored One, this bodhisattva has cultivated such profound virtue. In what samādhi does he dwell such that he can manifest these transformations and benefit countless beings?"

The Buddha replied: "This samādhi is called 'Manifesting All Forms.' Wonderful-Sound Bodhisattva dwells in this samādhi and thereby benefits countless sentient beings[^17]."

When the Dharma-Blossom Sutra regarding the Coming and Going of Wonderful-Sound was taught, the eighty-four thousand beings who had journeyed with Wonderful-Sound all obtained the Samādhi of Manifesting All Forms. Moreover, countless bodhisattvas throughout the Sahā world and the ten directions obtained this samādhi and dharma-gate[^8].

After paying reverence and offering to Śākyamuni Buddha and the stupa of the eternally-present Buddha, Wonderful-Sound Bodhisattva returned to his own realm together with the eighty-four thousand bodhisattvas. As they traveled through all the lands they passed, six-fold trembling occurred, precious lotus flowers rained, and hundreds of millions of kinds of celestial music played.

Having returned to his realm, Wonderful-Sound approached the Buddha Pure Flower Constellation King Wisdom together with the eighty-four thousand bodhisattvas and addressed him: "World-Honored One, I have journeyed to the Sahā world and derived great benefit for all sentient beings. I have seen Śākyamuni Buddha, perceived the stupa of the eternally-present Buddha Prabhūtaratna, and met Mañjuśrī the Dharma-Prince and other bodhisattvas including Medicine King and Courageous-Giver. I have also enabled these eighty-four thousand bodhisattvas to obtain the Samādhi of Manifesting All Forms. Moreover, through teaching this teaching of the Wonderful-Sound Bodhisattva's Coming-and-Going, forty-two thousand celestial deities have obtained the recognition of the non-arising of dharmas, and the Bodhisattva Dharma-Virtue has obtained the Dharma-Blossom Samādhi[^19]."
## The Transformation-Manifestation
*At that time, the Buddha wished to restate this meaning through verse:*

From the eastern realm, beyond reckoning,
From the Pure-Light-Adorned World,
There came a bodhisattva named Wonderful-Sound,
Together with eighty-four thousand beings[^20].

He cultivated virtue in the ancient past,
And made celestial-music offerings
To the Buddha Cloud-Thunder-Sound-Sovereign,
For twelve thousand years continuously.

Through this offering, he attained realization,
And was born in that pure realm,
Where he dwells perfected in all merits,
In the light-adorned paradise.

He manifests infinite forms,
In all the worlds of the ten directions,
Teaching the dharma in countless ways,
Transforming according to each being's need[^21].

If one requires a Buddha-form for teaching,
He manifests as Buddha;
If one requires a bodhisattva-form,
He manifests accordingly.

If one requires extinction to reach peace,
He demonstrates that nirvāṇa;
In such boundless manifestations,
He performs his sacred work.

Upon hearing Śākyamuni Buddha's name,
And learning of the Dharma-Blossom Sutra,
He journeyed across incalculable worlds,
With eighty-four thousand attending companions.

Eighty-four thousand precious lotus flowers,
With golden stems and silver leaves,
Adorned with diamond pistils,
And ruby calyxes in profusion[^22].

The earth trembled with six-fold motion,
While precious flowers fell like rain,
And celestial music played spontaneously,
As the great assembly perceived his coming.

This bodhisattva's body measures vastly,
Forty-two thousand yojanas in extent,
Adorned with hundreds of thousands of marks,
Resplendent with wisdom and merit[^23].

The Buddha's eyebrow-light revealed him,
And all beheld the great being's form,
And heard the dharma he expounded,
The path of manifesting all forms.

All those who traveled with him,
Gained the samādhi of manifestation,
And forty-two thousand celestial deities,
Obtained the dharma-eye of recognition.

After paying reverence to the eternal Buddha,
And to the stupa of Prabhūtaratna,
The Wonderful-Sound Bodhisattva returned,
To his own Pure-Light realm.

## Philosophical Implications

Chapter 24 demonstrates a revolutionary principle: that bodhisattvas can exist in multiple Buddha-realms simultaneously and maintain autonomous agency even while being expressions of another being's miraculous power. The paradox is emphasized repeatedly: Wonderful-Sound "did not rise from his seat, his body remained unmoved, yet through the power of samādhi" he manifested elsewhere.

This suggests a Buddhist understanding of consciousness that is radically non-local. The bodhisattva's consciousness is not confined to a single body but can inhabit multiple manifestations without fragmentation. This is not reincarnation (sequential birth in different forms) but simultaneous manifestation (existing in multiple forms at once).

# Chapter 25: Avalokiteśvara Bodhisattva's Gateway of Universal Access

---

## Imperial Preface to the Avalokiteśvara Universal Gate Chapter
### 御製觀世音普門品經序

*Imperial Preface by the Yongle Emperor*
*(永樂九年五月初一日 — May 1, 1411)*

---

Avalokiteśvara Bodhisattva, with a heart of adamantine resolve, responds inexhaustibly to all transformations. Through sovereign spiritual powers, [this Bodhisattva] travels freely throughout the Dharma-realm, entering micro-dust lands to expound the Dharma and bring salvation. Possessed of wondrous marks in full, [this Bodhisattva's] great vow is vast as the ocean. Whoever has the karmic connection and arouses a pure mind—the moment they raise their voice to call upon [this Bodhisattva], [this Bodhisattva] immediately responds to that sound, and all their desires are fulfilled according to their wishes.

The Universal Gate Chapter of the *Lotus Sutra of the Wonderful Dharma* is the true teaching for liberating [beings] from suffering and affliction. If one can constantly contemplate this sutra, the moment a single thought arises, one immediately perceives the victorious marks of Great Compassion, able to extinguish all suffering; its merit is inconceivable.

I [the Emperor] reflect that the Way of Heaven brings fortune to the good and calamity to the licentious; therefore, the Buddha revealed karmic retribution to make people do good and not dare to do evil. Heaven and Hell are both made by human actions—they do not depart from within one's own heart. Therefore, those who do good ascend to Heaven; those who do evil fall into Hell.

Loyal ministers, filial children, auspicious people, and steadfast gentlemen—their minds are Buddha. Therefore, divine spirits protect them and their karmic obstructions are entirely eliminated. Thus, in life they do not transgress the laws, and in death they do not fall into uninterrupted [Hell].

As for cruel and obstinate people who are bent on doing evil, who discard the Five Relationships like worn-out brooms and tread upon criminal law as if drinking something sweet, who would rather feed rākṣasas than revere the Buddha's Way—human nature is fundamentally good. Those who do evil are merely distorted by their temperament. If they can transform their minds, change their thoughts, cultivate self-reflection, and approach with caution, then in an instant evil can become good. To do good is to become a good person. The faults accumulated in the past become like a speck of dust in the vast sky, like a flake of snow in a red-hot furnace—cleansed and purified completely. Though karmic retribution exists, where shall it be applied?

I constantly reflect upon this. I only fear that people of the world, having faults, do not know to reform, but willingly abandon themselves. Therefore, I have promulgated this sutra so that virtuous gentlemen may forever strengthen their minds in upholding the precepts and broadly receive immeasurable blessing. The merit of doing good—how can it have any limit!

*The first day of the fifth month of the ninth year of the Yongle reign*

---

## The Bodhisattva of Boundless Compassion
At that time, the Bodhisattva Boundless-Intention rose from his seat, bowed respectfully with his head to the Buddha's feet, and posed this inquiry: "World-Honored One, I wish to ask: For what reason is the Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara called by this name[^1]?"

The Buddha replied: "Excellent question, Boundless-Intention. If countless billions of sentient beings experiencing suffering hear the name Avalokiteśvara and call upon this bodhisattva with sincere intention, the Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara will immediately perceive the sound of their invocation. That being will at once gain liberation. For this reason, this bodhisattva is named Avalokiteśvara—the One Who Perceives the World's Sounds of Suffering[^2].

"If a being faces great fire and calls upon Avalokiteśvara, the flames cannot burn such a person, because the bodhisattva's majestic spiritual power prevents the fire from destroying them. If one is swept away by a great flood and cries out to Avalokiteśvara, one will suddenly find oneself in shallow water. If a hundred thousand billion sentient beings venture onto the great ocean seeking treasures—silver, lapis lazuli, crystal, agate, coral, amber, pearls and other jewels—and their boat is caught in a black wind and driven toward the realm of the rākṣasa demons, a single person among them calling upon Avalokiteśvara will rescue all from the danger of the demons[^3].

"If someone faces impending execution and invokes Avalokiteśvara, the executioner's weapons will shatter into fragments and the condemned person will escape. If a being is bound with chains or shackles and calls upon this bodhisattva, all restraints will break free, and that person will attain liberation. If a region is filled with countless night-demons and rākṣasas intending to cause harm, and they hear the name Avalokiteśvara invoked, these harmful beings will not dare even look upon the invocant with malice, much less cause injury[^4].

"Moreover, Boundless-Intention, if a being harbors excessive lust and constantly honors and reveres Avalokiteśvara, that being will be liberated from lust. If one is enslaved by anger, constant reverence to Avalokiteśvara brings liberation from anger. If one is trapped in delusion, such reverence brings freedom from delusion. Therefore, in this Sahā world, he is called the Giver of Fearlessness (施無畏者)[^5].

"Avalokiteśvara possesses such great divine power. If one wishes to bear a son, one should reverence and offer to this bodhisattva, and one will birth a virtuous, wise, and meritorious son. If one wishes a daughter, one will birth a beautiful, accomplished, and virtuous daughter, beloved and respected by all.

"Boundless-Intention, any sentient being who venerates Avalokiteśvara will not lose the fruit of that reverence. For this reason, all beings should always turn their thoughts toward this bodhisattva.

"If someone sustains the names of sixty-two billion Bodhisattvas equal to the dust of the Ganges River, and provides them with all necessities—food, clothing, bedding, and medicine—throughout their lives, what merit would they accumulate?"

Boundless-Intention replied: "Immeasurable, World-Honored One."

The Buddha declared: "If another person sustains the name of Avalokiteśvara, even offering a single moment of reverence, the merit would be identical—no difference whatsoever. Even through incalculable billions of eons, the merit could never be exhausted[^6].

"Boundless-Intention, if I were to teach all the dharmas concerning how Avalokiteśvara traverses this Sahā world, in what manner Avalokiteśvara teaches the dharma through skillful means, the discussion would require incalculable eons. Therefore, in summary: all sentient beings experiencing anxiety and distress, if they hear of Avalokiteśvara, will find immediate relief through the bodhisattva's power of wise compassion. For this reason, all should trust in Avalokiteśvara[^7]."
## The Thirty-Three Manifestations
Then Buddha continued: "Boundless-Intention, if sentient beings require the form of a Buddha to be taught and liberated, Avalokiteśvara will manifest as a Buddha and teach them the dharma. If they require the form of a solitary-buddha to achieve liberation, the bodhisattva will manifest as a solitary-buddha. If they require a śrāvaka-form, the bodhisattva manifests accordingly—the bodhisattva can manifest as a Brahma-king, as Śakra, as a self-mastering deity, as a great self-mastering deity, as a celestial general, as King Vaiśravaṇa, as a Cakravartin-king, as a smaller king[^8].

"If they require the form of a householder to be taught, Avalokiteśvara manifests as a householder. If they require the form of an official, merchant, Brahmin, or member of any other occupation, the bodhisattva manifests accordingly.

"If they require the form of a monk, nun, male lay follower, or female lay follower, the bodhisattva manifests as such. If a being is to be liberated through the appearance of a wife, the bodhisattva manifests as a wife; through a concubine, as a concubine; through a daughter, as a daughter; through a mother, as a mother. If one requires manifestation as a divine being, a dragon, a yakṣa, a gandharva, an asura, a garuda, a kinnara, a mahoraga, a human, or a non-human being—in all these forms, Avalokiteśvara manifests to teach and liberate.

"If a being is to be liberated through the appearance of an arhat, the bodhisattva manifests as an arhat. If one requires the manifestation of a Pratyeka-Buddha, the form manifests accordingly. Moreover, Avalokiteśvara manifests even as a Vajrapāṇi (Vajra-holding Spirit). In such unlimited ways, through countless forms, in all the worlds of the ten directions, the bodhisattva travels, liberating all beings. For this reason, all should turn their sincere attention toward Avalokiteśvara and cultivate reverence[^9]."
## *[Verses Translated by the Sui Dynasty Śramaṇa Jñānagupta]*

> **Note**: Kumārajīva's original Chinese translation (姚秦, 406 CE) contained only the prose section above. The following verses (重頌) were translated later by the North Indian Śramaṇa Jñānagupta (闍那崛多) during the Sui Dynasty and subsequently integrated into the canonical text.

*At that time, Boundless-Intention wished to restate these teachings in verse:*

O World-Honored One of wondrous form,
I now inquire of you again:
Why is this bodhisattva called by this name?
What is the source of Avalokiteśvara's designation[^10]?

The Buddha replied to Boundless-Intention:
Listen to the Practice of Avalokiteśvara,
This bodhisattva responds skillfully in all realms,
Establishing profound vows across countless eons.

The power of Avalokiteśvara's vow is immeasurable as the ocean,
Having served infinite billions of Buddhas, continuing without measure,
By cultivating profound wisdom and boundless compassion,
The bodhisattva responds to all cries and delivers all beings[^11].

If malicious intent arises and someone pushes you into a great pit of fire,
Call upon the power of Avalokiteśvara,
And the fire will transform into a lotus pond.
Or if swept away by a violent flood,
Drowning seems certain,
Call upon the power of Avalokiteśvara,
And you will find yourself in shallow waters.

If you are caught in a great ocean storm,
While seeking precious treasures,
With waves high as mountains and demons threatening,
Call upon the power of Avalokiteśvara,
And you shall be delivered safely.

If facing execution, blades and weapons raised against you,
Call upon the power of Avalokiteśvara,
And the weapons will shatter into fragments,
And you will escape unharmed.

If bound in chains or locked in prison stocks,
Your hands and feet shackled,
Call upon the power of Avalokiteśvara,
And the restraints will fall away,
Your liberation complete.

When a region is filled with demons and yakṣas,
Intending to disturb and torment people,
Call upon the power of Avalokiteśvara,
And even their hateful glances will not fall upon you,
Much less can they do you harm[^12].

If curses, poisons, or witchcraft are employed against you,
Meant to injure your body,
Call upon the power of Avalokiteśvara,
And all such harm will rebound to the sender.

If you encounter wicked rākṣasas or poisonous dragons,
Fierce beasts with sharp teeth and claws,
Call upon the power of Avalokiteśvara,
And all will flee in all directions.

If surrounded by threatening serpents, scorpions,
Their poison smoke burning like fire,
Call upon the power of Avalokiteśvara,
And these will immediately turn back and flee.

When thunder roars and lightning flashes,
Hail falls and rain pours down,
Call upon the power of Avalokiteśvara,
And all these disturbances will clear away.

Boundless beings in distress,
Oppressed by countless sufferings,
Through the wondrous wisdom and power of Avalokiteśvara,
All can be liberated from suffering.

The Bodhisattva possesses supernatural power,
With vast expedient skill and boundless compassion,
In all lands throughout the ten directions,
The bodhisattva manifests in every place.

In all the evil realms—
Hell-realm, hungry ghost realm, animal realm—
And in all the places of difficulty and hardship,
The Bodhisattva manifests to liberate all beings.

He appears as the king of all heavens,
Or as the king of universal rulers,
As the sovereign Brahma-king,
Or as Śakra, lord of the thirty-three heavens,
Or as governors and ministers,
Appearing wherever called, in whatever form needed.

In the palaces of royalty and nobility,
The bodhisattva appears as a female form,
Teaching the dharma to those who need such manifestation.

Perfect perception of all sounds—pure light!
The light of wisdom breaking through all darkness,
The light that vanquishes all suffering and disaster,
This is why all should revere this bodhisattva.

With the eyes of compassion watching all beings,
With the heart of compassion radiating boundless love,
With countless merits and virtues,
Avalokiteśvara sees and relieves the world's pain[^13].

O bodhisattva of sincere vow,
Ocean-deep compassion, immeasurable in extent,
World after world, throughout all times,
You manifest as protector of all sentient beings.

True Regard, Pure Regard,
Vast Wisdom Regard,
Regard of Pity and Regard of Loving-Kindness—
Constantly desired, constantly looked up to[^14].

All who hear of Avalokiteśvara,
And keep that name ever in their heart,
Never falling back in their practice,
Will swiftly attain Buddhahood.

If one vows to support sixty-two billion bodhisattvas,
Offering them sustenance throughout their lives,
The merit would be immeasurable indeed,
But not to compare with one who hears

And venerates Avalokiteśvara's name,
Even for a single moment, with sincere heart,
The merit is exactly equal,
Enduring through all future eons.

## Philosophical Implications

Chapter 25 represents the Lotus Sutra's most accessible teaching. Where earlier chapters emphasized abstract doctrines (Buddha-nature universality, eternal transmission, cosmic verification), Chapter 25 offers immediate, practical compassion available through simple invocation.

The principle of Avalokiteśvara's responsiveness—"perceives the sound of suffering"—suggests that compassion is not earned through elaborate practice but is eternally available to those in distress. The bodhisattva does not require payment, ritual preparation, or spiritual qualification. One need only call. This democracy of access contradicts hierarchical religious systems requiring priestly mediation or prolonged study.

The enumeration of thirty-three manifestation-forms (Buddha, solitary-buddha, śrāvaka, Brahma-king, Śakra, various deities, kings, officials, merchants, Brahmins, monks, nuns, lay followers, various family members, diverse beings from dragons to demons, arhat, pratyeka-buddha, bodhisattva) represents the principle that compassion adapts to every condition. There is no being too lowly, no situation too hopeless for compassionate manifestation.

The paradox of manifestation deserves attention. Avalokiteśvara's true form remains metaphysically unclear. The chapter does not specify what Avalokiteśvara "really is" beneath the manifestations. This suggests that the bodhisattva's essence is precisely this capacity for unlimited adaptation. Compassion has no fixed form; it becomes whatever is needed.

The comparison of merit (sustaining sixty-two billion bodhisattvas versus invoking Avalokiteśvara once) inverts conventional merit-hierarchies. Enormous effort and elaborate practice produce less merit than a single moment of sincere invocation. This emphasizes that enlightenment-potential is immediately available, not something requiring lengthy cultivation.

The emphasis on "hearing the name" is significant. The name "Avalokiteśvara" is not merely verbal but carries power. To speak or hear this name is to activate compassion-presence. The name and the bodhisattva are not separable; calling the name calls forth the reality.

# Chapter 26: The Dharani of Protective Formulas

## The Protective Commitments
At that time, the Bodhisattva Medicine King rose from his seat, bowed respectfully, and addressed the Buddha: "World-Honored One, if virtuous men and women receive and maintain this Dharma-Blossom Sutra, whether they read it, recite it, understand it, or write it out, how much merit would they obtain?"

The Buddha replied to Medicine King: "If a virtuous man or woman were to make offerings to eight hundred million billion nayuta Ganges-river-sand-number of Buddhas, what do you think? Would they accumulate immeasurable merit?"

Medicine King responded: "Immeasurable indeed, World-Honored One."

The Buddha declared: "If a virtuous man or woman receives and maintains this sutra—even simply receiving one four-line verse, reading it aloud, understanding its meaning, and practicing according to it—the merit accumulated would be equally immeasurable[^1]."

Then Medicine King Bodhisattva addressed the Buddha: "World-Honored One, I now offer to all dharma-teachers the protective mantra-formula (dharani), so that those who recite it will be protected and guarded."

Then Medicine King spoke the protective mantra:

*Ān-ěr (安爾), Màn-ěr (曼爾), Mó-nì (摩禰), Mó-mó-nì (摩摩禰), Zhǐ-lì (旨隸), Zhē-lí-dì (遮梨第), Shē-miē (賒咩)[^ph1], Shē-lǚ-duō-wěi (賒履多瑋), Shān-dì (羶帝), Mù-dì (目帝), Mù-duō-lǚ (目多履), Suō-lǚ (娑履), Ā-wěi-suō-lǚ (阿瑋娑履), Sāng-lǚ (桑履), Suō-lǚ (娑履), Chā-yì (叉裔), Ā-chā-yì (阿叉裔), Ā-qí-nì (阿耆膩), Shān-dì (羶帝), Shē-lǚ (賒履), Tuó-luó-ní (陀羅尼), Ā-lú-jiā-pó-suō-bǒ-zhè-pí-chā-nì (阿盧伽婆娑簸蔗毗叉膩), Nǐ-pí-tì (禰毗剃), Ā-biàn-duō-luó-nǐ-lǚ-tì (阿便哆邏禰履剃), Ā-dàn-duō-bō-lì-shū-dì (阿亶哆波隸輸地), Ōu-jiū-lì (漚究隸), Móu-jiū-lì (牟究隸), Ā-luó-lì (阿羅隸), Bō-luó-lì (波羅隸), Shǒu-jiā-chà (首迦差), Ā-sān-mó-sān-lǚ (阿三磨三履), Fó-tuó-pí-jí-lì-zhì-dì (佛馱毗吉利袠帝), Dá-mó-bō-lì-chà-dì (達磨波利差帝), Sēng-qié-niè-qú-shā-nǐ (僧伽涅瞿沙禰), Pó-shě-pó-shě-shū-dì (婆舍婆舍輸地), Màn-duō-luó (曼哆邏), Màn-duō-luó-chā-yè-duō (曼哆邏叉夜多), Yóu-lóu-duō (郵樓哆), Yóu-lóu-duō-jiāo-shě-lüè (郵樓哆憍舍略), È-chā-luó (惡叉邏), È-chā-yě-duō-yě (惡叉冶多冶), Ā-pó-lú (阿婆盧), Ā-mó-ruò-nà-duō-yè (阿磨若那多夜)*

[^ph1]: **Phonetic Performance Notes**: The Taishō 262 critical apparatus provides interlinear *fanqie* (反切) pronunciation guides for ritual chanting. These instructions reflect 5th-century Chinese Buddhist vocalization of Sanskrit dhāraṇī:

| Syllable | *Fanqie* | Pronunciation |
|----------|----------|---------------|
| 賒咩 (*Shē-miē*) | **羊鳴音** | "sheep bleating sound" |
| 羶 (*Shān*) | **輸千反** | *Shū* initial + *Qiān* final |
| 亶 (*Dàn*) | **多罕反** | *Duō* initial + *Hǎn* final |
| 哆 (*Duō*) | **都餓反** | *Dū* initial + *È* final |
| 賒履 (*Shē-lǚ*) | **冈雉反** | *Gāng* initial + *Zhì* final |
| 娑 (*Suō*) | **蘇奈反** | *Sū* initial + *Nài* final |
| 地 (*Dì*) | **途賣反** | *Tú* initial + *Mài* final |
| 差 (*Chà*) in 首迦差 | **初几反** | *Chū* initial + *Jǐ* final |
| 差 (*Chà*) in 達磨波利差 | **猜離反** | *Cāi* initial + *Lí* final |
| 略 (*Lüè*) | **來加反** | *Lái* initial + *Jiā* final |
| 若 (*Ruò*) | **荏蔗反** | *Rěn* initial + *Zhè* final |

**Textual Variant**: For the syllable 梨 (*Lí*), the Taishō text reads 梨; the Dunhuang manuscripts (【敦乙】【敦丙】) read 犁.

Medicine King declared: "World-Honored One, this mantra-formula of protection has been spoken by sixty-two billion Ganges-river-sand-number of Buddhas. Any who harm this dharma-teacher through this protection would thereby harm all those Buddhas[^2]."

At that time, the Buddha praised Medicine King: "Excellent! Excellent, Medicine King! Through compassion for the dharma-teachers, you have spoken this protective formula. This brings immeasurable benefit to all sentient beings."

Then Courageous-Giver Bodhisattva rose from his seat and addressed the Buddha: "World-Honored One, I too wish to offer protection to those who receive, read, recite, understand, and practice this Dharma-Blossom Sutra, by proclaiming a protective formula. If any yakṣa, rākṣasa, hungry ghost, or other malevolent being attempts to harm such a dharma-teacher, this protection will ensure they cannot succeed."

Then Courageous-Giver spoke his mantra:

*Cuò-lì (痤隸)[^ph2], Mó-hē-cuò-lì (摩訶痤隸), Yù-zhī (鬱枳), Mù-zhī (目枳), Ā-lì (阿隸), Ā-luó-pó-dì (阿羅婆第), Niè-lì-dì (涅隸第), Niè-lì-duō-pó-dì (涅隸多婆第), Yī-zhì-nǐ (伊致柅), Wéi-zhì-nǐ (韋致柅), Zhǐ-zhì-nǐ (旨致柅), Niè-lì-chí-nǐ (涅隸墀柅), Niè-lì-chí-pó-dǐ (涅犁墀婆底)*

[^ph2]: **Phonetic Note**: The Taishō source provides the *fanqie* pronunciation **誓螺反** (*Shì-Luó fǎn*): combine *Shì* initial with *Luó* final.

Then the Heavenly King Vaiśravaṇa, guardian of the north direction, surrounded by a thousand billion celestial beings, approached the Buddha and declared: "World-Honored One, I too wish to protect those who maintain this sutra through proclaiming my protective formula."

Vaiśravaṇa spoke:

*Ā-lì (阿梨), Nà-lì (那梨), Nóu-nà-lì (㝹那梨), Ā-nà-lú (阿那盧), Nà-lǚ (那履), Jū-nà-fù (拘那覆)*

Vaiśravaṇa declared: "World-Honored One, through this protection, I shall myself guard the dharma-teachers within a hundred yojanas, ensuring they are free from all afflictions and disturbances[^3]."

Then the Heavenly King Dhṛtarāṣṭra, guardian of the east direction, surrounded by countless celestial attendants, approached the Buddha: "World-Honored One, I also wish to protect the dharma-teachers through proclaiming my protective formula."

Dhṛtarāṣṭra spoke:

*Ā-qié-nǐ (阿伽禰), Qié-nǐ (伽禰), Qú-lì (瞿利), Qián-tuó-lì (乾陀利), Zhān-tuó-lì (旃陀利), Mó-dèng-qí (摩蹬耆), Cháng-qiú-lì (常求利), Fú-lóu-shā-nǐ (浮樓莎柅), È-dǐ (頞底)*

Dhṛtarāṣṭra declared: "World-Honored One, this protection, spoken by forty-two billion Buddhas, ensures that if one seeks to harm the dharma-teacher, one thereby harms all those Buddhas[^4]."

Then the ten Rakṣasī (female protective demons) approached the Buddha, together with the Yakṣa Mother and her children and retinue. The ten Rakṣasīs were named: (1) Lambā, (2) Vilambā, (3) Crooked-Teeth, (4) Flower-Teeth, (5) Black-Teeth, (6) Many-Haired, (7) Insatiable, (8) Holding-Necklaces, (9) Kuntī, and (10) Stealer-of-Vital-Spirit.

[^fn_rakshasi]: **Ten Rākṣasī Daughters (十羅剎女):** The names follow Kumārajīva's specific mix of transliteration and translation: (1) Lambā (藍婆), (2) Vilambā (毘藍婆), (3) Crooked-Teeth (曲齒), (4) Flower-Teeth (華齒), (5) Black-Teeth (黑齒, Skt. Makuṭadantī), (6) Many-Haired (多髮), (7) Insatiable (無厭足, Skt. Acalā—distinct from "Immovable"), (8) Holding-Necklaces (持瓔珞), (9) Kuntī (睪帝), and (10) Stealer-of-Vital-Spirit (奪一切眾生精氣).

These ten Rakṣasīs, together with the Yakṣa Mother, her children, and retinue, approached the Buddha and declared: "World-Honored One, we too wish to protect those who read, recite, receive, and maintain this Dharma-Blossom Sutra, relieving them of afflictions. If any seeks to harm the dharma-teacher, we shall ensure they cannot succeed."

Then the ten Rakṣasīs spoke their protection:

*Yī-tí-lǚ (伊提履), Yī-tí-mǐn (伊提泯), Yī-tí-lǚ (伊提履), Ā-tí-lǚ (阿提履), Yī-tí-lǚ (伊提履), Ní-lǚ (泥履), Ní-lǚ (泥履), Ní-lǚ (泥履), Ní-lǚ (泥履), Ní-lǚ (泥履), Lóu-xǐ (樓醯), Lóu-xǐ (樓醯), Lóu-xǐ (樓醯), Lóu-xǐ (樓醯), Duō-xǐ (多醯), Duō-xǐ (多醯), Duō-xǐ (多醯), Dōu-xǐ (兜醯), Nóu-xǐ (㝟醯)*

The Rakṣasīs then declared: "Those who fail to obey our protection and harm the dharma-teacher: may their heads split into seven pieces like the branches of the Arjuna tree; may they experience the karma of those who kill their parents; may they experience the suffering of those who crush oil; may they experience the karma of those who deceive with false weights; may they experience the karma of Devadatta who split the sangha. This is the retribution for harming the dharma-teacher[^5]."

At that time, the Buddha addressed the Rakṣasīs: "Excellent, excellent! If you simply protect those who maintain the sutra's name, the merit is immeasurable. How much greater is the merit when you protect those who fully receive and maintain the complete sutra, offering flowers, fragrances, garlands, powdered incenses, anointing oils, burning incenses, banners, jeweled coverings, silk tapestries, various kinds of musical instruments, and oil-lamps of every description[^6]!"
## The Assembled Protections
*At that time, the Buddha wished to restate this meaning through verse:*

When the dharma-teachers maintain this sutra,
All the bodhisattvas offer their protection,
Medicine King proclaims his mantra,
Courageous-Giver adds his power.

The four Heavenly Kings—
Guardians of the four directions,
Vaiśravaṇa of the north,
Dhṛtarāṣṭra of the east,
And their companions—
All pledge their protection.

The ten Rakṣasīs, female protective demons,
Together with the Yakṣa Mother and her retinue,
Vow to guard all dharma-teachers,
Ensuring no harm can befall them.

Whoever harms these dharma-teachers
Will incur terrible retribution:
Their head will split into seven pieces,
They will experience the karma of parent-killers,
The suffering of oil-pressing,
The deception of false weights,
The breaking of the sangha's unity.

Thus protected by bodhisattvas and celestial beings,
The dharma-teachers dwell in safety,
Proclaiming the Dharma-Blossom Sutra
Throughout the world, without fear[^7].

## Philosophical Implications

Chapter 26 represents the sutra's integration of protective practice with doctrinal teaching. The mantras themselves—rendered in transliterated form that resists literal translation—possess power not through semantic meaning but through sonic resonance. This suggests a Buddhist understanding that language operates on multiple levels: semantic (conveying meaning), magical (activating power), and spiritual (creating consciousness-states).

The enumeration of protectors is significant. Rather than presenting a single ultimate guardian, Chapter 26 shows an entire assembly of beings committed to protection: bodhisattvas (Medicine King, Courageous-Giver), heavenly kings (the four directional guardians), female demons (the ten Rakṣasīs), the Yakṣa Mother. This suggests that protection operates through multiple channels and that cosmic beings of all types participate in dharma-defense.

The principle that harming a dharma-teacher equates to harming all Buddhas establishes the dharma-teacher as sacred. To injure the teacher is not merely a personal wrong but a cosmic crime against the entire Buddha-family. This consecrates the dharma-teacher's status.

The threats enumerated—yakṣas, demons, hungry ghosts, malevolent beings—reflect popular Buddhist cosmology where evil forces threaten practitioners. Yet the sutra's response is not to condemn these beings as permanently evil but to recruit them as protectors. The Rakṣasīs (female demons) and Yakṣa Mother represent transformation of potentially hostile powers into protective allies. This reflects a sophisticated Buddhist understanding that even demonic forces can be converted to dharma-service through proper cultivation.

The mantras' lack of literal meaning directs attention to their sonic-magical dimension. In tantric Buddhism, mantras are understood as embodying the actual presence of Buddhas and bodhisattvas. To recite the mantra is not merely to speak words but to invoke and manifest those beings. The mantra is not a request for protection but an actualization of protective presence.

# Chapter 27: The Wonderful-Adornment King's Original Practice

## The Transformation of a Skeptical Ruler
At that time, the Buddha addressed the assembled great audience: "In ages long past—spanning incalculable eons beyond measurement—there existed a Buddha named Cloud-Thunder-Sound-Constellation-King-Flower-Wisdom, the Tathāgata, the Arhat, the Perfectly Awakened One, the One Perfectly Accomplished in Knowledge and Conduct, the Sugata, the Knower of the World, the Unsurpassable Guide, the Tamer of the Untamed, the Teacher of Gods and Humans, the Buddha, the World-Honored One. His realm was named Radiance-Flourishing, and the age was called Joyful-Perception[^1].

"In that realm, there was a king named Wonderful-Adornment. His queen was named Pure-Virtue. The king had two sons: one was named Pure-Treasury, the other Pure-Vision. Both sons possessed great supernatural powers, deep karmic-roots, long-cultivated merit, and profound wisdom. They had perfected the six perfections (generosity, discipline, patience, effort, meditation, wisdom), bodhisattva-methods of skillful means, and compassion-love. They had also mastered countless samādhis and absorbed the thirty-seven aids-to-enlightenment[^2].

"At that time, Buddha Cloud-Thunder-Sound-Constellation-King-Flower-Wisdom wished to transform the Wonderful-Adornment King and to liberate all beings in his realm, so he expounded the Dharma-Blossom Sutra. The two princes approached their mother and said: 'Dear Mother, we wish to go to the Buddha Cloud-Thunder-Sound-Constellation-King-Flower-Wisdom to pay reverence, draw near, make offerings, and receive the teachings. We earnestly desire to hear the Dharma-Blossom Sutra[^3].'

"Their mother replied: 'Your father, the king, is deeply attached to the teachings of external religions and cannot easily accept the dharma. You must first convince your father to go with us.'

"The two princes responded respectfully: 'Mother, we understand that our father has incorrect views. We shall show him miracles so that his heart becomes pure and clear. Then he will listen to us and agree to go to the Buddha.'

"Thereupon, the two pure sons, desiring to transform their father, soared into the void. They rose seven palm-trees high and demonstrated miraculous powers. Standing in the air, they walked, stood, sat, and reclined. From their upper bodies, they manifested fire; from their lower bodies, they manifested water. From their lower bodies, they manifested fire; from their upper bodies, they manifested water. They caused their bodies to appear large, filling the sky, then small again. They appeared and disappeared in the void, demonstrating miraculous transformations that enabled the king's heart to become pure and faithful[^4].

"When the king witnessed such supernatural powers, he experienced great joy and, speaking to his sons, said: 'Who is your teacher? To whom do you offer reverence?'

"The two sons replied: 'Great King, the Buddha Cloud-Thunder-Sound-Constellation-King-Flower-Wisdom dwells beneath the seven-jeweled Bodhi tree, seated on a dharma-throne, teaching the Dharma-Blossom Sutra to all the gods and humans. We are his disciples[^5].'

"The king then addressed his sons: 'I too wish to see your teacher. Shall we go together?'

"At that moment, the two sons descended from the void and approached their mother, saying: 'Dear Mother, Father's mind is now pure and ready for enlightenment. We have accomplished our bodhisattva-work for him. We now request permission to leave the household and renounce worldly life to practice under that Buddha'[^6].

"The two sons then spoke this verse to their mother:

*'We ask your blessing, beloved mother,*
*To leave this world and become monks,*
*For Buddhas are so rarely encountered,*
*Like the lotus flower that blooms once in eons.*

*To find one's way to a Buddha,*
*Is harder than finding a one-eyed turtle,*
*Floating in a vast ocean,*
*Encountering a wooden yoke with a single hole.*

*Our karmic roots are deep and mature,*
*We have been born in this Buddha's age,*
*This is why, dear parents,*
*We ask permission to renounce[^7].'*

"The mother replied: 'Go forth, my sons. The Buddha is so rarely encountered that your desire to leave the household is indeed justified.'

"Thereupon, the two sons addressed their parents: 'Dear Father and Mother, we earnestly invite you to go to the Buddha's presence with us, to make offerings and receive teachings. The Buddha is so rare to encounter—like the lotus that blooms once in countless eons. Meeting a Buddha is rarer still, like a one-eyed turtle encountering a wooden yoke with a single hole floating in the vast ocean. Our karmic roots are deep, and we have been born in the Buddha's age. Therefore, you must permit us to leave the household and practice[^8].'

"At that time, the Wonderful-Adornment King, together with his officials and retinue, the Pure-Virtue Queen with all her attendants, and the two sons with their four thousand two hundred followers, all journeyed together to the Buddha's presence. Upon arrival, they bowed with their heads to the Buddha's feet, circumambulated him three times, and stood reverently to the side.

"The Buddha then expounded the dharma to the Wonderful-Adornment King, revealing its significance and teaching its benefits. The king received great joy from this teaching. At that moment, the King and Queen removed from their necks pearl and jeweled ornaments worth hundreds of thousands and scattered them before the Buddha as offerings. In the void, these scattered jewels were transformed into four jeweled platforms, each bearing a jeweled throne as wide as a hand's span. Upon each throne sat a Buddha, shining with radiant light[^9].

"The Wonderful-Adornment King then perceived the miraculous transformation and reflected: 'The Buddha's body is rare and extraordinary, possessing supreme beauty and perfection, adorned with the marks of a supreme being[^10].'

"At that time, Buddha Cloud-Thunder-Sound-Constellation-King-Flower-Wisdom addressed the assembly: 'Do you see the Wonderful-Adornment King standing here in reverence? This king will become a monk and diligently cultivate the dharma, assisting the Buddha's way. This king will become a Buddha named Sal-Tree-King (娑羅樹王). His realm will be named Great-Light, and the age will be called Great-Exalted-Kings. The Buddha Sal-Tree-King will have innumerable bodhisattvas and incalculable śrāvakas. His realm will be perfectly even, adorned with extraordinary merits[^11].'

"Immediately upon hearing this prophecy, the Wonderful-Adornment King, relinquishing his kingdom to his younger brother, together with his queen, two sons, and all retinue, entered the monastic order.

"The king diligently practiced for eighty-four thousand years, eventually achieving the samādhi of Complete Purification and Merit-Adornment. Rising into the void to a height of seven palm-trees, he addressed the Buddha: 'World-Honored One, these two sons of mine have already accomplished bodhisattva-work for me through their miraculous powers and transformations. They converted my incorrect views, enabling me to dwell purely in the Buddha-dharma and to see you, the World-Honored One. These two sons are my virtuous teachers. They were born in my family to awaken my original karmic-roots from past eons, and to benefit me greatly, showing me the path to awakening[^12].

'All who wish to attain enlightenment should know: virtuous teachers (kalyāṇa-mitras) are the great cause and circumstance for transformation. Through virtuous teachers' guidance, liberation is accomplished. Virtuous teachers teach us the dharma, show us benefits, bring us joy, and establish us in unsurpassed enlightenment[^13]. Great King, you have seen these two sons. They have served as transformative virtuous teachers to you, converting you and all your retinue toward enlightenment. They cultivated this dharma-teaching in past Buddha-realms[^14].'

"The king then descended from the void, bowed respectfully, and addressed the Buddha: 'World-Honored One, the Tathāgata is exceedingly rare! The Tathāgata's dharma is complete and unsurpassable, perfected through wisdom and virtue. Your body radiates with divine marks of perfection. Your eyes are vast and beautiful, azure-blue in color. Your eyebrow-marks gleam white as the moon. Your teeth are bright and perfectly aligned, always emitting light. Your lips are beautifully colored, resembling ripe pomegranate fruit.'

"Having offered such praise, the Wonderful-Adornment King addressed the Buddha once more: 'World-Honored One, the dharma is most extraordinary! I have never encountered teachings so wondrous and complete. From this day forward, I shall no longer follow my heart's incorrect inclinations, nor shall I harbor arrogance, anger, or malice. I shall purely dwell in the Buddha-dharma, forever forsaking all false views[^15].'

"With these words, the king bowed reverentially and departed."

## Narrative Conclusion

"The Buddha then addressed the assembly: 'Do you comprehend this account? The Wonderful-Adornment King of that ancient time was none other than the Bodhisattva Dharma-Excellence who sits before you now. That Pure-Virtue Queen was the Bodhisattva Light-Illumination-Excellence-Adornment, who was reborn in that realm through compassion for the Wonderful-Adornment King and his retinue. Those two sons, Pure-Treasury and Pure-Vision, are the bodhisattvas Medicine King and Medicine-Excellence. These two great bodhisattvas, through their accumulated spiritual practice and extraordinary virtues, have perfected such profound capacities. They have already made offerings to innumerable Buddhas, cultivated roots of virtue in countless realms, and accomplished inconceivable virtuous deeds. If any being simply knows these two bodhisattvas' names, the entire celestial and human assembly should offer them reverence[^16].'

"The Buddha concluded: 'Understand this: the Dharma-Blossom Sutra provides inconceivable benefit to all bodhisattva-practitioners. It swiftly brings them to unsurpassed perfect enlightenment. Therefore, all bodhisattva-practitioners should, after the Tathāgata's passing, constantly receive, maintain, read, recite, explain, and write out this sutra[^17].'

"When the Buddha expounded this Wonderful-Adornment King chapter, eighty-four thousand beings immediately abandoned dusty defilements and attained the pure dharma-eye. Transcending the realm of discrimination, they obtained pure dharma-vision regarding all phenomena."

# Chapter 28: The Encouragement of the Universally-Worthy Bodhisattva

## The Final Exhortation
At that time, the Bodhisattva Samantabhadra (the Universally-Worthy Bodhisattva) approached the Buddha with his innumerable, boundless, incalculable bodhisattva-retinue from the east, manifesting his transcendent power and magnificence, renowned throughout the ten directions. Wherever he passed, the ground trembled with six kinds of motion, precious lotus flowers rained down, and hundreds of millions of kinds of celestial music played spontaneously.

Samantabhadra arrived at Vulture Peak Mountain, bowed with his head to the feet of Śākyamuni Buddha, circumambulated him seven times, and addressed him: "World-Honored One, in my realm called Precious-Glory, I heard, from far away, that this Sahā world-realm teaches the Dharma-Blossom Sutra. Together with innumerable bodhisattvas, I have journeyed here to listen. I earnestly request that you teach this dharma. If there are virtuous men or women who will receive, maintain, read, recite, remember, learn, and practice this Dharma-Blossom Sutra after the Tathāgata's passage, how will they accomplish this? How will they protect themselves[^1]?"

The Buddha replied to Samantabhadra: "If virtuous men and women are to receive this dharma after the Tathāgata's passing, they must accomplish four conditions. First, they must be held in mindfulness by all the Buddhas. Second, they must plant the roots of virtue. Third, they must enter the cluster of correct determination. Fourth, they must awaken the mind to rescue all sentient beings. Those virtuous men and women who accomplish these four conditions will definitely obtain this Dharma-Blossom Sutra after the Tathāgata's passage[^fn_four_conditions].

[^fn_four_conditions]: **The Four Conditions (四法):** The precise Kumārajīva terminology for these prerequisites is: (1) To be held in mindfulness by the Buddhas (*wei zhu fo hu nian* 為諸佛護念); (2) To plant the roots of virtue (*zhi zhong de ben* 殖眾德本—using the specific character *zhí* 殖); (3) To enter the cluster of correct determination (*ru zheng ding ju* 入正定聚); and (4) To awaken the mind to rescue all sentient beings (*fa jiu yi qie zhong sheng zhi xin* 發救一切眾生之心).
## Samantabhadra's Vow
"Samantabhadra, in the degenerate age five hundred years after the Tathāgata's passage, among those who maintain this sutra, I shall guard and protect them, relieving them of all afflictions.
