I will ensure that no spirits, demons, demon-children, demon-women, demon-followers, demon-possessed individuals, yakṣas, rākṣasas, kumbhāṇḍas, piśācas, yakṣa-spirits, rich-demons, vetālas, and other harmful beings find any opportunity to molest them. Whether the person walks, stands, reads, recites, or contemplates this sutra, I shall ride my six-tusked white elephant, together with my great bodhisattva-assembly, travel to their location, appear before them, and supply them with all forms of comfort and safety, additionally supporting their dharma-practice[^3].

"When one sits in contemplation of this sutra, and one forgets or loses even a single phrase or verse, I shall appear on the white elephant, ride down, and personally teach you, helping you restore what was forgotten and recover full fluency[^4].

"When practitioners of the Dharma-Blossom Sutra practice intensely for three seven-day cycles—meaning twenty-one days of single-minded dedication—they should perceive my form. I shall then ride my white elephant, together with countless bodhisattvas, surround them, manifest myself in whatever form the practitioner needs to see, teach the dharma, supply whatever support is required, and grant protective formulas[^5].

"In the degenerate age of five hundred years, if monks, nuns, male lay followers, or female lay followers desire to maintain this sutra and practice its dharma through continuous effort, I shall personally protect them with the power of all the other bodhisattvas. Not a single non-human being will be able to cause harm, nor will any woman suffer confusion or seduction through unwanted attractions. I shall provide a protective mantra-formula:

*Ā-tán-dì (阿檀地)[^ph3], Tán-tuó-pó-dì (檀陀婆地), Tán-tuó-pó-dì (檀陀婆地), Tán-tuó-jiū-shě-lì (檀陀鳩舍隷), Tán-tuó-xī-lì (檀陀渫梨), Tán-tuó-bō-tuó-ní (檀陀波陀尼), Xiū-tán-tuó (修檀陀), Xiū-duō-lóu-tán-tuó (修多樓檀陀), Sā-pó-hē (薩婆訶)*

[^ph3]: **Phonetic Note**: The Taishō source provides the *fanqie* pronunciation **途賣反** (*Tú-Mài fǎn*) for the character 地 (*Dì*): combine *Tú* initial with *Mài* final.

"The benefits of this dharani are such that whoever hears it shall escape demon-influence, avoid seduction by unwanted attractions, and be protected with unbreakable security[^6].

"World-Honored One, in ages past when there were Buddhas, I practiced this dharma in their presence. When this era's Buddha has passed and the final five hundred years of degeneration arrive, if there are earnest practitioners who practice this sutra, I shall manifest my presence before them on a white elephant, maintain and protect them throughout all time, ensuring their practice proceeds without interruption[^7]."
## The Fruit of Practice
The Buddha then addressed Samantabhadra: "Excellent! Excellent! You possess such incomparable miraculous power and compassionate vow that all practitioners of this sutra will attain liberation. Your virtue is profound, your compassion vast, and your original intention of enlightenment is deep and ancient. You accomplish these protective vows for the benefit of countless beings[^8]."

"Such practitioners need not construct stupas or establish monastic dwellings and support the sangha. Why? Because such persons are already constructing the greatest stupas, establishing the greatest monastic dwellings, supporting the greatest sangha. Those who write this sutra achieve such merits as this[^10].

"If such a person writes out this sutra, after their lifetime is complete, they shall be born in the Trayastriṃśa Heaven (the Heaven of the Thirty-Three), surrounded by eighty-four thousand divine maidens, immediately adorned with a crown of seven treasures, experiencing every pleasure among the heavenly consorts.[^11] But how much greater are the merits of those who receive and maintain, read and recite, understand and practice this sutra!

"If there are people who receive, read, recite, understand and practice this sutra, in their next lifetime they shall be reborn in the Tuṣita heaven before Maitreya Bodhisattva, who will grasp their hand with compassion. When Maitreya Bodhisattva becomes the Buddha and presides in the Three Dragon Flower Assemblies (龍華三會), such practitioners shall be among the assembly and shall achieve unsurpassed perfect enlightenment[^12].

"Samantabhadra, if those who receive, maintain, and practice this sutra encounter those who ridicule them and say, 'You are a fool! You will gain nothing by this practice!'—such practitioners should cultivate these thoughts: 'The Buddha has explained this sutra as the foremost among all teachings. Those who practice it are assured of enlightenment. Even if people criticize me, I will continue without doubt.' Through such resolve, the practitioner accomplishes the practice of the Bodhisattva Way[^13].

"Samantabhadra, know this: if one sees a practitioner of this sutra, one should rise up to greet them just as one would greet the Buddha himself. If one places flowers, fragrances, garlands, musical instruments, silk banners, burning incenses, oil-lamps, and all other precious offerings before such practitioners, considering them equivalent to the Buddha, one will acquire immeasurable merits[^14].

"Samantabhadra, in the ages after the Tathāgata's passing, if one encounters a practitioner of this sutra and hears them speak even a single verse of this dharma, one should understand: this person has not long before entering the bodhi-seat, defeating all demonic forces, turning the dharma-wheel, striking the dharma-drum, blowing the dharma-conch, raining the dharma-rain, seated upon a lion-throne in the midst of the celestial and human assembly[^15]."
## The Final Benediction
"Samantabhadra, if one encounters someone lightly reviling a practitioner, commenting on their faults (whether true or false), this person shall in the present lifetime develop pale-white leprosy. If one encounters such a practitioner and fails to honor them, or criticizes them, or shows contempt, one shall experience these consequences: eyelessness, blindness, deafness, severe stammering, cleft lip, a malformed face, a shortened form, offensive odor, tumorous growths, putrid sores, water-swollen belly, shortness of breath, and numerous serious illnesses[^16].

"Therefore, Samantabhadra, you should recognize that all those who receive, read, recite, understand, and practice this Dharma-Blossom Sutra are themselves performing the practices of the Universally-Worthy Bodhisattva. Such practitioners will not cling to material pleasures, will not seek external doctrines, will not cultivate frivolous associations, will not pursue false attachments, will not be tormented by greed, anger, or delusion, nor by jealousy, pride, arrogance, or superiority. Such practitioners will develop few desires, knowing contentment, able to practice the Universally-Worthy Way[^17]."

The Universally-Worthy Bodhisattva,
Pure-hearted and compassionate,
Has arrived from his distant realm,
Leading countless bodhisattvas in his retinue.

To protect those who maintain this sutra,
He rides upon a white elephant with six tusks,
With his assembly of great bodhisattvas,
Traveling to support the practitioners.

When a sutra-practitioner walks or stands,
When they read, recite, or contemplate,
Samantabhadra appears before them,
Offering comfort and protection always[^19].

If one writes this supreme dharma-teaching,
After completing their lifetime,
They shall be reborn in Trayastriṃśa heaven,
Adorned with a seven-jeweled crown,
Surrounded by celestial maidens dancing,
Experiencing all heavenly delights.

When Maitreya descends and becomes Buddha,
And gathers the three assemblies,
Such practitioners shall be present,
Achieving supreme enlightenment together[^20].

Those who maintain and practice this sutra,
Should be honored as buddhas themselves,
Receiving offerings of flowers and incense,
Revered in the midst of all assemblies.

Those who criticize such practitioners,
Shall suffer terrible consequences:
Paleness, blindness, deafness,
Severe deformity and disease[^21].

But those who honor the practitioners,
And make offerings and reverential bows,
Shall attain boundless merits,
Dwelling in the eternal dharma-way.

Samantabhadra's protective vow,
Extends across all future ages,
Ensuring that none can harm,
Those devoted to this supreme teaching[^22].

All those who practice with sincere heart,
Will gradually progress toward enlightenment,
Will not long delay before becoming Buddhas,
Achieving the wisdom of all-knowing Buddha-nature.

The Dharma-Blossom Sutra is supreme,
The sovereign of all teachings,
Those who practice it shall attain,
The highest wisdom, the Buddha's enlightenment[^23].

*[End of Fascicle 7 (卷七)]*

---

# Postscript to the Lotus Sutra
## 妙法蓮華經後序

*Composed by the Śramaṇa Sengrui of Later Qin*
*(後秦沙門僧叡述)*

---

The *Lotus Sutra* is the secret treasury of all the Buddhas, the true substance of all the sutras. It takes "flower" as its name to illumine its origin; it is called *Puṇḍarīka* to extol its flourishing. Its arising is profoundly mysterious, its meaning extremely elegant. Unless one of penetrating insight transmits it, rarely does anyone find their way to its gate.

The blossoms of a hundred plants and herbs are the origin of their fruits and seeds; the eighty-four thousand treasury of dharmas is the source of the fruit of the Way—hence the metaphor. Among all flowers, the lotus is supreme. When not yet open, it is called *kumuda*; when open yet about to fall, *kamala*; in its prime at mid-stage, *puṇḍarīka*. The unopened flower symbolizes the Two Vehicles; the falling flower signifies nirvāṇa; but its radiant glory alone suffices to symbolize this scripture.

As for the *Prajñā* sutras, their depth is without limit, hence those of the Way take refuge in them; their vastness leaves nothing uncovered, hence those of the Vehicle cross over by means of them. Yet in broad outline, all take adaptive transformation as their greatness. In the gate of responding to affairs, they cannot but employ skillful expedients. Expedient transformation, though vast in awakening beings, is insufficient regarding the true substance—all such [teachings] belong to the *Lotus Sutra*, as is fitting.

Tracing its profound meaning—expansive, vast, and deep—what it encompasses is far-reaching. How could it be merely speaking the real and returning to the root, or definitively distinguishing different paths? Rather, it truly illumines the great principle of awakening and encompasses past and present.

It says the Buddha's lifespan is immeasurable—even eternal kalpas are insufficient to clarify its duration. It says the emanation-bodies are countless—even myriad forms are insufficient to differentiate its substance. Thus, the "Lifespan" chapter establishes that it is beyond number; the "Emanation Bodies" reveal that it is without substantiality; Samantabhadra displays that it is without becoming; Prabhūtaratna illumines that it is without extinction.

To transcend the mysterious ancient to reach the present, ten thousand generations become a single day; to awaken to the mysterious through ten thousand transformations, a thousand paths have no divergent tracks. Being thus, birth after birth is insufficient to anticipate existence, and eternal stillness likewise cannot be said to be extinction. Tracing the profound lineage to cut off the past, one loses accomplishment in original non-being; controlling the reins of the mind in samādhi, one forgets expectation in the two stages.

Though this sutra has flowed to this land for nearly a hundred years, translators have been unclear about its empty crossing-place, and the spiritual gate has never been opened. Commentators have deviated from its standard, and few have been able to follow its hidden traces. Despite searching and researching until white-haired, none had glimpsed its gate.

Yao Song, Prefect of the Capital Region, General of the Left, and Marquis of Ancheng of the Qin [dynasty], attuned himself to the profound gate, dwelling his mind beyond the world. He devoted his sincerity to this scripture with ever-increasing faith. Each time he sought to trace its text, he deeply recognized the translators' errors. Upon encountering the Dharma Master Kumārajīva, [Yao Song] had him transmit and transcribe it. [Kumārajīva] pointed to its great principle of truth—it was as if parting the layered clouds to tread on high, ascending Kunlun to look down below.

At that time, the monks who listened, received, and comprehended numbered over eight hundred—all were outstanding talents from various regions, the finest of their generation.

*This was the eighth year of the Hongshi era [406 CE], the year of the Lesser Fire Star.*

---

# Tang Dynasty Manuscript Colophon (Bo Edition)
## 博本記

> **Note**: The "Bo Edition" (博本) preserves a colophon recording that this manuscript was "copied on the first day of the sixth month of the third year of the Changshou era [694 CE] by Li Yuanhui (李元會) of Chang'an County **at Yangzhou**" (長壽三年六月一日抄訖...於楊州...長安縣李元會書). This provides physical evidence of the text's circulation during the reign of Empress Wu Zetian.

---

# Song Dynasty Donor Dedication
## 魯國太夫人張氏題記

*(紹興二十一年正月十五日 — January 15, 1151 CE)*

---

Lady Zhang, Grand Lady of the State of Lu, on the occasion of the anniversary of her deceased husband's passing—the Grand Tutor and Grand Chancellor, Lord Li—respectfully contributed pure funds to the Tripitaka Repository of Fuzhou Kaiyuan Temple. [The funds] were used to carve the *Lotus Sutra of the Wonderful Dharma* in seven fascicles, the *Lotus Samādhi* and other sutras in three fascicles, totaling ten fascicles altogether. May this superior karmic cause make solemn offerings and enable [Lord Li] to transcend rebirth in the Pure Land.

*Respectfully inscribed on the fifteenth day of the first month of the twenty-first year of the Shaoxing era [1151 CE]*

---
